Locke's Critique of Innate Ideas
Locke's arguments against innate ideas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Locke's two arguments against innate ideas as presented in the passage, and identify how they challenge the rationalist position.

Core Idea
Locke argues that no ideas are innate because they are neither universal nor known from birth.

The passage presents John Locke's famous attack on the doctrine of innate ideas, a cornerstone of rationalism. Locke offers two main arguments: first, that supposed innate ideas are not universal (since there are people who lack them), and second, that they are not present in children or the simple-minded from the beginning of awareness. This critique has implications for Islamic theology, especially the concept of fitrah, which often refers to an innate disposition toward tawhid. Understanding Locke's arguments helps us appreciate the rationalist-empiricist debate and its Islamic parallels.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rationalist claim being attacked
The rationalists claim there are innate ideas (al-afkar al-fitriyya) or first principles of the mind, such as the principle of non-contradiction, that are present in all people from birth.
2
Find Locke's first argument
Locke says if these ideas were truly universal, then all people would accept them. But there exist savage tribes who do not know them. Thus they are not universal.
This is an empirical counterexample.
3
Find Locke's second argument
If these ideas were perceived immediately upon mental awareness, then children would know them from infancy. But children are ignorant even of the principle of non-contradiction. Therefore, ideas are acquired through experience.
Locke uses the example of the impossibility of contradiction.
4
Apply to Islamic concept of fitrah
In Islam, fitrah refers to an innate disposition to recognize tawhid, but it does not necessarily mean fully formed ideas. Compare Locke's critique: can the concept of fitrah withstand the objection that children do not explicitly know tawhid?
This is a point of discussion among scholars.

أهمية الحواس

تحتل الحواس - بوصفها مصدراً للمعرفة وطريقة لها - أهمية لا يقلل من قدرها باحث منصف. فالحس أحد منافذ المعرفة إلى نفس الإنسان، ويكاد المرء العادي لا يعترف بسواها وسيلة لمعرفته إذ إن معارفه كلها مبنية على ما رآه وسمعه ولمسه بنفسه.
ومعظم حقائقه (Truths) عن الدنيا الموضوعية والدنيا الخارجية المحيطة به إنما هي مدركات حسية (۱).
ولا شك أن المعرفة الحسية تكون يقينية عندما يُقدم الحس شهادته مؤكدة قاطعة بعد عمليات الإدراك الحسي المتواترة، والمتفقة مع شهادات الحواس الأخرى، وشهادات الآخرين من غير أن تتعارض مع أصل من أصول العقل وقوانينه (۲)، مع أن بعض الباحثين لا يسلّم حتى بقانون العلية أو قوانين العقل الأولية تلك، إذ إن العلاقة بين العلة والمعلول لا تقوم -حسب هذه الوجهة- على مبدأ عدم التناقض الصوري، الذي يذهب إليه العقليـون بوصفه قانوناً حتمياً من قوانين العقل الأولية، وإنما على أساس التجربة (۳).
ومن قبل تزعم (جون لوك) لواء هذه المقولة في كتابه (مقالة في العقل البشري فذهب إلى إنكار وجود أفكار أولية موروثة، أو مايسمى ببدائــه العقول، كما يقول أصحاب المذهب العقلي.
ويرد (لوك) على ما يُقدّم من أدلة تؤكد صحة دعوتهم بما يلي: أولاً : إن القول بأن هذه الأفكار مسلم بها مـن جميـع النـاس بـلا استثناء
محجوج بوجود قبائل متوحشة لا تعرفها.
ثانياً : إن القول بأن العقل البشري يدرك هذه الأفكار بمجرد وعيه ويقظته محجوج بأن العقل لا يستطيع إدراك تلك الآراء بمجرد يقظته في السنين الأولى من العمر، بدليل أن الأطفال تجهلها تماماً. فالقول مثلاً باستحالة اجتماع النقيضين في وقت واحد أمر يجهله الأطفال والمتوحشون والبلهاء على الرغم من بداهته. وبذلك فلا يمكن القول بفطرية مثل هذه الآراء، بل هي مكتسبة بتجربة طويلة (١).
وعلى الرغم من حدّة الخلاف بين الحسيين والعقليين إلا أن ذلك لا يعني إنكار العقليين المطلق لأهمية الحس أو العكس، وإنمـا مـدار الخلاف كامن في أيهما الأصل، وأيهما الفرع له (٢).
ولتن حدث ما يخالف هذا فهو خروج على الاتجاه العام لدى هذا الطرف أو
ذاك، وتطرف مذموم لا يحمل تبعاته جمهور الحسيين أو العقليين (۳).
وبالنسبة إلى موقف القرآن الكريم من التجربة أو الحس فإن التجربة تمثل - في نظر بعض الدارسين لآياته - المعرفة بعواقب الأشياء، وهذه الطريقة في
(۱) عدنان زرزور مقالة في المعرفة، ۲۹ - ۳۰.
(۲) راجع في موقف الحسيين راجح الكردي، مرجع سابق، ٥٤٠ ٥٨١ والزنيدي، مرجع سابق، ٥٢٦ - ٥٢٨. وفي موقف العقليين الكردي، المرجع السابق، ٥٨٣ - ٥٨٤، والزنيدي، المرجع السابق، ٥٢٦ - ٥٢٨، ومحمد جواد رضا فلسفة التربية، ٣٣٣ - ٣٣٤ . (۳) أشير هنا إلى فرقة السُّمَنيَّة وهم (عبدة الأصنام والقائلون بالتناسخ، وقيل لهم السمنية نسبة إلى سومنات الهند انظر : نظرية المعرفة في القرآن لآية الله جواد ،آمليه الهامش (۱)). وتزعم هذه الفرقة أنه لا سبيل إلى معرفة شيء إلا عن طريق الحواس الخمس، وأبطلوا العلوم النظرية، وزعموا أن المذاهب كلّها باطلة. ويلزمهم على هذا القول إبطال مذهبهم، لأن القول بإبطال المذهب مذهب. (انظر: الإنسان والعقل لنايف معروف ۱۲ - ۱۳). وبالمقابل فإن الترانستتدالية تغالي في أهمية العقل إلى الحد الذي تجعله مصدراً أوحد للمعرفة، لأن العلوم كلها كامنة فيه، وعالم الحس يعمل على تشويش معارف العقل. (انظر: المرجع السابق للزنيدي، (٥٢٧ - ٥٢٨)
Chapter Three: Section One - Sensation
Importance of the Senses

The senses - as a source and method of knowledge - occupy an importance that no fair researcher diminishes. For sensation is one of the entrances of knowledge into the human soul, and the ordinary person almost does not recognize any other means for his knowledge, since all his knowledge is built on what he saw, heard, and touched himself. Most of his truths about the objective world and the external world surrounding him are sensory perceptions (1). There is no doubt that sensory knowledge becomes certain when the sense presents its testimony in a decisive and conclusive manner after repeated sensory perception processes, in agreement with the testimonies of other senses and the testimonies of others, without conflicting with any principle of the principles of reason and its laws (2), even though some researchers do not even accept the law of causality or those primary laws of reason, since the relationship between cause and effect - according to this view - is not based on the principle of non-contradiction, which the rationalists consider a necessary law of the primary laws of reason, but rather on experience (3). Previously, John Locke championed this view in his book "An Essay Concerning Human Understanding", denying the existence of innate ideas, or what is called the first principles of minds, as the rationalists say. Locke refutes the evidence presented to confirm the validity of their claim as follows: First: The claim that these ideas are accepted by all people without exception is refuted by the existence of savage tribes that do not know them. Second: The claim that the human mind perceives these ideas simply upon its awareness and wakefulness is refuted by the fact that the mind cannot perceive those ideas upon its wakefulness in the early years of life, as evidenced by the fact that children are completely ignorant of them. For example, the statement that it is impossible for two contradictories to coexist at the same time is something that children, savages, and the feebleminded are ignorant of, despite its self-evidence. Thus, it cannot be said that such ideas are innate, but rather they are acquired through long experience (1). Despite the intensity of the disagreement between empiricists and rationalists, that does not mean an absolute denial by rationalists of the importance of sensation or vice versa. Rather, the point of contention lies in which of them is the origin and which is the derivative (2). And if anything contrary to this occurs, it is a departure from the general direction of this or that side, and a reprehensible extremism whose consequences are not borne by the majority of empiricists or rationalists (3). With regard to the stance of the Noble Quran on experience or sensation, experience - in the view of some scholars of its verses - represents knowledge of the consequences of things, and this method in
(1) Adnan Zarzur, Maqala fi al-Ma'rifa, pp. 29-30.
(2) See regarding the position of the empiricists: Rajih al-Kurdi, previous reference, pp. 540-581; and al-Zanidi, previous reference, pp. 526-528. And regarding the position of the rationalists: al-Kurdi, previous reference, pp. 583-584; and al-Zanidi, previous reference, pp. 526-528; and Muhammad Jawad Rida, Falsafat al-Tarbiya, pp. 333-334. (3) This refers to the sect of al-Sumaniyya, who are (idol worshipers and believers in reincarnation; they were called al-Sumaniyya after Somnath in India. See: Nazariyyat al-Ma'rifa fi al-Quran by Ayatullah Jawad Amuli, footnote (1)). This sect claims that there is no way to know anything except through the five senses, they invalidated theoretical sciences, and they claimed that all doctrines are false. Their statement necessitates the invalidation of their own doctrine, because the statement invalidating a doctrine is itself a doctrine. (See: Usul al-Din by Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, pp. 10-11; and also al-Farq bayn al-Firaq, p. 311). The sophists followed this doctrine. (See: al-Insan wa al-'Aql by Na'if Ma'ruf, pp. 12-13). Conversely, transcendentalism exaggerates the importance of reason to the extent that it makes it the sole source of knowledge, because all sciences are latent in it, and the world of sensation works to confuse the knowledge of reason. (See: previous reference of al-Zanidi, pp. 527-528)
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the role of sense perception in knowledge. The author begins by affirming the importance of the senses as a source of knowledge, noting that ordinary people rely almost exclusively on sensory experience for their understanding of the world. Sensory perceptions form the basis of most truths about the objective external world. The author then outlines the conditions under which sensory knowledge becomes certain: repeated sensory perceptions that are consistent across different senses and with the testimonies of others, and that do not contradict the fundamental principles of reason. However, the author notes that some researchers reject even the law of causality, which rationalists consider a primary rational principle, instead grounding causality in experience – an empiricist view. The author then presents John Locke's denial of innate ideas, as expressed in his 'Essay Concerning Human Understanding'. Locke argues against the rationalist position that certain ideas are innate and universally accepted. His first argument is that if these ideas were universally accepted, then all peoples would hold them, but there exist savage tribes who do not. His second argument is that if these ideas were perceived immediately upon mental awareness, then children would know them from infancy, but they are ignorant even of self-evident principles like the impossibility of contradiction. Therefore, such ideas are acquired through long experience. The author then clarifies that the debate between empiricists and rationalists is not about denying the other's contribution entirely, but about which is primary and which secondary. Extremism in either direction is condemned. Finally, the author briefly touches on the Quranic stance, indicating that experience (or sensation) is seen by some exegetes as providing knowledge of the consequences of things. This passage is an expansion on the epistemological debate, drawing on Western philosophical arguments but contextualizing them within an Islamic framework, as seen in the references to the Quran and Islamic sects like al-Sumaniyya. The author uses the example of the impossibility of contradiction (a principle of logic) to illustrate Locke's point, which is a good Islamic example as it relates to the law of non-contradiction used in Islamic logic (Kalam). The passage also warns against extreme positions like sensualism (al-Sumaniyya) and transcendentalism, both of which are criticized for their one-sidedness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Locke reject the claim that innate ideas are universal?
A) Because they are not found in children.
B) Because there are savage tribes that do not know them.
C) Because they contradict the law of non-contradiction.
D) Because they are only known to philosophers.

Key Takeaway
Locke denies innate ideas by showing they are neither universal nor known from birth, arguing that all knowledge comes from experience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Apply Locke's first argument to the claim that 'the belief in one God is innate in all humans.' Would the existence of atheists refute this? Discuss how an Islamic scholar might defend the fitrah doctrine while acknowledging that some people do not explicitly believe.
?
Construct a counterargument from an Islamic perspective: using the concept of fitrah, explain how Locke's second argument (children do not know principles) may not disprove innate disposition, as disposition is not the same as explicit knowledge.

The Quranic Stance on Experience and Avoiding Extremes
Quranic view on experience and criticism of extremes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic view of experience as knowledge of consequences and identify the two extreme positions (al-Sumaniyya and transcendentalism) that the author criticizes.

Core Idea
The Quran values experience as revealing consequences, while rejecting both pure empiricism (al-Sumaniyya) and pure rationalism (transcendentalism).

The passage concludes by addressing the Quranic stance on sensory experience and warns against two extremist positions. Some exegetes interpret that the Quran presents experience (tajriba) as a means to know the consequences of things, encouraging observation of nature. The author then warns against the sect of al-Sumaniyya, who claimed that only sensory knowledge is valid and denied theoretical sciences, and against transcendentalism, which made reason the sole source of knowledge. The balanced Islamic position is that both senses and reason are valid sources when used appropriately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic view on experience
The author mentions that according to some scholars of the Quran, experience represents knowledge of the consequences of things. This refers to learning from observation and trial.
2
Find the first extreme: al-Sumaniyya
Al-Sumaniyya are described as idol worshipers who deny any knowledge except through the five senses. They reject theoretical knowledge and all doctrines except their own. The author notes a self-contradiction: their own position is a doctrine, so they invalidate themselves.
This is used as an example of extreme empiricism.
3
Find the second extreme: transcendentalism
Transcendentalism is characterized as exaggerating the role of reason, making it the sole source of knowledge, claiming all sciences are latent in it, and viewing sensory experience as a distraction.
This is the extreme rationalist position.
4
Understand the balanced middle path
The author implies that both senses and reason are legitimate sources, and extremism is condemnable. This reflects the Islamic epistemological principle that knowledge comes from multiple sources: revelation, reason, and senses.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
أهمية الحواس

تحتل الحواس - بوصفها مصدراً للمعرفة وطريقة لها - أهمية لا يقلل من قدرها باحث منصف. فالحس أحد منافذ المعرفة إلى نفس الإنسان، ويكاد المرء العادي لا يعترف بسواها وسيلة لمعرفته إذ إن معارفه كلها مبنية على ما رآه وسمعه ولمسه بنفسه.
ومعظم حقائقه (Truths) عن الدنيا الموضوعية والدنيا الخارجية المحيطة به إنما هي مدركات حسية (۱).
ولا شك أن المعرفة الحسية تكون يقينية عندما يُقدم الحس شهادته مؤكدة قاطعة بعد عمليات الإدراك الحسي المتواترة، والمتفقة مع شهادات الحواس الأخرى، وشهادات الآخرين من غير أن تتعارض مع أصل من أصول العقل وقوانينه (۲)، مع أن بعض الباحثين لا يسلّم حتى بقانون العلية أو قوانين العقل الأولية تلك، إذ إن العلاقة بين العلة والمعلول لا تقوم -حسب هذه الوجهة- على مبدأ عدم التناقض الصوري، الذي يذهب إليه العقليـون بوصفه قانوناً حتمياً من قوانين العقل الأولية، وإنما على أساس التجربة (۳).
ومن قبل تزعم (جون لوك) لواء هذه المقولة في كتابه (مقالة في العقل البشري فذهب إلى إنكار وجود أفكار أولية موروثة، أو مايسمى ببدائــه العقول، كما يقول أصحاب المذهب العقلي.
ويرد (لوك) على ما يُقدّم من أدلة تؤكد صحة دعوتهم بما يلي: أولاً : إن القول بأن هذه الأفكار مسلم بها مـن جميـع النـاس بـلا استثناء
محجوج بوجود قبائل متوحشة لا تعرفها.
ثانياً : إن القول بأن العقل البشري يدرك هذه الأفكار بمجرد وعيه ويقظته محجوج بأن العقل لا يستطيع إدراك تلك الآراء بمجرد يقظته في السنين الأولى من العمر، بدليل أن الأطفال تجهلها تماماً. فالقول مثلاً باستحالة اجتماع النقيضين في وقت واحد أمر يجهله الأطفال والمتوحشون والبلهاء على الرغم من بداهته. وبذلك فلا يمكن القول بفطرية مثل هذه الآراء، بل هي مكتسبة بتجربة طويلة (١).
وعلى الرغم من حدّة الخلاف بين الحسيين والعقليين إلا أن ذلك لا يعني إنكار العقليين المطلق لأهمية الحس أو العكس، وإنمـا مـدار الخلاف كامن في أيهما الأصل، وأيهما الفرع له (٢).

?
Read Quranic verses that encourage observation of nature (e.g., Surah Al-Imran: 190-191). How do they show that experience (sensory observation) leads to knowledge of Allah? How does this avoid the extreme of al-Sumaniyya (only senses) and transcendentalism (only reason)?

Empirical Refutation of Innate Ideas
Author critiques innate ideas using empirical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's inductive argument against innate ideas and evaluate its strength using Islamic epistemological criteria.

Core Idea
Children's ignorance proves that even the most obvious principles are not innate.

This lesson focuses on the author's central argument against the doctrine of innate ideas (fitriyya). He points to the fact that children, savages, and the mentally impaired do not know the principle of non-contradiction, despite its supposed self-evidence. This observation serves as empirical evidence that such knowledge is acquired through experience, not present from birth. We will analyze this argument as an inductive inference and assess its force in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target doctrine
Find where the author states the claim he is refuting: that the intellect grasps certain ideas merely by being awake (فطرية).
The target is the view that logical and metaphysical principles are innate.
2
Extract the counterevidence
Locate the evidence the author offers: children, savages, and idiots are ignorant of the impossibility of two contradictories coexisting.
This is an empirical observation meant to disprove innateness.
3
Classify the inference type
Recognize that the author is using an inductive generalization: because many individuals lack this knowledge, it is likely acquired, not innate.
Inductive arguments in Islamic epistemology can provide strong support but not absolute certainty.
4
Evaluate the argument's strength
Consider whether the observation of ignorance is sufficient to deny innateness. Does the author assume that if something were innate, everyone would know it?
The argument is persuasive but may be questioned if innateness is understood as potential rather than actual knowledge.

ثانياً : إن القول بأن العقل البشري يدرك هذه الأفكار بمجرد وعيه ويقظته محجوج بأن العقل لا يستطيع إدراك تلك الآراء بمجرد يقظته في السنين الأولى العمر، بدليل أن الأطفال تجهلها تماماً. فالقول مثلاً باستحالة اجتماع النقيضين في وقت واحد أمر يجهله الأطفال والمتوحشون والبلهاء على الرغم من بداهته. وبذلك فلا يمكن القول بفطرية مثل هذه الآراء، بل هي مكتسبة، وبتجربة طويلة. وعلى الرغم من حدّة الخلاف بين الحسيين والعقليين إلا أن ذلك لا يعني إنكار العقليين المطلق لأهمية الحس أو العكس، وإنما مدار الخلاف كامن في أيهما الأصل، وأيهما الفرع له. ولتن حدث ما يخالف هذا فهو خروج على الاتجاه العام لدى هذا الطرف أو ذاك، وتطرف مذموم لا يحمل تبعاته جمهور الحسيين أو العقليين. أشير هنا إلى فرقة السُّمَنيَّة وهم (عبدة الأصنام والقائلون بالتناسخ، وقيل لهم السمنية نسبة إلى سومنات الهند انظر : نظرية المعرفة في القرآن لآية الله جواد آمليه الهامش (۱)). وتزعم هذه الفرقة أنه لا سبيل إلى معرفة شيء إلا عن طريق الحواس الخمس، وأبطلوا العلوم النظرية، وزعموا أن المذاهب كلّها باطلة. ويلزمهم على هذا القول إبطال مذهبهم، لأن القول بإبطال المذهب مذهب. (انظر: أصول الدين لأبي منصور البغدادي، ۱۰-۱۱، وكذا الفرق بين الفرق، ۳۱۱). وممن شايع هذا المذهب السفسطائيون. (انظر: الإنسان والعقل لنايف معروف ۱۲ - ۱۳). وبالمقابل فإن الترانستتدالية تغالي في أهمية العقل إلى الحد الذي تجعله مصدراً أوحد للمعرفة، لأن العلوم كلها كامنة فيه، وعالم الحس يعمل على تشويش معارف العقل. (انظر: المرجع السابق للزنيدي، (٥٢٧ - ٥٢٨).
Second: The claim that the human intellect grasps these ideas merely by its awareness and wakefulness is refuted by the fact that the intellect cannot perceive those views merely by wakefulness in the early years of life, evidenced by children being completely ignorant of them. For example, the impossibility of the coexistence of two contradictories at one time is something children, savages, and idiots are ignorant of, despite its self-evidence. Thus, one cannot claim the innateness of such views; rather, they are acquired through long experience. Despite the intensity of the dispute between empiricists and rationalists, that does not mean the rationalists absolutely deny the importance of the senses or vice versa; rather, the crux of the dispute lies in which is the origin and which is the branch. If anything contrary occurs, it is a departure from the general trend of that party or the other, and a blameworthy extremism not borne by the majority of empiricists or rationalists. I refer here to the sect of al-Sumaniyya, who are idol worshippers and believers in reincarnation, called al-Sumaniyya after Somnath in India (see: Theory of Knowledge in the Quran by Ayatollah Jawad Amuli, footnote 1). This sect claims that there is no way to know anything except through the five senses, and they invalidate theoretical sciences, claiming that all doctrines are false. This entails the invalidation of their own doctrine, since the claim that doctrines are false is itself a doctrine. (See: Usul al-Din by Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, 10-11, and also al-Farq bayn al-Firaq, 311). Among those who follow this doctrine are the Sophists. (See: al-Insan wa al-Aql by Naif Maarouf, 12-13). In contrast, the transcendentalists exaggerate the importance of reason to the extent that they make it the sole source of knowledge, because all sciences are latent in it, and the sensory world works to confuse the intellect's cognitions. (See: the previous reference by al-Zunidi, 527-528).
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage critiques the doctrine of innate ideas (fitriyya) by pointing out that children and savages do not know even the most basic logical principles (like non-contradiction) despite their claimed obviousness. Therefore, these ideas must be acquired through experience. The author then clarifies that the debate between empiricists (Hissiyyun) and rationalists (Aqliyyun) is not about total rejection of either source, but about which is primary. Extreme positions are represented by al-Sumaniyya, who deny any knowledge beyond sense perception, and the transcendentalists, who make reason the sole source and view the senses as disruptive. The Sumaniyya are refuted by a self-defeating argument: their claim that all doctrines are false is itself a doctrine, so they must reject their own position. The transcendentalists are criticized for over-reliance on reason. This passage thus stakes out a middle ground, advocating for both sense and reason in knowledge acquisition.

Key Terms
فطرية
حسيين
عقليين
السُّمَنيَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence does the author use to refute the claim that the principle of non-contradiction is innate?
A) The principle is not found in any scripture.
B) Children, savages, and idiots are ignorant of it.
C) The principle is too complex for the human mind.
D) The principle is only known through revelation.

Key Takeaway
Observable ignorance of supposedly self-evident principles suggests they are acquired through experience, not innate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
A child does not know that 2+2=4 until taught. Construct an inductive argument similar to the author's to show that arithmetic knowledge is not innate, using only Islamic educational contexts (e.g., teaching Qur'anic counting).
?
Identify the inductive steps in the author's argument and state whether the conclusion is yaqini (certain) or zanni (probable). Explain why.

Balancing Sense and Reason: Critique of Extremes
Author critiques extreme empiricism and rationalism, advocating a middle path.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the author's moderate position between empiricism and rationalism and identify the self-defeating nature of radical empiricism (al-Sumaniyya).

Core Idea
The real debate is about primacy, not total rejection; extremes self-destruct.

After refuting innate ideas, the author clarifies that the disagreement between empiricists (hissiyyun) and rationalists (aqliyyun) is not about whether sense or reason have value, but which is primary. He then exposes two extreme groups: al-Sumaniyya, who deny any knowledge beyond sense perception, and the transcendentalists, who exalt reason to the exclusion of sense. The author shows that al-Sumaniyya's position refutes itself. This lesson will dissect that critique.

Guided Path
1
Clarify the moderate position
Find where the author says the dispute is about 'which is the origin and which is the branch', not about total rejection.
Both sense and reason are accepted; the issue is hierarchy.
2
Identify the extreme empiricist position
Locate al-Sumaniyya's claim: only the five senses provide knowledge; theoretical sciences are invalid.
They are cited as an example of extreme empiricism.
3
Analyze the self-defeating argument
The author points out that claiming 'all doctrines are false' is itself a doctrine, so it must also be false. This is a classic logical refutation.
This is a performative contradiction; the claim cannot be consistently stated.
4
Contrast the rationalist extreme
Find the description of transcendentalists: reason as the sole source, senses as disruptive.
This is opposed to the author's balanced view.

?

?

Empirical Knowledge as the Decisive Path to Truth: A Quranic Foundation
Author defines empirical knowledge and cites Quranic verse about testing benefit and harm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the author grounds empirical knowledge in Quranic methodology, citing the verse of Ibrahim and the pre-test/post-test logic.

Core Idea
Empirical knowledge, tested through benefit and harm, is the Quranically sanctioned path to truth.

This passage positions empirical knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-tajribiyya) as the decisive means to truth, tracing its origins to human trial of plants. The author then elevates this method by grounding it in the Quranic story of Ibrahim, who questions whether idols can hear or benefit. The passage even outlines a quasi-experimental design with pre-test and post-test, showing the Quranic basis for modern scientific reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition of knowledge
The author calls knowledge the ‘decisive means to reaching truth’. Note that this is a functional definition emphasizing empirical testing.
Al-ma'rifa is defined as the decisive method, not just information.
2
Recognize the historical testing method
Humans tested plants by eating them to distinguish benefit from harm. This is presented as the origin of empirical testing.
The method is trial-based, using sensory experience.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse of Ibrahim
The verse asks whether idols hear, benefit, or harm. The author presents this as evidence that testing for benefit/harm is a Quranic principle.
The verse is from Surah al-Shu'ara' 26:72-73.
4
Extract the experimental structure
The author mentions pre-test, post-test, independent variable intervention, and dependent variable outcome. This mirrors modern controlled experiments.
The passage uses the terms 'pre-test' (ikhtibar qabli) and 'post-test' (ikhtibar ba'di).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعرفة تعدّ الوسيلة القاطعة لبلوغ الحقيقة. وهي طريقة استخدمها الإنسان حين كان يجمع النباتات ويجربها ويأكلها ليميز بين النافع والضار. وكلما تمكن المرء من تحقيق أكثر النفع يكون قد اقترب من الحق أكثر. وهذا منهج قرآني معتبر فقد جاء على لسان إبراهيم: ﴿هَلْ يَسْمَعُونَكُمْ إِذْ تَدْعُونَ، أَوْ يَنْفَعُونَكُمْ أَوْ يَضُرُّونَ ﴾ [الشعراء: ٧٢/٢٦-٧٣](١). ويوسعنا أن نقول إن القرآن الكريم يقدّم هنا إشارات إلى ضرورة اختبار بعض الظواهر اختباراً قبلياً وآخر بعدياً لينتج عنهما الفرق في النفع أو التأثير، قبل أن يطرأ متغير مستقل جديد وبعد أن يطرأ، ليظهر ذلك جلياً في المتغير التابع في الحالين.
Knowledge is the decisive means to reaching truth. It is a method used by humans when they were gathering plants, testing them, and eating them to distinguish between beneficial and harmful. And the more a person is able to achieve benefit, the closer he has come to the truth. This is a respected Quranic methodology, for it came on the tongue of Ibrahim: 'Do they hear you when you call, or do they benefit you or harm you?' [Al-Shu'ara' 26:72-73]. And we may say that the noble Quran here provides indications of the necessity of testing some phenomena with a pre-test and a post-test to produce the difference in benefit or effect, before an independent new variable intervenes and after it intervenes, so that becomes clear in the dependent variable in both cases.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage introduces empirical knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-tajribiyya) as the decisive means to truth. The author grounds it in human historical practice—collecting and testing plants—and then anchors it in the Quranic verse where Ibrahim asks about idols not hearing or benefiting. The author extends this to outline a quasi-experimental method: pre-test and post-test with a control variable, showing the Quranic basis for scientific methodology.

Key Terms
المعرفة (al-ma'rifa): Knowledge gained through empirical testing and experience, seen as the decisive path to truth.
الحس (al-hiss): Empirical observation and sensory experience, part of the method of testing.
النفع والضر (al-naf' wa al-darr): Benefit and harm as criteria for distinguishing truth, derived from Quranic context.
اختبار قبلي (ikhtibar qabli): Pre-test, observation before the intervention.
اختبار بعدي (ikhtibar ba'di): Post-test, observation after the intervention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what Quranic example supports the empirical method?
A) The story of Adam naming the angels
B) Ibrahim's question about idols hearing or benefiting
C) The splitting of the sea for Musa
D) The creation of the universe in six days

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse of Ibrahim (AS) provides a clear foundation for empirical testing as a method to distinguish truth from falsehood, anticipating modern experimental design.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the logical structure of pre-test and post-test in another Quranic verse, such as the story of Abraham's argument about the sun and moon (Al-An'am 6:76-78). Write a short paragraph showing how Abraham uses a sequential observation (pre-test before sunset, post-test after) to identify the true Creator.
?
Consider the hadith: 'There is no disease that Allah has created except that He also has created its treatment.' This encourages empirical medical testing. Write a one-sentence explanation of how the empirical method from the passage (test for benefit/harm) applies to finding cures.

Hearing as a Sensory Tool in the Quran
Author defines hearing and sight, then illustrates the Quranic emphasis on hearing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of hearing (al-sam') as given in the passage and explain its significance in the Quranic worldview.

Core Idea
Hearing is the gateway to guidance; the Quran's 139 mentions underscore its primacy in human responsibility.

In this passage, the author defines the sense of hearing and sight, then demonstrates through Quranic verses how hearing is uniquely emphasized as a tool for receiving divine guidance. We will explore the definition and the logical relationship between hearing, belief, and accountability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and differentia in the definition of hearing
Find where the author defines hearing. Note that it is placed under the broader category of 'sensation' (al-hiss), and the specific difference is that it perceives sounds via the ear.
The definition is: 'The sensation by which sounds are perceived, whose instrument is the ear.'
2
Note the statistical prominence of hearing in the Quran
The author states that the word hearing and its derivatives occur 139 times individually, more than sight (106 times). This numerical emphasis signals the Quran's special focus on hearing.
3
Examine how hearing is linked to belief and obedience
Read the verses cited: the command to listen to the Quran, the response 'We hear and obey', and the likening of disbelievers to the dead. Notice the pattern: hearing is the prerequisite for responding to truth.
Verses: 7:204, 24:51, 6:36, etc.
4
Understand the analogy of disbelievers as dead due to non-use of hearing
The author compares disbelievers to the dead because both fail to benefit from hearing. This illustrates the logical consequence of neglecting the sense of hearing for guidance.
The verse 6:36: 'Only those who hear will respond.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
وفي هذا السياق أرشد الله تعالى موسى - عليه السلام- إلى استخدام أداة النظر لملاحظة التغير الذي سيطرأ على الجبل حالة تجلي الله – سبحانه له، ومنه يصل المرء إلى حقيقة تتصل بالخالق - سبحانه، وهي استحالة رؤيته في الدنيا
وَلَمّا جاءَ مُوسَى لِمِيقَاتِنا وَكَلَّمَهُ رَبُّهُ قالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنْظُرْ إِلَيْكَ قَالَ لَنْ تَرانِي وَلَكِن انظُرْ إِلَى الْجَبَل فَإِن اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكَّا وَخَرَّ مُوسَى صَعِقَا فَلَمّا أَفاقَ قَالَ سُبْحانَكَ تُبْتُ إِلَيْكَ وَأَنَا أَوَّلُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٤٣/٧].
ونظراً للمكانة التي تحتلها أدوات الحس في القرآن؛ فقد تكرر لفظ السمع ومشتقاته المتعلقة بالإنسان (۱۳۹) مرّة منفرداً(۱) . في حين تكرر لفظ البصر أكثر من مئة مرّة (١٠٦) منفرداً (۳). وجمع بينهما في مواضع كثيرة أخرى، كما سنشير إلى ذلك لاحقاً -بإذن الله تعالى.
وقد عُرف السمع بأنه: (الإحساس الذي به إدراك الأصوات، الذي آلته الصماخ والإبصار الإحساس المدرك للذوات، الذي آلته الحدقة))(۳). ومن المواطن التي ورد فيها ذكر السمع مستقلاً في القرآن بوصفها إحدى نعم الله الكبرى، بما يحمل دعوة الإنسان لتوظيفها على النحو المشروع: وَكَمْ أَهْلَكْنَا قَبْلَهُمْ مِنْ قَرْنِ هَلْ تُحِسُّ مِنْهُمْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ أَوْ تَسْمَعُ لَهُمْ ركزا [مريم: ۹۸/۱۹] ﴿وَإِذا قُرِئَ الْقُرْآنُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنْصِتُوا لَعَلَّكُمْ تُرْحَمُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٠٤/٧].
والي آمَنتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ فَاسْمَعُونِ ﴾ [يس: ٢٥/٣٦].
وَلَوْلا إِذْ سَمِعْتُمُوهُ قُلْتُمْ ما يَكُون لَنا أَنْ تَتَكَلَّمَ بِهَذَا سُبْحانَكَ هَذَا بُهتان عظيم [النور: ١٦/٢٤].
إنما كان قَوْلَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذا دُعُوا إِلَى اللهِ وَرَسُولِهِ لِيَحْكُمَ بَيْنَهُمْ أَن يَقُولُوا سَمِعْنَا وَأَطَعْنا﴾ [النور: ٥١/٢٤].
﴿قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ إِنْ جَعَلَ اللهُ عَلَيْكُمُ اللَّيْلَ سَرْمَداً إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ مَنْ إِلَهُ غَيْرُ اللهِ يَأْتِيكُمْ بِضِياء أَفَلا تَسْمَعُونَ﴾ [القصص: ۷۱/۲۸].
ولأهمية السمع شبه الكفار بالموتى بجامع عدم استفادة كلا الفريقين من هذه الأداة:
إِنما يَسْتَجِيبُ الَّذِينَ يَسْمَعُونَ وَالْمَوْتَى يَبْعَثُهُمُ اللَّهُ ﴾ [الأنعام: ٣٦/٦]. : وإنك لا تُسْمِعُ الْمَوْتَى وَلا تُسْمِعُ الصُّمَّ الدُّعَاءَ إِذَا وَلَّوْا مُدْبِرِينَ، وَمَا أنتَ بِهادِي العُمْيِ عَنْ ضَلالَتِهِمْ إِنْ تُسْمِعُ إِلَّا مَنْ يُؤْمِنُ بِآيَاتِنَا فَهُمْ مُسْلِمُونَ ﴾ [النمل: ۸۰/۲۷-۸۱] .
ولأهمية السمع كذلك جعل الله تعالى مناط إنهاء إجارة المشرك المستجير سماع القرآن الكريم كمحطة رئيسة قبل بلوغه مأمنه:
﴿وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلامَ اللَّهِ ثُمَّ أَبْلِغْهُ مَامَنَهُ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُمْ قَوْمٌ لا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [التوبة: ٦/٩].
ويصور القرآن حالة الكفر في منتهى الإعراض عن سماع الحق، وذلك حينما يضع المرء بين ذاته وبين دعوة التوحيد حجاباً يحول دون أن يلامس سمعه فكر جديد أو رأي مخالف؛ فقال على لسان نوح عليه السلام:
Chapter Three: First Section - Sensation. In this context, Allah Almighty guided Moses - peace be upon him - to use the tool of sight to observe the change that would occur to the mountain at the manifestation of Allah - glorified be He - to him, and thereby one arrives at a truth related to the Creator - glorified be He - which is the impossibility of seeing Him in this world. And when Moses came at Our appointed time and his Lord spoke to him, he said: 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You.' [Allah] said: 'You will not see Me, but look at the mountain; if it should remain in its place, then you will see Me.' And when his Lord appeared to the mountain, He rendered it level, and Moses fell unconscious. And when he awoke, he said: 'Exalted are You! I have repented to You, and I am the first of the believers.' [Al-A'raf 7:143]. And due to the status occupied by the senses in the Quran, the word 'hearing' and its derivatives related to humans occur 139 times individually, while the word 'sight' occurs more than a hundred times (106) individually. And they are combined in many other places, as we will indicate later - by Allah's permission. Hearing has been defined as: 'The sensation by which sounds are perceived, whose instrument is the ear, and sight is the sensation that perceives objects, whose instrument is the pupil.' Among the instances in which hearing is mentioned independently in the Quran as one of Allah's great blessings, carrying an invitation for man to employ it in the lawful manner: 'And how many generations have We destroyed before them. Do you perceive from them any [remaining] one or hear from them a sound?' [Maryam 19:98]; 'And when the Quran is recited, then listen to it and pay attention that you may receive mercy.' [Al-A'raf 7:204]; 'And I have believed in your Lord, so listen to me.' [Ya-Sin 36:25]; 'And why, when you heard it, did you not say: 'It is not for us to speak of this. Exalted are You; this is a great slander.' [An-Nur 24:16]; 'The only statement of the [true] believers when they are called to Allah and His Messenger to judge between them is that they say: 'We hear and we obey.' [An-Nur 24:51]; 'Say, 'Have you considered: if Allah should make for you the night continuous until the Day of Resurrection, what deity other than Allah could bring you light? Then will you not hear?'' [Al-Qasas 28:71]. And due to the importance of hearing, He likened the disbelievers to the dead, through the commonality of both groups not benefiting from this tool: 'Only those who hear will respond. But the dead - Allah will resurrect them.' [Al-An'am 6:36]; 'And indeed, you cannot make the dead hear, nor can you make the deaf hear the call when they turn their backs retreating. And you are not [able to] guide the blind from their error. You will only make hear those who believe in Our verses so they are Muslims.' [An-Naml 27:80-81]. And due to the importance of hearing, Allah also made the termination of the protection of a polytheist who seeks asylum contingent upon hearing the Quran as a major station before he reaches his place of security: 'And if any one of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the words of Allah. Then deliver him to his place of safety. That is because they are a people who do not know.' [At-Tawbah 9:6]. And the Quran depicts the state of disbelief in the utmost aversion to hearing the truth, when a person places between himself and the call to monotheism a veil that prevents his hearing from touching new thought or opposing opinion; so he said on the tongue of Noah, peace be upon him:
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and exegetical discussion about the sense of hearing (al-sam') in the Quran. The author begins by referencing the story of Moses (peace be upon him) asking to see Allah, and the command to look at the mountain as a lesson in using the tool of sight to infer truths about the Creator, specifically the impossibility of seeing Him in this world. Then, the author emphasizes the importance of the senses in the Quran, particularly hearing and sight. The author provides statistical frequency: the word 'hearing' (sam') and its derivatives occur 139 times, while 'sight' (basar) occurs 106 times individually, and they are often combined. Following this, the author gives a technical definition: hearing is the sensation by which sounds are perceived, with the ear as its organ; sight is the sensation that perceives objects, with the pupil as its organ. The rest of the passage illustrates the Quranic emphasis on hearing through numerous verses, showing hearing as a great blessing, a tool for receiving guidance, and a criterion for moral responsibility. The author also notes that disbelievers are likened to the dead because they do not benefit from hearing the truth, and that hearing the Quran is a prerequisite for granting asylum to a polytheist. The passage concludes by describing the extreme aversion to hearing the truth as a veil that prevents new ideas from reaching the heart, citing the example of Noah (peace be upon him).

البصر
الحس

A) The sensation by which objects are perceived, whose instrument is the pupil.
B) The sensation by which sounds are perceived, whose instrument is the ear.
C) The ability to understand speech, whose instrument is the mind.
D) The sense that distinguishes between right and wrong.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hearing as a sensory tool, combined with its 139 Quranic occurrences, establishes hearing as the primary channel for receiving and responding to divine guidance.

The Epistemological Role of Hearing and Sight in the Quran
Author discusses the Quranic emphasis on hearing and sight as primary means of knowledge acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic rationale for emphasizing hearing and sight over other senses in knowledge acquisition.

Core Idea
The Quran singles out hearing and sight because they are the primary gates to knowledge and belief.

The author of this passage explores why the Quran repeatedly mentions hearing and sight together. Through a careful analysis of Quranic verses, he argues that these two senses are the most effective for learning and for perceiving the evidences of true belief. This lesson will help you understand the epistemological reasoning behind this emphasis and the subtle linguistic cues that reinforce it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the senses highlighted
Look at the Quranic verses cited. Which two faculties are repeatedly mentioned? The author focuses on hearing (al-sam‘) and sight (al-basar). Note how they appear together in many verses.
The author also cites verses that mention each sense separately.
2
Determine the author's ranking
The author states that hearing is more effective than sight in developing, acquiring, and comprehending knowledge. Find the sentence where he makes this comparison.
Sight is still important but comes in a degree after hearing.
3
Extract the reasons for their special mention
The author gives two reasons: (1) hearing and sight are the basis of animal life, human perfection, and acquisition of primary sciences; (2) perception of the evidences of true belief is only through them. Locate these reasons in the passage.
The reasons explain why the Quran singles them out repeatedly.
4
Analyze the linguistic pattern
When hearing and sight are mentioned together, hearing appears in the singular (sam‘) while sight appears in the plural (absar) except in one verse. The author draws attention to this. Consider what this grammatical detail might indicate about their treatment in the Quran.
The exceptional verse is where basar appears singular; can you find it?
5
Consider the qualification about other senses
The author clarifies that singling out hearing and sight does not negate the importance of other senses. He says it might be a case of mentioning the part to stand for the whole. This prevents a misinterpretation that only these two senses matter.
This shows careful epistemological reasoning, not exclusivity.

﴿وَفِي أَنْفُسِكُمْ أَفَلا تُبْصِرُونَ ﴾ [الذاريات: ٢١/٥١].
وَيُرِيكُمْ آيَاتِهِ فَأَيَّ آيَاتِ اللهِ تُنْكِرُونَ) [غافر: ٨١/٤٠].
قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ شُرَكَاءَكُمُ الَّذِينَ تَدْعُونَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ أَرُونِي مَاذَا خَلَقُوا مِنَ الأَرْضِ أَمْ لَهُمْ شِرْكٌ فِي السَّماواتِ أَمْ آتَيْنَاهُمْ كِتاباً فَهُمْ عَلَى بَيِّنَةٍ مِنه...
[فاطر: ٤٠/٣٥]
هَذا خَلْقَ اللهِ فَأَرُونِي ماذا خَلَقَ الَّذِينَ مِنْ دُونِهِ بَلِ الظَّالِمُونَ فِي ضَلالٍ مبين [لقمان: ۱۱/۳۱]. وَجَعَلُوا الْمَلائِكَةَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ عِبادُ الرَّحْمَنِ إِنَاثًا أَشَهِدُوا خَلْقَهُمْ سَتُكْتَبُ شَهادَتْهُمْ وَيُسْأَلُونَ ﴾ [الزخرف: ١٩/٤٣].
وهذا يشير إلى أهمية حاسة البصر في عملية التعلم، وإن كانت تأتي في درجة تالية للسمع من حيث فاعليتها في تنمية المعرفة وتحصيلها واستيعابها. وهناك مواطن جُمِعَ فيها بين السمع والبصر :
قُلْ مَنْ يَرْزُقُكُمْ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ أَمْ مَنْ يَمْلِكُ السَّمْعَ وَالْأَبْصارَ
[يونس: ۳۱/۱۰].
يوما كانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ وَمَا كَانُوا يُبْصِرُونَ ﴾ [هود: ٢٠/١١]. وَعَرَضْنَا جَهَنَّمَ يَوْمَئِذٍ لِلْكَافِرِينَ عَرْضاً، الَّذِينَ كَانَتْ أَعْيُنُهُمْ فِي غِطَاء عَنْ ذِكْرِي وَكَانُوا لا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ سَمْعاً﴾ [الكهف: ۱۰۰/۱۸-۱۰۱].
أسْمِعْ بِهِمْ وَأَبْصِرْ يَوْمَ يَأْتُونَنا لَكِنِ الظَّالِمُونَ الْيَوْمَ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِين
[مريم: ۳۸/۱۹].
أُولَئِكَ لَمْ يَكُونُوا مُعْجِزِينَ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَمَا كَانَ لَهُمْ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ مِنْ أَوْلِياءَ يُضاعَفُ لَهُمُ الْعَذابُ ما كانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ وَمَا كَانُوا يُبْصِرُونَ
[هود: ۲۰/۱۱]
وَاذْكُرْ فِي الْكِتابِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِنَّهُ كانَ صِدِّيقاً نَبِيّاً، إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ يَا أَبَتِ لِمَ
تَعْبُدُ ما لا يَسْمَعُ وَلا يُبْصِرُ وَلا يُغْنِي عَنكَ شَيْئًا [مريم: ٤١/١٩-٤٢]. ولاشك أن أعلى درجات الاستيعاب والتحصيل تلك التي يشترك فيها سمع المتعلم وبصره، ومن هنا كان لزاماً أن ترفد المعارف التي يشملها المحتوى
بتقنيات (سمع بصرية) ليتحقق أعلى مستوى من الاستيعاب والتحصيل. وفي ضوء هذا العرض لآيات السمع والبصر يجدر أن نشير إلى الأمور التالية: الأمر الأول: إن اختصاص القرآن الكريم أدائي السمع والأبصار بالذكر، على هذا النحو من التكرار دون غيرهما يعود إلى كونهما مدار الحياة الحيوانية، وكمال البشرية، وتحصيل العلوم الأولية (۱).
ولكون إدراك دلائل الاعتقاد الحق لا يكون إلا بهما (۳).
ولكن ذلك لا ينفي وجود أهمية قصوى لبقية الحواس، لأن اختصاص السمع والبصر بالذكر يعني الأهمية المتميزة بالخصوصية ليس أكثر. وقد يكون من باب ذكر الجزء لأهميته مع إرادة الكل في حقيقة الأمر.
الأمر الثاني: إن السمع حين ورد في القرآن الكريم بوصفه مصدر (سمع) مقروناً بالبصر؛ يرد مفرداً، في حين يرد (البصر) جمعاً (أبصار) إلا في موطن
واحد وهو قول الله تعالى:
(۱) محمد رشید رضا تفسير المنار، ٣٥٥/١١. (۲) ابن عاشور، تفسير التحرير والتنوير، ٢٣٢/١٣.
Chapter Three: First Section - Sense
And say, 'Observe what is in the heavens and the earth...' [Yunus 10:101]. Say, 'Have you considered if Allah should make for you the day continuous until the Day of Resurrection, what deity other than Allah could bring you night in which you rest? Then do you not see?' [Al-Qasas 28:72].
'And within yourselves. Then do you not see?' [Adh-Dhariyat 51:21].
'And He shows you His signs. So which of the signs of Allah do you deny?' [Ghafir 40:81].
Say, 'Have you considered your partners whom you invoke besides Allah? Show me what they have created from the earth, or have they partnership in the heavens? Or have We given them a book so they are upon clear evidence from it...' [Fatir 35:40].
'This is the creation of Allah. So show me what those other than Him have created. Rather, the wrongdoers are in manifest error.' [Luqman 31:11]. And they have made the angels, who are servants of the Most Merciful, females. Did they witness their creation? Their testimony will be recorded, and they will be questioned. [Az-Zukhruf 43:19].
And this indicates the importance of the sense of sight in the process of learning, even though it comes in a degree after hearing in terms of its effectiveness in developing, acquiring, and comprehending knowledge. And there are instances where hearing and sight are combined:
Say, 'Who provides for you from the heaven and the earth? Or who controls hearing and sight?' [Yunus 10:31].
'On the day they were unable to hear, and they did not see.' [Hud 11:20]. And We will present Hell on that Day to the disbelievers in plain view, those whose eyes were covered from My remembrance, and they were unable to hear. [Al-Kahf 18:100-101].
'How well they hear and see on the Day they come to Us! But the wrongdoers today are in manifest error.' [Maryam 19:38].
'Those were not causing failure [to Allah] on earth, nor did they have any protectors besides Allah. For them the punishment will be doubled. They were unable to hear, and they did not see.' [Hud 11:20].
And mention in the Book, Abraham. Indeed, he was a man of truth, a prophet. When he said to his father, 'O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear and does not see and does not benefit you at all?' [Maryam 19:41-42]. And there is no doubt that the highest levels of comprehension and acquisition are those in which the learner's hearing and sight participate. Hence, it is necessary to supply the knowledge included in the content with audio-visual techniques to achieve the highest level of comprehension and acquisition. In light of this presentation of the verses on hearing and sight, it is appropriate to point out the following: The first matter: That the Quran's specification of the two faculties of hearing and sight in this repeated manner, to the exclusion of others, is due to their being the basis of animal life, human perfection, and the acquisition of primary sciences (1).
And because perception of the evidences of true belief is only through them (3).
But that does not negate the existence of utmost importance for the rest of the senses, because specifying hearing and sight indicates distinguished importance by specificity, no more. And it may be a case of mentioning the part for its importance while intending the whole in reality.
The second matter: That hearing when it occurs in the Holy Quran as a source (sam') coupled with sight, comes in the singular, while (sight) comes in the plural (absar) except in one place, which is the saying of Allah Almighty:
(1) Muhammad Rashid Rida, Tafsir al-Manar, 11/355. (2) Ibn Ashur, Tafsir al-Tahrir wa al-Tanwir, 13/232.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion within a Quranic exegetical framework, focusing on the role of the senses of hearing and sight in acquiring knowledge. The author begins by citing numerous Quranic verses that highlight these senses, demonstrating their frequent mention. The commentary then argues that while sight is important, hearing is considered more effective in developing and comprehending knowledge. The author notes that some verses combine both senses. The core of the passage is the analysis of why the Quran specifically and repeatedly mentions hearing and sight. The author gives two reasons: first, they are the basis of animal life, human perfection, and the acquisition of primary sciences; second, perception of the evidences of true belief is only through them. The author clarifies that this does not deny the importance of other senses; the mention is due to their special significance, possibly a case of mentioning a part to stand for the whole. Finally, a grammatical observation is made: when hearing (sam') is mentioned with sight, it appears in the singular, while sight appears in the plural (absar) except in one Quranic instance. This linguistic detail underscores the unique treatment of these senses in the Quran.

البصر
الحس

According to the passage, how does the Quran typically use the words for hearing (sam') and sight (basar) when they are mentioned together?
A) Both appear in the singular.

C) Hearing appears in the singular, while sight appears in the plural.
D) Hearing appears in the plural, while sight appears in the singular.

Key Takeaway
The Quran emphasizes hearing and sight due to their foundational role in knowledge and belief, with hearing considered more effective, and a linguistic pattern reflects their distinct treatment.

Why the Quran Emphasizes Hearing and Sight
Author explains the Quran's emphasis on hearing and sight in knowledge acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Quran specifically highlights hearing and sight over other senses in knowledge acquisition.

Core Idea
Hearing and sight are foundational for human perfection and perception of divine proofs.

The Quran repeatedly pairs hearing and sight in verses about belief and knowledge. The author provides a reasoned explanation for this emphasis, rooted in their role as the primary tools for acquiring sciences and recognizing truth. Let us analyze the first matter he presents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses cited
Locate the three verses quoted at the beginning of the passage. Notice how they connect hearing and sight to belief, knowledge, and worship.
Verses from Surah Maryam, Hud, and Maryam again.
2
Extract the author's main claim
The author states that hearing and sight are the pivot of animal life, human perfection, and the acquisition of primary sciences. They are also necessary for perceiving the proofs of true belief.
This explains their repeated mention.
3
Understand the qualification
The author clarifies that other senses are still important; the emphasis is due to particular significance, possibly as a synecdoche (part for the whole).
Do not conclude that other senses are negligible.
4
Apply to educational context
The author concludes that highest learning involves both hearing and sight, recommending audio-visual techniques.
Connect to modern pedagogical insights.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
أسْمِعْ بِهِمْ وَأَبْصِرْ يَوْمَ يَأْتُونَنا لَكِنِ الظَّالِمُونَ الْيَوْمَ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِين [مريم: ۳۸/۱۹].
أُولَئِكَ لَمْ يَكُونُوا مُعْجِزِينَ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَمَا كَانَ لَهُمْ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ مِنْ أَوْلِياءَ يُضاعَفُ لَهُمُ الْعَذابُ ما كانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ وَمَا كَانُوا يُبْصِرُونَ [هود: ۲۰/۱۱]
وَاذْكُرْ فِي الْكِتابِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِنَّهُ كانَ صِدِّيقاً نَبِيّاً، إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ يَا أَبَتِ لِمَ تَعْبُدُ ما لا يَسْمَعُ وَلا يُبْصِرُ وَلا يُغْنِي عَنكَ شَيْئًا [مريم: ٤١/١٩-٤٢]. ولاشك أن أعلى درجات الاستيعاب والتحصيل تلك التي يشترك فيها سمع المتعلم وبصره، ومن هنا كان لزاماً أن ترفد المعارف التي يشملها المحتوى بتقنيات (سمع بصرية) ليتحقق أعلى مستوى من الاستيعاب والتحصيل. وفي ضوء هذا العرض لآيات السمع والبصر يجدر أن نشير إلى الأمور التالية: الأمر الأول: إن اختصاص القرآن الكريم أدائي السمع والأبصار بالذكر، على هذا النحو من التكرار دون غيرهما يعود إلى كونهما مدار الحياة الحيوانية، وكمال البشرية، وتحصيل العلوم الأولية (۱). ولكون إدراك دلائل الاعتقاد الحق لا يكون إلا بهما (۳). ولكن ذلك لا ينفي وجود أهمية قصوى لبقية الحواس، لأن اختصاص السمع والبصر بالذكر يعني الأهمية المتميزة بالخصوصية ليس أكثر. وقد يكون من باب ذكر الجزء لأهميته مع إرادة الكل في حقيقة الأمر.
الأمر الثاني: إن السمع حين ورد في القرآن الكريم بوصفه مصدر (سمع) مقروناً بالبصر؛ يرد مفرداً، في حين يرد (البصر) جمعاً (أبصار) إلا في موطن واحد وهو قول الله تعالى: وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً ﴾ [الإسراء: ٣٦/١٧]. هذا يرى بعض المفسرين أنه : أفرد السمع لأنه مصدر، فهو دال على وعن الجنس الموجود في جميع حواس الناس. وأما الأبصار فجيء به جمعاً لأنه اسم، فهو ليس نصاً في إفادة العموم لاحتمال توهم بصر مخصوص، فكان الجمع أدل على قصد العموم، وأنفى لاحتمال العهد ونحوه، بخلاف قوله: ﴿إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً) [الإسراء: ٣٦/١٧، لأن المراد الواحد لكل مخاطب بقوله: ﴿وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ ) .
ويمكن أن يكون ذلك ضرباً من ضروب الإعجاز، إذ إن حاسة السمع تستقبل الأصوات الصادرة من جميع الجهات في حين لا ترى العين إلا إذا اتجه الإنسان ببصره نحو الشيء الذي يريد أن يراه (۳ ). ومن ناحية أخرى فإنه إذا حدث صوت في مكان يجتمع فيه جمع من الناس فإنهم جميعاً سيسمعون الصوت ذاته تقريباً، بينما ينظر كل واحد منهـم صـوب الشيء الواحد من زوايا مختلفة (۳).
الأمر الثالث: إن القرآن الكريم يقدّم السمع على البصر كلما اقترنــا ببعضهما. ولعلّ ذلك يرجع إلى قوة السمع بحيث يستطيع الإدراك من الجهات الست، وفي الضوء والظلمة ولا يدرك البصر إلا من جهة المقابلة، وبواسطة من ضياء وشعاع. وهذا قول المعتزلة، ولكنه لا يسلم من نزاع(4).
(۱) محمد رشید رضا تفسير المنار، ٣٥٥/١١. (۲) ابن عاشور، تفسير التحرير والتنوير، ٢٣٢/١٣.
(۳) نجاتي، المرجع السابق، ۱۲۸.
(٤) أبو منصور البغدادي أصول الدين، ١٠.
Chapter Three: First Section - The Sense
"Make them hear and see on the day they come to Us, but the wrongdoers today are in clear error" [Maryam 19:38].
"Those are not causing failure [to Allah] in the earth, and they had no protectors besides Allah; the punishment will be multiplied for them; they were not able to hear, nor did they see" [Hud 11:20].
"And mention in the Book, Abraham. Indeed, he was a truthful prophet, when he said to his father, 'O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear and does not see and does not avail you anything?'" [Maryam 19:41-42].
There is no doubt that the highest levels of comprehension and acquisition are those in which the hearing and sight of the learner participate. Hence, it is necessary that the knowledge included in the content be supported by (audio-visual) techniques to achieve the highest level of comprehension and acquisition.
In light of this presentation of the verses of hearing and sight, it is appropriate to point out the following matters:
The first matter: Indeed, the Holy Quran's specification of the two tools of hearing and sight by mention, in this manner of repetition without others, is due to them being the pivot of animal life, the perfection of humanity, and the acquisition of primary sciences (1). And because the perception of the proofs of true belief is only through them (3). But this does not negate the existence of paramount importance for the remaining senses, because the specification of hearing and sight by mention indicates distinguished importance by particularity, nothing more. And it may be on the basis of mentioning the part for its importance while intending the whole in reality.
The second matter: Indeed, when hearing is mentioned in the Holy Quran as a source (sam') coupled with sight, it comes in the singular, while "sight" (al-basar) comes in the plural (absar) except in one place, which is the saying of Allah the Exalted: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned" [Al-Isra' 17:36]. Some commentators hold that He singled out hearing because it is a verbal noun (masdar), so it indicates the genus existing in all people's senses. As for the sights (absar), it was brought in the plural because it is a noun (ism), so it is not explicit in indicating generality (al-umum) due to the possibility of imagining a specific sight, so the plural was more indicative of the intended generality and more repelling of the possibility of specification and the like, contrary to His saying: "Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned" [Al-Isra' 17:36], because the intended is the single [sense] for each addressee by His saying: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge."
And it can be that this is a type of miracle (i'jaz), since the sense of hearing receives sounds emanating from all directions, whereas the eye only sees if a person directs his sight toward the thing he wants to see (3). On the other hand, if a sound occurs in a place where a group of people gather, they all will hear approximately the same sound, while each one of them looks toward the same thing from different angles (3).
The third matter: Indeed, the Holy Quran gives precedence to hearing over sight whenever they are paired together. Perhaps this is due to the strength of hearing such that it can perceive from the six directions, in light and darkness, while sight perceives only from the direction of facing, and by means of light and a ray. This is the saying of the Mu'tazila, but it is not free from dispute (4).
(1) Muhammad Rashid Rida, Tafsir al-Manar, 11/355. (2) Ibn 'Ashur, Tafsir al-Tahrir wa al-Tanwir, 13/232.
(3) Najati, the previous reference, 128.
(4) Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, Usul al-Din, 10.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion of the senses of hearing and sight as highlighted in the Quran. The author begins by quoting several Quranic verses that emphasize the importance of hearing and sight, particularly in the context of belief and knowledge. The author then asserts that the highest levels of comprehension involve both hearing and sight, and thus educational content should be supported by audio-visual techniques. The core of the passage is organized into three matters (أمور).

In the first matter, the author explains that the Quran's frequent mention of hearing and sight specifically, rather than other senses, is because they are the foundation of animal life, human perfection, and the acquisition of primary sciences. Additionally, true belief can only be attained through these two senses. However, the author clarifies that this does not diminish the importance of other senses; rather, hearing and sight are highlighted due to their particular significance, possibly as a synecdoche where the part stands for the whole.

In the second matter, the author observes a linguistic pattern: when hearing (سمع) and sight (بصر) are paired in the Quran, hearing is always in the singular form, while sight appears in the plural (أبصار), except in one verse (Surah al-Isra', 17:36) where both are singular. The author reports the view of some commentators that hearing is a verbal noun (مصدر) and thus naturally indicates the genus of hearing present in all people, so it remains singular. On the other hand, sight is a noun (اسم) and could be misunderstood as referring to a specific sight, so the plural is used to ensure generality. In the exceptional verse, the context addresses each individual separately, so the singular is appropriate. The author then suggests that this linguistic phenomenon is a type of miracle (إعجاز), because hearing perceives sounds from all directions simultaneously, and everyone present hears the same sound, whereas sight is directional and each person sees from a different angle.

In the third matter, the author notes that when hearing and sight are mentioned together, hearing always precedes sight. The reason proposed is that hearing is more powerful: it can perceive from all six directions, in light and darkness, while sight only works in one direction and requires light. This explanation is attributed to the Mu'tazila, but the author notes it is disputed.

Throughout the passage, the author uses Quranic verses and linguistic analysis to support the epistemological primacy of hearing and sight in acquiring knowledge and belief.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the main reason the Quran repeatedly mentions hearing and sight?
A) They are the only senses involved in knowledge acquisition.
B) They are the pivot of animal life, human perfection, and acquisition of primary sciences.
C) They are mentioned due to the Mu'tazila's influence.
D) All other senses are unimportant.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's repeated mention of hearing and sight is due to their foundational role in human perfection and the perception of divine truths, but other senses retain importance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find another Quranic verse that pairs hearing and sight (e.g., Al-Isra' 17:36 or Al-Mu'minun 23:78) and explain how it supports the author's argument about their role in knowledge.

The Linguistic Miracle: Singular Hearing, Plural Sight
Author examines the linguistic pattern of singular hearing and plural sight in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Quranic usage of singular 'sam' and plural 'absar' and explain its epistemological significance.

Core Idea
The singular form of 'hearing' indicates its universal character; the plural of 'sight' emphasizes individual perspectives.

In the second matter, the author observes a striking linguistic pattern: when paired, hearing is always singular while sight is mostly plural, with one exception. He then explores the grammatical and epistemological reasons behind this, linking it to the physical nature of the senses.

Guided Path
1
Observe the linguistic pattern
Find in the passage where the author notes that 'sam' (hearing) is always singular when paired with 'basar' (sight), while 'absar' (sights) is usually plural. Note the exceptional verse (Al-Isra' 17:36) where both are singular.
The pattern is consistent throughout the Quran.
2
Understand the grammatical distinction
The author cites commentators: 'sam' is a masdar (verbal noun) which naturally indicates the genus of hearing, so singular suffices. 'Basar' is an ism (noun) which could be interpreted as a specific instance, so the plural is used to ensure generality.
Masdar implies universality; ism requires plural for generality.
3
Analyze the epistemological implication
This linguistic choice reflects the nature of the senses: hearing receives sounds equally from all directions, so one hearing fits all; sight is directional and personal, so multiple perspectives are needed for general knowledge.
The author suggests this is a form of i'jaz (miracle).
4
Consider the exceptional verse
In Al-Isra' 17:36, both are singular because the context addresses each individual separately ('do not pursue what you have no knowledge of'), so the singular fits the personal command.
The exception proves the rule.

Chapter Three: First Section - The Sense
"Make them hear and see on the day they come to Us, but the wrongdoers today are in clear error" [Maryam 19:38].
"Those are not causing failure [to Allah] in the earth, and they had no protectors besides Allah; the punishment will be multiplied for them; they were not able to hear, nor did they see" [Hud 11:20].
"And mention in the Book, Abraham. Indeed, he was a truthful prophet, when he said to his father, 'O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear and does not see and does not avail you anything?'" [Maryam 19:41-42].
There is no doubt that the highest levels of comprehension and acquisition are those in which the hearing and sight of the learner participate. Hence, it is necessary that the knowledge included in the content be supported by (audio-visual) techniques to achieve the highest level of comprehension and acquisition.
In light of this presentation of the verses of hearing and sight, it is appropriate to point out the following matters:
The first matter: Indeed, the Holy Quran's specification of the two tools of hearing and sight by mention, in this manner of repetition without others, is due to them being the pivot of animal life, the perfection of humanity, and the acquisition of primary sciences (1). And because the perception of the proofs of true belief is only through them (3). But this does not negate the existence of paramount importance for the remaining senses, because the specification of hearing and sight by mention indicates distinguished importance by particularity, nothing more. And it may be on the basis of mentioning the part for its importance while intending the whole in reality.
The second matter: Indeed, when hearing is mentioned in the Holy Quran as a source (sam') coupled with sight, it comes in the singular, while "sight" (al-basar) comes in the plural (absar) except in one place, which is the saying of Allah the Exalted: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned" [Al-Isra' 17:36]. Some commentators hold that He singled out hearing because it is a verbal noun (masdar), so it indicates the genus existing in all people's senses. As for the sights (absar), it was brought in the plural because it is a noun (ism), so it is not explicit in indicating generality (al-umum) due to the possibility of imagining a specific sight, so the plural was more indicative of the intended generality and more repelling of the possibility of specification and the like, contrary to His saying: "Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned" [Al-Isra' 17:36], because the intended is the single [sense] for each addressee by His saying: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge."
And it can be that this is a type of miracle (i'jaz), since the sense of hearing receives sounds emanating from all directions, whereas the eye only sees if a person directs his sight toward the thing he wants to see (3). On the other hand, if a sound occurs in a place where a group of people gather, they all will hear approximately the same sound, while each one of them looks toward the same thing from different angles (3).
The third matter: Indeed, the Holy Quran gives precedence to hearing over sight whenever they are paired together. Perhaps this is due to the strength of hearing such that it can perceive from the six directions, in light and darkness, while sight perceives only from the direction of facing, and by means of light and a ray. This is the saying of the Mu'tazila, but it is not free from dispute (4).

(3) Najati, the previous reference, 128.
(4) Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, Usul al-Din, 10.

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion of the senses of hearing and sight as highlighted in the Quran. The author begins by quoting several Quranic verses that emphasize the importance of hearing and sight, particularly in the context of belief and knowledge. The author then asserts that the highest levels of comprehension involve both hearing and sight, and thus educational content should be supported by audio-visual techniques. The core of the passage is organized into three matters (أمور).

In the first matter, the author explains that the Quran's frequent mention of hearing and sight specifically, rather than other senses, is because they are the foundation of animal life, human perfection, and the acquisition of primary sciences. Additionally, true belief can only be attained through these two senses. However, the author clarifies that this does not diminish the importance of other senses; rather, hearing and sight are highlighted due to their particular significance, possibly as a synecdoche where the part stands for the whole.

In the second matter, the author observes a linguistic pattern: when hearing (سمع) and sight (بصر) are paired in the Quran, hearing is always in the singular form, while sight appears in the plural (أبصار), except in one verse (Surah al-Isra', 17:36) where both are singular. The author reports the view of some commentators that hearing is a verbal noun (مصدر) and thus naturally indicates the genus of hearing present in all people, so it remains singular. On the other hand, sight is a noun (اسم) and could be misunderstood as referring to a specific sight, so the plural is used to ensure generality. In the exceptional verse, the context addresses each individual separately, so the singular is appropriate. The author then suggests that this linguistic phenomenon is a type of miracle (إعجاز), because hearing perceives sounds from all directions simultaneously, and everyone present hears the same sound, whereas sight is directional and each person sees from a different angle.

In the third matter, the author notes that when hearing and sight are mentioned together, hearing always precedes sight. The reason proposed is that hearing is more powerful: it can perceive from all six directions, in light and darkness, while sight only works in one direction and requires light. This explanation is attributed to the Mu'tazila, but the author notes it is disputed.

Throughout the passage, the author uses Quranic verses and linguistic analysis to support the epistemological primacy of hearing and sight in acquiring knowledge and belief.

Why Hearing Precedes Sight in the Quran
Author discusses the Quranic precedence of hearing over sight and its justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reasons for the Quranic order of hearing before sight and assess the Mu'tazili explanation.

Core Idea
Hearing's superiority in range and conditions explains its priority over sight.

The third matter notes a consistent Quranic pattern: whenever hearing and sight are mentioned together, hearing comes first. The author proposes a reason based on the perceptual capabilities of hearing, attributing it to the Mu'tazila, but also notes that it is disputed.

Guided Path
1
Note the Quranic order
Observe that in every verse where hearing and sight are paired, hearing is mentioned first. This is a consistent stylistic feature.
For example, in Surah Maryam, Hud, and Al-Isra'.
2
Identify the proposed reason
The author reports that the Mu'tazila explain the precedence by hearing's greater strength: it can perceive from all six directions, in light and darkness, while sight only works from one direction and requires light.
This reason is cognitive-physical.
3
Consider the dispute
The author explicitly says 'this is the saying of the Mu'tazila, but it is not free from dispute.' So there are alternative views.
The author does not endorse a side.
4
Evaluate alternative explanations
Think of other possible reasons: hearing is the first sense to develop, it is essential for receiving revelation, or the Arabic linguistic structure itself might require this order.
Compare with the linguistic analysis of the second matter.
