الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
أسْمِعْ بِهِمْ وَأَبْصِرْ يَوْمَ يَأْتُونَنا لَكِنِ الظَّالِمُونَ الْيَوْمَ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِين [مريم: ۳۸/۱۹].
أُولَئِكَ لَمْ يَكُونُوا مُعْجِزِينَ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَمَا كَانَ لَهُمْ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ مِنْ أَوْلِياءَ يُضاعَفُ لَهُمُ الْعَذابُ ما كانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ وَمَا كَانُوا يُبْصِرُونَ [هود: ۲۰/۱۱]
وَاذْكُرْ فِي الْكِتابِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِنَّهُ كانَ صِدِّيقاً نَبِيّاً، إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ يَا أَبَتِ لِمَ تَعْبُدُ ما لا يَسْمَعُ وَلا يُبْصِرُ وَلا يُغْنِي عَنكَ شَيْئًا [مريم: ٤١/١٩-٤٢]. ولاشك أن أعلى درجات الاستيعاب والتحصيل تلك التي يشترك فيها سمع المتعلم وبصره، ومن هنا كان لزاماً أن ترفد المعارف التي يشملها المحتوى بتقنيات (سمع بصرية) ليتحقق أعلى مستوى من الاستيعاب والتحصيل. وفي ضوء هذا العرض لآيات السمع والبصر يجدر أن نشير إلى الأمور التالية: الأمر الأول: إن اختصاص القرآن الكريم أدائي السمع والأبصار بالذكر، على هذا النحو من التكرار دون غيرهما يعود إلى كونهما مدار الحياة الحيوانية، وكمال البشرية، وتحصيل العلوم الأولية (۱). ولكون إدراك دلائل الاعتقاد الحق لا يكون إلا بهما (۳). ولكن ذلك لا ينفي وجود أهمية قصوى لبقية الحواس، لأن اختصاص السمع والبصر بالذكر يعني الأهمية المتميزة بالخصوصية ليس أكثر. وقد يكون من باب ذكر الجزء لأهميته مع إرادة الكل في حقيقة الأمر.
الأمر الثاني: إن السمع حين ورد في القرآن الكريم بوصفه مصدر (سمع) مقروناً بالبصر؛ يرد مفرداً، في حين يرد (البصر) جمعاً (أبصار) إلا في موطن واحد وهو قول الله تعالى: وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً ﴾ [الإسراء: ٣٦/١٧]. هذا يرى بعض المفسرين أنه : أفرد السمع لأنه مصدر، فهو دال على وعن الجنس الموجود في جميع حواس الناس. وأما الأبصار فجيء به جمعاً لأنه اسم، فهو ليس نصاً في إفادة العموم لاحتمال توهم بصر مخصوص، فكان الجمع أدل على قصد العموم، وأنفى لاحتمال العهد ونحوه، بخلاف قوله: ﴿إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً) [الإسراء: ٣٦/١٧، لأن المراد الواحد لكل مخاطب بقوله: ﴿وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ ) .
ويمكن أن يكون ذلك ضرباً من ضروب الإعجاز، إذ إن حاسة السمع تستقبل الأصوات الصادرة من جميع الجهات في حين لا ترى العين إلا إذا اتجه الإنسان ببصره نحو الشيء الذي يريد أن يراه (۳ ). ومن ناحية أخرى فإنه إذا حدث صوت في مكان يجتمع فيه جمع من الناس فإنهم جميعاً سيسمعون الصوت ذاته تقريباً، بينما ينظر كل واحد منهـم صـوب الشيء الواحد من زوايا مختلفة (۳).
الأمر الثالث: إن القرآن الكريم يقدّم السمع على البصر كلما اقترنــا ببعضهما. ولعلّ ذلك يرجع إلى قوة السمع بحيث يستطيع الإدراك من الجهات الست، وفي الضوء والظلمة ولا يدرك البصر إلا من جهة المقابلة، وبواسطة من ضياء وشعاع. وهذا قول المعتزلة، ولكنه لا يسلم من نزاع(4).
(۱) محمد رشید رضا تفسير المنار، ٣٥٥/١١. (۲) ابن عاشور، تفسير التحرير والتنوير، ٢٣٢/١٣.
(۳) نجاتي، المرجع السابق، ۱۲۸.
(٤) أبو منصور البغدادي أصول الدين، ١٠.
Chapter Three: First Section - The Sense
"Make them hear and see on the day they come to Us, but the wrongdoers today are in clear error" [Maryam 19:38].
"Those are not causing failure [to Allah] in the earth, and they had no protectors besides Allah; the punishment will be multiplied for them; they were not able to hear, nor did they see" [Hud 11:20].
"And mention in the Book, Abraham. Indeed, he was a truthful prophet, when he said to his father, 'O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear and does not see and does not avail you anything?'" [Maryam 19:41-42].
There is no doubt that the highest levels of comprehension and acquisition are those in which the hearing and sight of the learner participate. Hence, it is necessary that the knowledge included in the content be supported by (audio-visual) techniques to achieve the highest level of comprehension and acquisition.
In light of this presentation of the verses of hearing and sight, it is appropriate to point out the following matters:
The first matter: Indeed, the Holy Quran's specification of the two tools of hearing and sight by mention, in this manner of repetition without others, is due to them being the pivot of animal life, the perfection of humanity, and the acquisition of primary sciences (1). And because the perception of the proofs of true belief is only through them (3). But this does not negate the existence of paramount importance for the remaining senses, because the specification of hearing and sight by mention indicates distinguished importance by particularity, nothing more. And it may be on the basis of mentioning the part for its importance while intending the whole in reality.
The second matter: Indeed, when hearing is mentioned in the Holy Quran as a source (sam') coupled with sight, it comes in the singular, while "sight" (al-basar) comes in the plural (absar) except in one place, which is the saying of Allah the Exalted: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned" [Al-Isra' 17:36]. Some commentators hold that He singled out hearing because it is a verbal noun (masdar), so it indicates the genus existing in all people's senses. As for the sights (absar), it was brought in the plural because it is a noun (ism), so it is not explicit in indicating generality (al-umum) due to the possibility of imagining a specific sight, so the plural was more indicative of the intended generality and more repelling of the possibility of specification and the like, contrary to His saying: "Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned" [Al-Isra' 17:36], because the intended is the single [sense] for each addressee by His saying: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge."
And it can be that this is a type of miracle (i'jaz), since the sense of hearing receives sounds emanating from all directions, whereas the eye only sees if a person directs his sight toward the thing he wants to see (3). On the other hand, if a sound occurs in a place where a group of people gather, they all will hear approximately the same sound, while each one of them looks toward the same thing from different angles (3).
The third matter: Indeed, the Holy Quran gives precedence to hearing over sight whenever they are paired together. Perhaps this is due to the strength of hearing such that it can perceive from the six directions, in light and darkness, while sight perceives only from the direction of facing, and by means of light and a ray. This is the saying of the Mu'tazila, but it is not free from dispute (4).
(1) Muhammad Rashid Rida, Tafsir al-Manar, 11/355. (2) Ibn 'Ashur, Tafsir al-Tahrir wa al-Tanwir, 13/232.
(3) Najati, the previous reference, 128.
(4) Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, Usul al-Din, 10.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion of the senses of hearing and sight as highlighted in the Quran. The author begins by quoting several Quranic verses that emphasize the importance of hearing and sight, particularly in the context of belief and knowledge. The author then asserts that the highest levels of comprehension involve both hearing and sight, and thus educational content should be supported by audio-visual techniques. The core of the passage is organized into three matters (أمور).

In the first matter, the author explains that the Quran's frequent mention of hearing and sight specifically, rather than other senses, is because they are the foundation of animal life, human perfection, and the acquisition of primary sciences. Additionally, true belief can only be attained through these two senses. However, the author clarifies that this does not diminish the importance of other senses; rather, hearing and sight are highlighted due to their particular significance, possibly as a synecdoche where the part stands for the whole.

In the second matter, the author observes a linguistic pattern: when hearing (سمع) and sight (بصر) are paired in the Quran, hearing is always in the singular form, while sight appears in the plural (أبصار), except in one verse (Surah al-Isra', 17:36) where both are singular. The author reports the view of some commentators that hearing is a verbal noun (مصدر) and thus naturally indicates the genus of hearing present in all people, so it remains singular. On the other hand, sight is a noun (اسم) and could be misunderstood as referring to a specific sight, so the plural is used to ensure generality. In the exceptional verse, the context addresses each individual separately, so the singular is appropriate. The author then suggests that this linguistic phenomenon is a type of miracle (إعجاز), because hearing perceives sounds from all directions simultaneously, and everyone present hears the same sound, whereas sight is directional and each person sees from a different angle.

In the third matter, the author notes that when hearing and sight are mentioned together, hearing always precedes sight. The reason proposed is that hearing is more powerful: it can perceive from all six directions, in light and darkness, while sight only works in one direction and requires light. This explanation is attributed to the Mu'tazila, but the author notes it is disputed.

Throughout the passage, the author uses Quranic verses and linguistic analysis to support the epistemological primacy of hearing and sight in acquiring knowledge and belief.

سمع
بصر
المعتزلة
قوة السمع

Key Takeaway
The Quran's consistent precedence of hearing over sight likely reflects hearing's broader perceptual capabilities, a point of debate among theological schools.

Epistemological Priority of Hearing over Sight
Reasons and rebuttals for prioritizing hearing over sight in epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and categorize the reasons for the epistemological superiority of hearing over sight, and reconcile apparent Quranic counterexamples with the main thesis.

Core Idea
Hearing is epistemologically superior to sight for its continuous, comprehensive, and argumentative role.

This passage from a modern Quranic epistemology work presents a sustained argument for the primacy of hearing over sight in knowledge acquisition. The author combines empirical observations, Quranic citations, physiological research, and logical reasoning to support this view. He also addresses verses that seem to prioritize sight, showing that context resolves the apparent conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching claim
Find the main thesis of the passage. The author asserts that hearing is epistemologically superior to sight and supports this with multiple reasons and a rebuttal of apparent counterexamples.
2
List the empirical and scriptural reasons
Look at the first four reasons from researchers: hearing enables language learning, is linked to intellect in Quran (Surah al-Mulk), operates immediately after birth, and works continuously even during sleep (Surah al-Kahf). Note the Quranic evidence for each.
The People of the Cave example illustrates continuous operation even during sleep.
3
Examine the cognitive arguments
Identify four additional reasons from a cognitive perspective: hearing is crucial for establishing arguments (hujja), transmitting accumulated knowledge, perceiving distant sounds, and functioning day and night. Compare these to the limitations of sight.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of counterexamples
The author addresses verses that mention sight before hearing (e.g., al-A'raf 179, al-Isra 97, al-Sajda 12). For each, he provides a contextual explanation that does not undermine the epistemic priority of hearing. Identify at least two such contexts (e.g., animal comparison, punishment in the afterlife).
This shows the importance of interpreting Quranic verses in their proper context.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويذهب بعض الباحثين إلى سرد أسباب أخرى يمكن تلخيصها على النحو التالي:
١ - السمع أهم من البصر في عملية الإدراك الحسي والتعلم وتحصيل العلوم، ونحن نلاحظ أن فاقد البصر يمكن أن يتعلم اللغة، وتحصيل العلوم بخلاف فاقد السمع فإن من المتعذر تعلمه اللغة وتحصيل العلوم.
٢ - لقد جاء ذكر السمع مع العقل في بعض الآيات كقوله تعالى: {وَقَالُوا لَوْ كُنَّا نَسْمَعُ أَوْ نَعْقِلُ مَا كُنَّا فِي أَصْحَابِ السَّعِيرِ} [الملك: 10/67] وغيرها مما يشير إلى العلاقة الوثيقة التي تربط السمع بالعقل.
٣ - دلّت الأبحاث الفيسيولوجية الحديثة أن الطفل الوليد يسمع الأصوات عقب الولادة مباشرة، بينما يحتاج إلى فترة من الزمن كي يستطيع أن يرى الأشياء بوضوح.
٤ - مُيّزت حاسة السمع بالعمل الدائم، دون توقف، بخلاف حاسة البصر، فإنها قد تتوقف عن أداء وظيفتها بمجرد إغماض العينين، أو النوم، ولهذا فإن الله تعالى ذكر في قصة أهل الكهف أنه ضرب على آذانهم، حين يستغرقون في النوم، فلا يوقظهم صوت: {فَضَرَبْنَا عَلَى آذَانِهِمْ فِي الْكَهْفِ سِنِينَ عَدَدًا} [الكهف: 11/18].
ومن زاوية معرفية خالصة عَدّ بعض الباحثين ذلك التقديم للسمع على البصر قائماً على الأفضلية المعرفية للسمع حيث إن:
١ - السمع أهم في إقامة الحجة على الناس أما البصر فمحدود أكثر من السمع الذي يتميز بالعمومية والشمولية والطول في المدى والزمان.
٢ - السمع أهم في توصيل نتائج العقول إلى غيره، عندما ينقل معارف السابقين، في حين أن البصر يقتصر على نقل المعارف الجديدة.
٣ - السمع يدرك الأصوات من مسافات فيُحصل معرفة يعجز البصر عن إدراكها، حتى مع تقدم العلم. ولذلك فإن الإنسان الأعمى السميع، يُحصل المعرفة أكثر من شخص أصم، يرى فقط دون أن يسمع.
٤ - تشتغل حاسة السمع ليلاً ونهاراً، في حين أن حاسة البصر لا يظهر عملها إلا في النهار والنور.
وعلى هذا الأساس فإن الاهتمام بحاسة السمع عند المتعلم في المرحلة قبل الأساسية على وجه التحديد - ينبغي أن يحتل مكانته في سلم أولويات علم النفس النمو والتعلم، كما أن مراعاة اختيار الوسائل السمعية مقدم على الاهتمام بالوسائل البصرية، وإن كان الجمع بينهما أبلغ تأثيراً كما سبقت الإشارة.
هذا ولا يقلل من أهمية السمع وتقديمه على البصر أن جاءت بضع آيات تفيد ظواهرها تقديم البصر على السمع، فذلك محمول إما على تشبيههم بالحيوانات التي يمثل البصر بالنسبة إليها حاسة أهم من السمع، لأنه لا يعدو أن يكون وسيلة لحفظ الحياة، ولا يؤدي دوراً معرفياً ينتج عنه الهدى، كما هو الحال بالنسبة إلى الإنسان. وقد جاءت الإشارة إلى ذلك في بعض الآيات، كما في آية الأعراف (179). وإما أن ذلك جاء في سياق النكاية بالكفار في تعذيبهم في الآخرة انظر آية الإسراء (97). أو ندمهم على أعمالهم الدنيوية في الآخرة، وذلك ليس موقفاً معرفياً للحواس، كما هو الحال في الدنيا (انظر آية السجدة: 12). أو في سياق الاستهزاء بآلهتهم المدعاة (انظر: الأعراف: 195). أو في سياق الذم لبني إسرائيل الذين كثر فيهم الأنبياء فكان الأنسب أن تكون الحجة عليهم بالبصر قبل السمع).
Some researchers go to list other reasons that can be summarized as follows:
1 - Hearing is more important than sight in the process of sensory perception, learning, and acquisition of knowledge. We observe that a person who loses sight can learn language and acquire knowledge, unlike a person who loses hearing, for it is impossible for him to learn language and acquire knowledge.
2 - Hearing has been mentioned alongside the intellect in some verses, such as His saying: {And they say, 'If only we had listened or used our intellect, we would not be among the companions of the Blaze'} [Al-Mulk: 10/67] and others, indicating the close relationship that connects hearing with the intellect.
3 - Modern physiological research has shown that a newborn infant hears sounds immediately after birth, while he needs a period of time to be able to see things clearly.
4 - The sense of hearing is distinguished by continuous operation, without stopping, unlike the sense of sight, which may stop performing its function simply by closing the eyes or sleeping. For this reason, Allah mentioned in the story of the People of the Cave that He struck their ears (caused them to sleep deeply) when they were sleeping, so that no sound would wake them: {So We struck their ears in the cave for a number of years} [Al-Kahf: 11/18].
From a purely cognitive perspective, some researchers considered this prioritization of hearing over sight to be based on the cognitive superiority of hearing, such that:
1 - Hearing is more important in establishing argument (hujja) against people, while sight is more limited than hearing, which is characterized by generality, comprehensiveness, and length in range and time.
2 - Hearing is more important in conveying the results of intellects to others when it transmits the knowledge of predecessors, while sight is limited to conveying new knowledge.
3 - Hearing perceives sounds from distances, thus acquiring knowledge that sight is unable to perceive, even with the advancement of science. Therefore, a blind person who can hear acquires more knowledge than a deaf person who sees only without hearing.
4 - The sense of hearing works night and day, while the sense of sight only shows its work in daylight and light.
On this basis, attention to the sense of hearing in the learner, especially in the pre-primary stage, should occupy its place in the priorities of developmental psychology and learning. Also, consideration of selecting auditory aids precedes attention to visual aids, although combining them is more effective in impact, as previously indicated.
This does not diminish the importance of hearing and its prioritization over sight if a few verses appear to prioritize sight over hearing. That is attributed either to likening them to animals for which sight is a more important sense than hearing, because it is nothing but a means of preserving life and does not play a cognitive role that results in guidance, as is the case for humans. This has been indicated in some verses, such as in al-A'raf (179). Or that came in the context of tormenting the disbelievers in their punishment in the Hereafter (see al-Isra: 97), or their regret for their worldly deeds in the Hereafter, and that is not a cognitive stance of the senses as is the case in this world (see al-Sajda: 12), or in the context of mocking their alleged gods (see al-A'raf: 195), or in the context of blame for the Children of Israel who had many prophets among them, so it was more appropriate that the argument against them be by sight before hearing).
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument for the superiority of the sense of hearing (al-sam‘) over the sense of sight (al-basar) in knowledge acquisition, drawing on both empirical evidence and Quranic references. The author first lists four reasons from researchers. The first reason is that hearing is more critical for learning language and sciences: a blind person can learn, but a deaf person cannot. The second connects hearing with intellect in the Quran (Surah al-Mulk). The third cites modern physiology: newborns hear immediately but see only later. The fourth notes that hearing operates continuously, even during sleep, as illustrated by the story of the People of the Cave whose ears were 'struck' to prevent awakening. Then, from a purely cognitive angle, the author presents four more reasons: hearing is better for establishing proofs (ḥujja) due to its comprehensiveness and temporal range; it transmits accumulated knowledge across generations; it perceives sounds from distances, surpassing sight; and it functions night and day. The author then concludes by rebutting apparent Quranic verses that prioritize sight, explaining them as specific contexts (like animalistic comparison, punishment, regret, mockery, or blame) that do not undermine the general epistemic priority of hearing. Throughout, the commentary should note that the author's stance is not merely empirical but rooted in a Quranic worldview.

Key Terms

البصر
الحجة
الإدراك الحسي

D) Hearing can perceive objects at a distance, while sight cannot.

Key Takeaway
Hearing is epistemologically superior to sight due to its continuous operation, role in transmitting knowledge, and ability to establish arguments, with Quranic counterexamples resolved through contextual interpretation.

Epistemic Priority of Hearing over Sight
Author argues for hearing's epistemic superiority with practical implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two epistemic advantages of hearing over sight as argued from a Quranic perspective.

Core Idea
Hearing surpasses sight in knowledge: it works continuously and perceives the unseen.

The author begins by asserting that hearing has two clear advantages over sight in acquiring knowledge. First, hearing can perceive sounds from distances, gaining information that sight cannot reach even with advanced science. Second, hearing functions night and day, while sight requires light. This leads to important implications for how we prioritize learning tools in education, especially for young children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two arguments
Read the passage and list the two reasons the author gives for hearing's superiority. One concerns distance, the other concerns time.
Look for the phrases 'يدرك الأصوات من مسافات' and 'تشتغل حاسة السمع ليلاً ونهاراً'.
2
Contrast with sight's limitations
Understand how sight is limited: it requires daylight and cannot perceive sounds or distant events. The author contrasts a blind person who hears with a deaf person who sees.
The example shows that hearing contributes more to knowledge than sight.
3
Derive pedagogical implications
Based on these advantages, the author recommends prioritizing auditory aids over visual ones in early education, though combining both is best.
This is a practical application of the epistemic argument.

Chapter Three: First Section - The Sense of Hearing
-3- Hearing perceives sounds from distances, thus acquiring knowledge that sight is incapable of perceiving, even with advanced science. Therefore, a blind person who hears acquires more knowledge than a deaf person who only sees without hearing.
-4- The sense of hearing functions night and day, while the sense of sight only shows its work in daytime and light (1).
On this basis, attention to the sense of hearing in the learner, especially at the pre-primary stage, should occupy its place in the hierarchy of priorities for developmental and educational psychology. Also, consideration of selecting auditory aids precedes attention to visual aids, although combining both is more effective, as previously indicated.
This does not diminish the importance of hearing and its priority over sight, even though a few verses appear to give priority to sight over hearing (). That is interpreted either as comparing them to animals for which sight represents a more important sense than hearing, because it is merely a means of preserving life and does not play an epistemic role that produces guidance, as is the case for humans. This has been indicated in some verses, as in al-A'raf 179. Or it came in the context of afflicting the disbelievers in their punishment in the Hereafter, see al-Isra' 97, or their regret over their worldly deeds in the Hereafter, which is not an epistemic stance of the senses as in this world (see al-Sajda 12). Or in the context of mocking their alleged deities (see al-A'raf 195). Or in the context of blaming the Children of Israel, among whom prophets were abundant, so it was more appropriate that the proof against them be by sight before hearing).
(1) Rajih al-Kurdi, previous reference, 353-354.
(2) See al-A'raf 179, 195; al-Ma'ida 71; Hud 124; al-Isra' 97; al-Sajda 12.
(3) al-Kurdi, previous reference, 556-557.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion drawn from a Quranic perspective on the senses. It begins by stating that hearing has epistemic advantages over sight: it can perceive sounds from distances and acquire knowledge that sight cannot, even with advanced science. The author uses the example of a blind person who can hear and thus learns more than a deaf person who only sees. Then it notes that hearing operates continuously (night and day) while sight requires light. From this, the author derives pedagogical implications: in early education, auditory aids should be prioritized over visual ones, though combining both is most effective. The author then addresses a potential objection: some Quranic verses seem to prioritize sight over hearing. The response offers multiple interpretations: (1) such verses refer to animals for whom sight is crucial for survival but not for knowledge and guidance; (2) they come in contexts of punishment, regret, mockery, or blame in the Hereafter, not in an epistemic context. Thus, the apparent prioritization of sight does not undermine the epistemic superiority of hearing in this world.

البصر
المعرفة الحسية

Key Takeaway
Hearing's continuous operation and ability to perceive distant sounds make it epistemically superior to sight.

Reconciling Quranic Verses on Sight and Hearing
Author reconciles apparent Quranic prioritization of sight with his thesis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's four interpretations of Quranic verses that seem to prioritize sight over hearing.

Core Idea
Quranic verses that put sight before hearing are context-specific, not about epistemic rank.

The author anticipates an objection: some Quranic verses appear to give priority to sight over hearing. However, these verses are not intended to establish a general epistemic hierarchy. Instead, they are explained by four distinct contexts: comparison with animals, punishment in the Hereafter, mockery of false deities, and blame of the Children of Israel. In each case, the context shows that sight is mentioned first for reasons other than epistemic superiority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Find the part of the passage where the author acknowledges that some verses seem to prioritize sight. Understand why this could be seen as a problem for the thesis that hearing is epistemically superior.
The author mentions that there are 'بضع آيات تفيد ظواهرها تقديم البصر على السمع'.
2
List the four interpretations
The author provides four different contexts in which these verses appear. List them: (1) comparing humans to animals, (2) punishment in the Hereafter, (3) mockery of deities, (4) blame of Israelites.
Each context removes the epistemic dimension, so the order does not reflect sensory priority.
3
Explain why each does not undermine hearing's superiority
For each interpretation, explain why the verse does not claim that sight is epistemically better. For example, the animal comparison shows that for survival, sight is more important, but for knowledge, hearing is key.
The key is that these verses are not about knowledge acquisition in this world.

Relativity of the Senses and Criteria for Certain Sensory Knowledge
Author explains that senses are relative and not absolute sources of certain knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three criteria for certain sensory knowledge and explain why senses are relative to reality, using examples from Ibn Hazm.

Core Idea
Sensory knowledge is certain only when it is recurrent, consistent, and non-contradictory to reason.

The Quran emphasises the senses as a source of knowledge, but they are not absolute. This passage from the author clarifies that sensory perceptions can be deceptive and must meet strict conditions to yield certainty. By studying these conditions, you learn how Islamic epistemology evaluates sensory evidence and distinguishes between certain knowledge and mere conjecture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the opening sentence: despite the Quran's emphasis, senses are not absolute. Note that the author sets up a contrast between the importance of senses and their relativity.
2
Extract the three conditions for certainty
Find the sentence that begins with 'that is because certain sensory knowledge...'. Identify the three requirements: recurrence (tawatur), agreement among senses, and non-contradiction with primary rational principles.
These conditions mirror the criteria for mutawatir reports in hadith and usul.
3
Analyse the sight example
The author gives an example: a sighted person sees only a small portion of reality, so his 'blindness' is greater than his sight. This illustrates that senses are relative and partial.
The proportion of what one cannot perceive is far larger than what one can.
4
Examine Ibn Hazm's examples
Ibn Hazm describes cases where a person mistakes identity by sight, smell, or taste, swears an oath, and later discovers error. These show that even strong sensory conviction can be wrong.
These examples demonstrate that without the three conditions, sensory knowledge can be false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نسبية الحواس
على الرغم من تلك الأهمية التي يوليها القرآن للحواس عند الإنسان، إلا أن ذلك لا يعني إطلاقية قدرات الحواس، بحيث تصبح مصدراً للمعرفة أو أداة لها على نحو يخلو من النزاع. ذلك أن المعرفة الحسية اليقينية هي التي تقدم شهادة الحس مؤكدة قاطعة عندما تتواتر شهادات الحس هذه، وتتفق مع الحواس الأخرى، ولا تتعارض مع أصول العقل وقوانينه الأولية كما سبقت الإشارة أما عندما تنزل عن هذا المستوى فإن قيمتها المعرفية تتراجع إلى ما دونها حتى آخر مرتبة الظن المرجوح (۱) . إن أحد الناس بصراً لا يتمكن من رؤية ما هو موجود إلا قدراً يسيراً بالنظر إلى ما لا يستطيع رؤيته. فهو يملك من البصر بمقدار ما يرى ولديه من العمى بمقدار ما لا يستطيع رؤيته، وعليه فإن نسبة العمى عند كل المبصرين أعظم بكثير من نسبة البصر الذي يملكونه، كما أن كل المبصرين من المخلوقين لديهم عمى نسبي بمقدار ما لا يستطيعون رؤيته من الأشياء. وهكذا النسبية في جميع الحواس(٢).
وهذا ابن حزم الأندلسي) (ت:٤٥٦هـ) يعرض للاضطراب الذي قد يحصل لمن تكافأت عنده الأدلة، فينقلب إلى ضدّ ما كان يعتقده من قبل، ليهلك في سبيل إبطال ما كان يعتقده من قبل فيقول .... وهذا يعرض فيما يدرك بالحواس كثيراً، فيرى الإنسان شخصاً من بعيد فيظنه فلاناً، ويحلف عليه ويكابر ويجرد، ثم يتبين له أنه ليس هو الذي ظن، وقد يشمّ الإنسان رائحة يظنها من بعض الروائح، ويقطع على ذلك ويحلف عليه ومجدّاً، ثم يتبين لـه أنـه ليـس هـو الذي ظنّ، وهكذا في الذوق أيضاً)(۳).
(۱) الميداني، ضوابط المعرفة، ١٣٤. (۲) الميداني، بصائر للمسلم المعاصر، ٥٩. (٣) ابن حزم، مرجع سابق، ٢٦٦/٥ – ٢٦٧.
Relativity of the Senses
Despite the importance that the Quran gives to the senses in humans, that does not mean absoluteness of the senses' capabilities, such that they become a source of knowledge or a tool for it in a way devoid of contention. That is because certain sensory knowledge is that which presents the testimony of sense as confirmed and decisive when these testimonies of sense are recurrent, agree with other senses, and do not contradict the principles of reason and its primary laws, as previously indicated. But when it descends below this level, its epistemic value declines below that, down to the lowest rank of weak conjecture (1). Indeed, one person with sight cannot see what exists except a small amount relative to what he cannot see. He possesses sight to the extent of what he sees, and he has blindness to the extent of what he cannot see. Therefore, the proportion of blindness among all sighted people is far greater than the proportion of sight they possess. Similarly, all sighted beings have relative blindness to the extent of what they cannot see of things. And thus relativity in all senses (2).
And Ibn Hazm al-Andalusi (d. 456 AH) discusses the confusion that may occur for one whose proofs are balanced, so he turns to the opposite of what he used to believe, perishing in the way of invalidating what he used to believe. He says: 'And this occurs frequently in what is perceived by the senses. A person sees a person from afar and thinks he is so-and-so, swears an oath about him, persists and is vehement, then it becomes clear to him that he is not who he thought. And a person may smell a scent and think it is some scent, and decides on that, swears an oath about it and is vehement, then it becomes clear to him that it is not what he thought. And similarly with taste as well' (3).
(1) al-Maidani, Dawabit al-Ma‘rifa, 134. (2) al-Maidani, Basa'ir li’l-Muslim al-Mu‘asir, 59. (3) Ibn Hazm, previous reference, 5/266-267.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage discusses the relativity of the senses. It begins by affirming that despite the Quran's emphasis on the senses, they are not absolute; sensory knowledge is certain only when the sense testimonies are recurrent (mutawatir), consistent with other senses, and do not contradict the primary principles of reason. Below that level, sensory knowledge declines to mere conjecture. The author then gives an example: each sighted person sees only a small fraction of what exists, so they have far more 'blindness' than sight; this relativity applies to all senses. To illustrate the fallibility of senses, the author quotes Ibn Hazm, who recounts how a person may mistake a distant person's identity, swear an oath, only to be proven wrong; similarly with smell and taste. These examples show that sensory perceptions can be mistaken, so they cannot be taken as certain without corroboration.

Key Terms
نسبية الحواس
المعرفة الحسية اليقينية
الظن المرجوح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does sensory knowledge achieve certainty?
A) When it is based on a single strong sense perception.
B) When sense testimonies are recurrent, agree with other senses, and do not contradict reason.
C) When it is accompanied by an oath.
D) When it comes from sight alone.

Key Takeaway
Sensory knowledge achieves certainty only when it is mutawatir, consistent across senses, and in harmony with reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the sensory report of the sighting of the crescent moon by a single person. Does it meet the conditions for certain sensory knowledge? Explain.
?
In hadith criticism, why is a mutawatir hadith considered certain while an ahad hadith is only probable? Use the three conditions from this lesson.

The Range and Variability of Sense Perception
Author argues that the five senses are limited and often deceive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two types of sensory limitations (range and variability) and explain how they undermine the certainty of sensory knowledge.

Core Idea
Senses are neither uniform nor stable; they vary across individuals and conditions.

We often rely on our senses as if they give us the whole truth. But the author points out that even the most careful researcher knows his senses are limited. Let us explore how the range and variability of senses challenge their reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of limitations
Look for the two examples: the dog hearing sounds beyond human range (range limitation), and the variation of perception due to fatigue or state (variability).
The dog example shows species-specific range; the fatigue example shows temporal variability.
2
Analyze the dog example
Why does the author mention a dog? To show that other creatures have sensory abilities we lack, implying our senses are not exhaustive.
3
Consider the implications for certainty
If senses vary and are limited, they cannot provide universal or constant truth. This weakens their status as a foundation for certain knowledge.
This is a classic epistemological move in Islamic thought.

ويشير بعض الباحثين إلى أن الباحث - أي باحث- يجتهد في تسجيل المعلومات التي يصل إليها من الحواس، ولكنه يدرك أن أعضاء الحس في الإنسان محدودة في مداها وفي قدرتها على التمييز . بل إنه لو كان لدى الباحث كلب فإن لدى هذا الكلب من القدرة الحسية ما يؤهله لسماع نغمات صفارة لا يسمعها الباحث وزملاء الباحث قد يستطيعون السماع لمدى أكبر مما يستطيعه هو. ليس ذلك فحسب، بل إن إدراكه الحسي يختلف وفقاً للأحوال التي يمرّ بها. أي إنّ الصوت أو الطعم أو الرائحة يختلف من وقت لآخر تبعاً لحواسه التي هي عرضة للتعب أو الكيف.
وإذا كان ذلك في السمع فإن أمر البصر كذلك محدود. فمما ثبت بالتجربة النفسية أنه تم عرض رسم تخطيطي لوجه رجل لا يعبر عن شيء على شاشة أمام عشرين شخصاً. وبعد أن شاهدوا كلمة (سعيد) تعرض على فترات متفاوتة تحت الصور، ظنوا أن وجه الرجل أصبح تدريجياً أكثر سعادة على الرغم من أنه لم يتغير. وهكذا فإننا عرضة للخداع البصري مما يقودنا إلى استنتاجات خاطئة عن طريق الوهم والخداع في أكثر من موقف. وما يزال المثال التقليدي حول العصا عندما تبدو في الماء منحنية في حين أنها مستقيمة عند لمسها من أكثر الاستشهادات حضوراً على خداع الحواس.
إن الحواس الخمس لا تستطيع الإحاطة بكل شيء، ولو قدر لأي من الناس امتلاك غير هذه الحاسة فلربما اكتشف أشياء كثيرة مغيبة عنا الآن، لكننا لا نحس بها حيث ليس لدينا الحاسة الخاصة بإدراكها واكتشافها.
إن مقياس أو مقاييس درجة الحرارة أو الضغط الجوي أو مقادير الكثافة تشهد بأن ثمة نقصاً كبيراً في حواسنا. ولو قدر لأي منا القدرة على الإحساس بهذه الظواهر لكانت حواسنا أوسع مما عليه الحال الآن. وقد اكتشف العلم الحديث أن الفضاء مملوء بالصور التي لا نستطيع مشاهدتها بالنظر المجرد، لعدم وجود قدر من الانسجام والتوافق بين وضعها ووضع أبصارنا، والأصوات التي تعلو مستوى سمعنا أو دونه لا نسمع منها شيئاً. وثمة أجهزة توصل إليها العلم الحديث باتت قادرة على اكتشاف والتقاط الأصوات والصور من الجو لنقلها إلينا بعد تحويلها إلى صور وأصوات تتناسب مع مستوى وضع أسماعنا وأبصارنا. ويذهب أحد الباحثين إلى أن ما تقوم به الحواس إنما هو خلق المحسوسات أو نقلها إلينا من العالم الخارجي، ولكن دون معيار لدينا يتيح لنا التمييز بين ما تنقله وما تخلقه وبين الوجود الخارجي وصنع الخيال والوهم. ومثال ذلك قراءة مثل هذه الكلمات، فهل هذه القراءة تمثل حقيقة واقعية بعيدة عن الخيال أو الوهم؟ قد يجاب بأن قراءتي لها ليس من قبيل خداع الحواس، فأنا أرى بعيني الكلمات والكتاب وأمسكه بيدي. وحين السؤال عن البرهان على حقيقة ذلك سيكون الجواب هو الجواب السابق نفسه من حيث الرؤية واللمس للكتاب، ولكن ذلك لا يعني أن برهاناً قائماً على صدق الحواس. أو لا يمكن أن يكون ذلك مجرد رؤية وإمساك نائم يحلم، ومن ثم فلا يعدو ذلك الخيال، فلا وجود لها في الواقع. وقد يقال إن نفي حالة النوم هذه يتم عن طريق الإحساس بعدم النوم فالحركة والإشارة والغضب لكلام الكاتب يدل على أن ذلك حقيقة لا مراء فيها. ولكن قد يحدث أن المرء يحلم أنه يقظان يفعل كذا وكذا فيغضب ويناقش. وقد يحدث أن المرء أيضاً يسأل نفسه في الحلم هل هذا حلم أم حقيقة؟ فتكون الإجابة بأنها حقيقة وليس حلماً، ثم يحدث الاستيقاظ من النوم. إذن فجميع الأحلام التي يمر بها الإنسان تشعره بأنه مستيقظ متنبه الجميع حركاته. أي إن تمييز الأحلام لا يتم إلا بعد الاستيقاظ، وعليه فلماذا لا أشك في أني أحلم أني أقرأ وأكتب كتاباً الآن؟!
Some researchers indicate that the researcher—any researcher—strives to record information that he obtains from the senses, but he realizes that the sense organs in humans are limited in their range and in their ability to discriminate. Indeed, if the researcher had a dog, that dog would possess sensory ability enabling it to hear whistle tones that the researcher does not hear, and the researcher's colleagues might be able to hear over a greater range than he can. Not only that, but his sensory perception varies according to the conditions he experiences. That is, sound, taste, or smell differs from time to time depending on his senses, which are subject to fatigue or state. And if that is the case with hearing, then the matter of sight is also limited. For it has been established by psychological experiment that a schematic drawing of a man's face expressing nothing was shown on a screen to twenty people. After they saw the word 'happy' displayed at varying intervals under the images, they thought that the man's face gradually became happier despite the fact that it had not changed. Thus we are subject to visual deception, leading us to false conclusions through illusion and deception in more than one situation. The traditional example of the stick that appears bent in water while it is straight when touched remains one of the most cited instances of sensory deception. The five senses cannot encompass everything, and if any person were to possess another sense, perhaps he would discover many things hidden from us now, but we do not sense them because we do not have the specific sense for perceiving and discovering them. The measure or measures of temperature, atmospheric pressure, or density values testify that there is a great deficiency in our senses. If any of us were able to sense these phenomena, our senses would be broader than they are now. Modern science has discovered that space is filled with images that we cannot see by naked observation, due to a lack of harmony and congruence between their state and the state of our eyesight, and sounds that are above or below our hearing level we hear nothing of them. And there are devices arrived at by modern science that have become capable of discovering and capturing sounds and images from the air to transmit them to us after converting them into images and sounds that suit the level of our hearing and sight. One researcher argues that what the senses do is either create the sensed objects or transmit them to us from the external world, but without a criterion on our part that allows us to distinguish between what they transmit and what they create, and between external existence and the product of imagination and illusion. An example is reading words like these: does this reading represent a real reality far from imagination or illusion? It may be answered that my reading of them is not a case of sensory deception, for I see the words and the book with my eyes and hold it with my hand. When asked for the proof of its reality, the answer will be the same previous answer in terms of seeing and touching the book, but that does not mean that there is a proof based on the veracity of the senses. Or could it not be merely seeing and grasping by a sleeping person dreaming, and thus it is nothing but imagination, having no existence in reality. It might be said that the negation of this sleeping state is achieved by the feeling of being awake—movement, pointing, and anger at the writer's words indicate that it is reality without doubt. But it may happen that a person dreams that he is awake, doing such and such, and he becomes angry and argues. It may also happen that a person asks himself in the dream: Is this a dream or reality? The answer is that it is reality and not a dream, then he wakes up from sleep. Thus all the dreams that a person experiences make him feel that he is awake, alert, and in control of all his movements. That is, distinguishing dreams only occurs after waking up, and therefore why should I not doubt that I am dreaming that I am reading and writing a book now?!
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological critique of the reliability of sense perception as a source of certain knowledge. The author begins by noting that even researchers, who strive to record sensory information, are aware of the limitations of human sense organs. He uses the example of a dog hearing sounds beyond human range, and variations in perception due to fatigue or state, to show that senses are not uniform or stable. The discussion then moves to visual deception, citing a psychological experiment where a neutral face was perceived as happier after seeing the word 'happy', and the classic example of a stick appearing bent in water. The author argues that the five senses cannot perceive everything; other creatures may sense what we cannot, and scientific instruments reveal phenomena like temperature and pressure that our senses miss. Modern science discovers images and sounds beyond our natural range, which devices convert for us. The most profound critique comes from a researcher who suggests that senses either create or transmit sensations, but we lack a criterion to distinguish between external reality and the constructs of imagination and illusion. The author then raises the dream argument: even when we think we are awake and using senses, we could be dreaming. The common response that movement, emotion, etc. prove wakefulness is unreliable because one can dream of all these. Therefore, since dreams can be indistinguishable from waking life, one cannot be certain that the present experience is not a dream. This undermines sense perception as a foundation for certainty.

Key Terms
الحواس
الوهم
الخيال
الحلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the example of the dog show that human senses are limited?
A) Dogs have better eyesight than humans.
B) Dogs can hear sounds that humans cannot, indicating our auditory range is limited.
C) Dogs can see in the dark, unlike humans.
D) Dogs have more sensory organs than humans.

Key Takeaway
Senses vary in range and stability; this variability undermines their claim to provide certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In Fiqh, the sighting of the moon for Ramadan is sensory evidence. How does the range and variability of vision affect the reliability of a single witness's testimony? Discuss using the concepts from this lesson.
?
Consider the hadith about the sun and moon being signs of Allah. If our senses can be deceived about basic phenomena (like the size of celestial bodies), how does that affect our approach to such signs?

Visual Deception and the Illusion of Perception
Author argues that the five senses are limited and often deceive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how contextual cues (like the word 'happy') can distort visual perception and explain the epistemological significance of the bent stick illusion.

Core Idea
Visual perception is easily manipulated; what we 'see' is not always what is.

The author presents two compelling examples of visual deception: a psychological experiment where a neutral face appears happier after seeing the word 'happy', and the classic bent stick in water. These show that our eyes can lead us to false conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Examine the face experiment
Read the description: a neutral face was shown, and participants who saw the word 'happy' perceived the face as becoming happier. Identify the influence of expectation on perception.
This shows that sensory input is not raw; it is shaped by context and prior knowledge.
2
Analyze the bent stick example
The stick appears bent in water but is straight when touched. This is a classic illusion. Why does it happen? Due to refraction of light.
The conflict between sight and touch raises the question: which sense is more reliable?
3
Extract the epistemological lesson
These examples demonstrate that sense perception can be systematically deceived. Therefore, we cannot accept sensory reports without cross-checking.
This leads to the conclusion that senses alone are not a sufficient basis for certain knowledge.

What does the face experiment demonstrate about sensory perception?

The Dream Argument and the Question of Certainty
Author argues that the five senses are limited and often deceive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the dream argument as a challenge to sensory certainty and assess its force in undermining sense-based knowledge.

Core Idea
If dreams can perfectly mimic waking life, then sense perception cannot guarantee that we are not dreaming.

The author pushes the critique further: even when we feel certain we are awake, we could be dreaming. The dream argument is a powerful tool to show that sense perception cannot be the ultimate foundation for certainty.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dream argument
The author asks: how do we know we are not dreaming now? The usual responses (feeling awake, moving, etc.) are unreliable because we can dream all those things.
This is similar to Descartes' dreaming argument, but rooted in an Islamic context.
2
Analyze the attempted refutation
The imagined objector says: 'We can disprove dreaming by noticing we are moving and reacting.' The author shows that we dream of moving and reacting.
The refutation fails because it assumes what it tries to prove.
3
Draw the epistemological conclusion
Since we cannot distinguish waking from dreaming during the experience, we cannot be certain that our current sense experiences are real. This casts doubt on sense perception as a source of certainty.
This leads to the need for a more certain criterion, such as rational intuition or revelation.

ويشير بعض الباحثين إلى أن الباحث - أي باحث- يجتهد في تسجيل المعلومات التي يصل إليها من الحواس، ولكنه يدرك أن أعضاء الحس في الإنسان محدودة في مداها وفي قدرتها على التمييز . بل إنه لو كان لدى الباحث كلب فإن لدى هذا الكلب من القدرة الحسية ما يؤهله لسماع نغمات صفارة لا يسمعها الباحث وزملاء الباحث قد يستطيعون السماع لمدى أكبر مما يستطيعه هو. ليس ذلك فحسب، بل إن إدراكه الحسي يختلف وفقاً للأحوال التي يمرّ بها. أي إنّ الصوت أو الطعم أو الرائحة يختلف من وقت لآخر تبعاً لحواسه التي هي عرضة للتعب أو الكيف.
وإذا كان ذلك في السمع فإن أمر البصر كذلك محدود. فمما ثبت بالتجربة النفسية أنه تم عرض رسم تخطيطي لوجه رجل لا يعبر عن شيء على شاشة أمام عشرين شخصاً. وبعد أن شاهدوا كلمة (سعيد) تعرض على فترات متفاوتة تحت الصور، ظنوا أن وجه الرجل أصبح تدريجياً أكثر سعادة على الرغم من أنه لم يتغير. وهكذا فإننا عرضة للخداع البصري مما يقودنا إلى استنتاجات خاطئة عن طريق الوهم والخداع في أكثر من موقف. وما يزال المثال التقليدي حول العصا عندما تبدو في الماء منحنية في حين أنها مستقيمة عند لمسها من أكثر الاستشهادات حضوراً على خداع الحواس.
إن الحواس الخمس لا تستطيع الإحاطة بكل شيء، ولو قدر لأي من الناس امتلاك غير هذه الحاسة فلربما اكتشف أشياء كثيرة مغيبة عنا الآن، لكننا لا نحس بها حيث ليس لدينا الحاسة الخاصة بإدراكها واكتشافها.
إن مقياس أو مقاييس درجة الحرارة أو الضغط الجوي أو مقادير الكثافة تشهد بأن ثمة نقصاً كبيراً في حواسنا. ولو قدر لأي منا القدرة على الإحساس بهذه الظواهر لكانت حواسنا أوسع مما عليه الحال الآن. وقد اكتشف العلم الحديث أن الفضاء مملوء بالصور التي لا نستطيع مشاهدتها بالنظر المجرد، لعدم وجود قدر من الانسجام والتوافق بين وضعها ووضع أبصارنا، والأصوات التي تعلو مستوى سمعنا أو دونه لا نسمع منها شيئاً. وثمة أجهزة توصل إليها العلم الحديث باتت قادرة على اكتشاف والتقاط الأصوات والصور من الجو لنقلها إلينا بعد تحويلها إلى صور وأصوات تتناسب مع مستوى وضع أسماعنا وأبصارنا. ويذهب أحد الباحثين إلى أن ما تقوم به الحواس إنما هو خلق المحسوسات أو نقلها إلينا من العالم الخارجي، ولكن دون معيار لدينا يتيح لنا التمييز بين ما تنقله وما تخلقه وبين الوجود الخارجي وصنع الخيال والوهم. ومثال ذلك قراءة مثل هذه الكلمات، فهل هذه القراءة تمثل حقيقة واقعية بعيدة عن الخيال أو الوهم؟ قد يجاب بأن قراءتي لها ليس من قبيل خداع الحواس، فأنا أرى بعيني الكلمات والكتاب وأمسكه بيدي. وحين السؤال عن البرهان على حقيقة ذلك سيكون الجواب هو الجواب السابق نفسه من حيث الرؤية واللمس للكتاب، ولكن ذلك لا يعني أن برهاناً قائماً على صدق الحواس. أو لا يمكن أن يكون ذلك مجرد رؤية وإمساك نائم يحلم، ومن ثم فلا يعدو ذلك الخيال، فلا وجود لها في الواقع. وقد يقال إن نفي حالة النوم هذه يتم عن طريق الإحساس بعدم النوم فالحركة والإشارة والغضب لكلام الكاتب يدل على أن ذلك حقيقة لا مراء فيها. ولكن قد يحدث أن المرء يحلم أنه يقظان يفعل كذا وكذا فيغضب ويناقش. وقد يحدث أن المرء أيضاً يسأل نفسه في الحلم هل هذا حلم أم حقيقة؟ فتكون الإجابة بأنها حقيقة وليس حلماً، ثم يحدث الاستيقاظ من النوم. إذن فجميع الأحلام التي يمر بها الإنسان تشعره بأنه مستيقظ متنبه الجميع حركاته. أي إن تمييز الأحلام لا يتم إلا بعد الاستيقاظ، وعليه فلماذا لا أشك في أني أحلم أني أقرأ وأكتب كتاباً الآن؟!
Some researchers indicate that the researcher—any researcher—strives to record information that he obtains from the senses, but he realizes that the sense organs in humans are limited in their range and in their ability to discriminate. Indeed, if the researcher had a dog, that dog would possess sensory ability enabling it to hear whistle tones that the researcher does not hear, and the researcher's colleagues might be able to hear over a greater range than he can. Not only that, but his sensory perception varies according to the conditions he experiences. That is, sound, taste, or smell differs from time to time depending on his senses, which are subject to fatigue or state. And if that is the case with hearing, then the matter of sight is also limited. For it has been established by psychological experiment that a schematic drawing of a man's face expressing nothing was shown on a screen to twenty people. After they saw the word 'happy' displayed at varying intervals under the images, they thought that the man's face gradually became happier despite the fact that it had not changed. Thus we are subject to visual deception, leading us to false conclusions through illusion and deception in more than one situation. The traditional example of the stick that appears bent in water while it is straight when touched remains one of the most cited instances of sensory deception. The five senses cannot encompass everything, and if any person were to possess another sense, perhaps he would discover many things hidden from us now, but we do not sense them because we do not have the specific sense for perceiving and discovering them. The measure or measures of temperature, atmospheric pressure, or density values testify that there is a great deficiency in our senses. If any of us were able to sense these phenomena, our senses would be broader than they are now. Modern science has discovered that space is filled with images that we cannot see by naked observation, due to a lack of harmony and congruence between their state and the state of our eyesight, and sounds that are above or below our hearing level we hear nothing of them. And there are devices arrived at by modern science that have become capable of discovering and capturing sounds and images from the air to transmit them to us after converting them into images and sounds that suit the level of our hearing and sight. One researcher argues that what the senses do is either create the sensed objects or transmit them to us from the external world, but without a criterion on our part that allows us to distinguish between what they transmit and what they create, and between external existence and the product of imagination and illusion. An example is reading words like these: does this reading represent a real reality far from imagination or illusion? It may be answered that my reading of them is not a case of sensory deception, for I see the words and the book with my eyes and hold it with my hand. When asked for the proof of its reality, the answer will be the same previous answer in terms of seeing and touching the book, but that does not mean that there is a proof based on the veracity of the senses. Or could it not be merely seeing and grasping by a sleeping person dreaming, and thus it is nothing but imagination, having no existence in reality. It might be said that the negation of this sleeping state is achieved by the feeling of being awake—movement, pointing, and anger at the writer's words indicate that it is reality without doubt. But it may happen that a person dreams that he is awake, doing such and such, and he becomes angry and argues. It may also happen that a person asks himself in the dream: Is this a dream or reality? The answer is that it is reality and not a dream, then he wakes up from sleep. Thus all the dreams that a person experiences make him feel that he is awake, alert, and in control of all his movements. That is, distinguishing dreams only occurs after waking up, and therefore why should I not doubt that I am dreaming that I am reading and writing a book now?!
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological critique of the reliability of sense perception as a source of certain knowledge. The author begins by noting that even researchers, who strive to record sensory information, are aware of the limitations of human sense organs. He uses the example of a dog hearing sounds beyond human range, and variations in perception due to fatigue or state, to show that senses are not uniform or stable. The discussion then moves to visual deception, citing a psychological experiment where a neutral face was perceived as happier after seeing the word 'happy', and the classic example of a stick appearing bent in water. The author argues that the five senses cannot perceive everything; other creatures may sense what we cannot, and scientific instruments reveal phenomena like temperature and pressure that our senses miss. Modern science discovers images and sounds beyond our natural range, which devices convert for us. The most profound critique comes from a researcher who suggests that senses either create or transmit sensations, but we lack a criterion to distinguish between external reality and the constructs of imagination and illusion. The author then raises the dream argument: even when we think we are awake and using senses, we could be dreaming. The common response that movement, emotion, etc. prove wakefulness is unreliable because one can dream of all these. Therefore, since dreams can be indistinguishable from waking life, one cannot be certain that the present experience is not a dream. This undermines sense perception as a foundation for certainty.

Key Terms
الحلم
الوهم
الخيال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main challenge the dream argument poses to sense perception?
A) It shows that dreams are always false.
B) It shows that we cannot distinguish dreaming from waking during the experience, so we cannot be certain our senses are reliable.
C) It proves that we cannot use our senses at all.
D) It shows that only awake people can think clearly.

Key Takeaway
The dream argument demonstrates that sense perception cannot provide absolute certainty, necessitating a more secure foundation for knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a kalam debate, a skeptic uses the dream argument to deny that we can be certain of anything sensed. How would a mutakallim respond? Use the text to construct a possible response.

Write a short dialogue between a student and a teacher where the teacher tries to refute the dream argument using the idea that Allah removes doubt when one is truly awake. Evaluate whether this refutation succeeds.

Limitations of Sense Perception: The Dream Argument and Quranic Critique
Author critiques sense perception using dream argument and Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the dream argument against sense certainty and explain how desire-based bias and Quranic verses further undermine sensory reliance.

Core Idea
Sense perception cannot guarantee certainty because dreams are indistinguishable from waking, and desires distort what we perceive.

This passage challenges the reliability of sense perception as a foundation for certain knowledge. The author presents three interlocking critiques: the physical limits of the senses, the dream argument that blurs waking and dreaming, and the psychological bias that skews perception. Each critique is supported by modern empirical findings and Quranic verses. Understanding this critique is essential for any serious engagement with Islamic epistemology, as it clears the ground for revelation and reason as superior sources of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three critiques
Find in the passage the three distinct reasons the author gives for distrusting the senses: (a) sensory range is limited, (b) we cannot distinguish between waking and dreaming, (c) desires and values distort perception.
2
Analyze the dream argument
Trace the logic: the author gives an example (reading a book). He shows that a dream could feel exactly the same. Even the feeling of being awake can be part of the dream. Therefore, we cannot be certain we are not dreaming now. Identify the structure: it's a skeptical hypothesis.
The argument does not claim we are dreaming, only that we cannot be sure we are not.
3
Connect to Quranic evidence
Read the cited verses. They show that disbelievers have eyes but do not see, ears but do not hear. The author argues this is due to their whims. Note that the Quran attributes sensory failure to spiritual causes, not physical.
This reinforces the point that perception is influenced by inner states.
4
Assess the overall conclusion
The passage does not completely deny sense perception, but argues it is insufficient for certainty. The conclusion: senses require rational and revelatory guidance.
The author uses the Quran as the ultimate corrective.

الحديث أن الفضاء مملوء بالصور التي لا نستطيع مشاهدتها بالنظر المجرد، لعدم وجود قدر من الانسجام والتوافق بين وضعها ووضع أبصارنا، والأصوات التي تعلو مستوى سمعنا أو دونه لا نسمع منها شيئاً. وثمة أجهزة توصل إليها العلم الحديث باتت قادرة على اكتشاف والتقاط الأصوات والصور من الجو لنقلها إلينا بعد تحويلها إلى صور وأصوات تتناسب مع مستوى وضع أسماعنا وأبصارنا (۱). ويذهب أحد الباحثين إلى أن ما تقوم به الحواس إنما هو خلق المحسوسات أو نقلها إلينا من العالم الخارجي، ولكن دون معيار لدينا يتيح لنا التمييز بين مــا تنقله وما تخلقه وبين الوجود الخارجي وصنع الخيال والوهم. ومثال ذلك قراءة مثل هذه الكلمات، فهل هذه القراءة تمثل حقيقة واقعية بعيدة عن الخيال أو الوهم؟ قد يجاب بأن قراءتي لها ليس من قبيل خداع الحواس، فأنا أرى بعيني الكلمات والكتاب وأمسكه بيدي. وحين السؤال عن البرهان على حقيقة ذلك سيكون الجواب هو الجواب السابق نفسه من حيث الرؤية واللمس للكتاب، ولكن ذلك لا يعني أن برهاناً قائماً على صدق الحواس. أو لا يمكن أن يكون ذلك مجرد رؤية وإمساك نائم يحلم، ومن ثم فلا يعدو ذلك الخيال، فلا وجود لها في الواقع. وقد يقال إن نفي حالة النوم هذه يتم عن طريق الإحساس بعدم النوم فالحركة والإشارة والغضب لكلام الكاتب يدل على أن ذلك حقيقة لا مراء فيها. ولكن قد يحدث أن المرء يحلم أنه يقظان يفعل كذا وكذا فيغضب ويناقش. وقد يحدث أن المرء أيضاً يسأل نفسه في الحلم هل هذا حلم أم حقيقة؟ فتكون الإجابة بأنها حقيقة وليس حلماً، ثم يحدث الاستيقاظ من النوم. إذن فجميع الأحلام التي يمر بها الإنسان تشعره بأنه مستيقظ متنبه الجميع حركاته. أي إن تمييز الأحلام لا يتم إلا بعد الاستيقاظ، وعليه فلماذا لا أشك في أني أحلم أني أقرأ وأكتب كتاباً الآن؟! (۲).

وإذا كانت الحواس محدودة من حيث طبيعتها التي خلقت عليها فإن دوافع الفرد وقيمه ذات تأثير في انتباهه وإدراكه الحسي. وهذا ما توصلت إليه نتائج الدراسات التجريبية الحديثة في مجال التحليل النفسي، حيث أوضحت أن الإنسان يميل إلى عدم إدراك الأشياء التي تزعجه وتقلقه والمتعارضة مع أهوائه ورغباته. وذلك ما يشير إليه القرآن عندما يعرض لحال الكافرين الذين لم يستفيدوا من حواسهم وعقولهم نتيجة الدوافع والقيم والأهواء التي تملكنهم:
وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيراً مِنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنْسِ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌ لا يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا أُولَئِكَ كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْغَافِلُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۹/۷].
... قُلْ هُوَ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا هُدَى وَشِفَاءٌ وَالَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ فِي آذَانِهِمْ وَقَرٌ
وَهُوَ عَلَيْهِمْ عَمَى أُولَئِكَ يُنادَوْنَ مِنْ مَكان بَعِيد [فصلت: ٤٤/٤١]. أُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ لَعَنَهُمُ اللهُ فَأَصَمَّهُمْ وَأَعْمَى أَبْصَارَهُمْ [عمد: ٢٣/٤٧]. أفَأَنتَ تُسْمِعُ الصُّمَّ أَوْ تَهْدِي الْعُمْيَ وَمَنْ كَانَ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِينٍ (الزخرف: ١٤٠/٤٣). عمى نسبياً
وإذا كان هناك عمى حسي ناتج عن الخلقة ابتداءً فإن هناك طارئاً يولّده الهوى أو الحب، ولذلك فإن العاشق أو صاحب الهوى محجوب أشياء كثيرة لا يراها في حين يراها غيره إذ هو مصاب بعمى جزئي طارئ بسبب عشقه أو هواه، فلا يرى إلا البعد الذي يزيده هوى أو عشقاً. ولذلك جاء في قوم نوح عن
The discussion [says] that space is filled with images that we cannot see with bare sight, due to the lack of a degree of harmony and compatibility between their position and the position of our eyes, and sounds that rise above or below the level of our hearing we hear nothing of them. And there are devices that modern science has reached that are able to discover and capture sounds and images from the air to transmit them to us after converting them into images and sounds that match the level of our hearing and sight (1). And one researcher thinks that what the senses do is either create the perceived objects or transmit them to us from the external world, but without a criterion for us that allows us to distinguish between what they transmit and what they create, and between external existence and the product of imagination and illusion. An example of that is reading such words: does this reading represent a real truth far from imagination or illusion? It might be answered that my reading of it is not a kind of deception of the senses, for I see with my eyes the words and the book and I hold it with my hand. And when asked for the proof of the reality of that, the answer will be the same previous answer in terms of seeing and touching the book, but that does not mean that a proof exists based on the truthfulness of the senses. Or it could be that it is merely the seeing and holding of a sleeping person dreaming, and then it is nothing but imagination, so it has no existence in reality. And it might be said that the negation of this sleep state occurs through the sensation of not sleeping, for movement, gesture, and anger at the writer's words indicate that that is a truth without doubt. But it may happen that a person dreams that he is awake doing such-and-such, so he gets angry and argues. And it may also happen that a person asks himself in the dream: is this a dream or reality? Then the answer is that it is reality and not a dream, then he wakes up from sleep. So all the dreams that a person goes through make him feel that he is awake, alert, [with] all his movements. That is, distinguishing dreams only occurs after waking up, and therefore why should I not doubt that I am dreaming that I am reading and writing a book now?! (2).

And if the senses are limited in terms of their nature on which they were created, then the motives and values of the individual have an effect on his attention and sensory perception. This is what the results of modern experimental studies in the field of psychoanalysis have reached, as they showed that a person tends not to perceive things that bother and worry him and that conflict with his whims and desires. And that is what the Quran points to when it presents the state of the disbelievers who did not benefit from their senses and minds as a result of the motives, values, and whims that possessed them:
"And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. It is they who are the heedless" [Al-A'raf 7:179].
"... Say, 'It is for those who believe a guidance and a cure.' And those who do not believe – in their ears is deafness, and it is upon them blindness. Those are called from a distant place" [Fussilat 41:44]. "Those are the ones whom Allah has cursed, so He made them deaf and blinded their sight" [Muhammad 47:23]. "Then can you make the deaf hear or guide the blind and he who is in clear error?" [Az-Zukhruf 43:40].
Relative blindness
And if there is sensory blindness resulting from creation initially, then there is a temporary one generated by passion or love, and therefore the lover or the one with passion is veiled from many things that he does not see while others see him, as he is afflicted with partial temporary blindness due to his love or passion, so he only sees the dimension that increases his passion or love. And thus it came regarding the people of Noah about
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage critiques the reliability of sense perception as a source of certain knowledge. It begins by noting that human senses are limited: there are images and sounds beyond our natural perception, though modern devices can capture and translate them for us. The author then presents a researcher's view that the senses either create or transmit perceptions, but we lack a criterion to distinguish between what is externally real and what is a product of imagination or illusion. A concrete example is given: reading these words. One might claim it is real because we see and touch the book, but the author counters that a person dreaming could have the same experience. The dream argument is developed further: even if we feel awake, we could be dreaming that we are awake; dreams often feel real, and we only know they were dreams upon waking. Thus, we cannot be certain we are not currently dreaming. Next, the author argues that even if senses were reliable, they are influenced by personal motives and values. Modern psychology confirms that people tend to block out perceptions that disturb them or conflict with their desires. The Quran is cited to show that disbelievers' senses and hearts are sealed due to their whims, so they fail to perceive guidance. Finally, the author notes a temporary sensory blindness caused by love or passion, where a lover only sees what reinforces his passion, analogous to the people of Noah who were blind to the truth. This passage thus systematically dismantles the claim that sense perception provides certainty, using both rational arguments (dream) and scriptural evidence.

Key Terms
الحواس (al-hawas): The five senses; the author argues they are limited in scope, prone to deception (as in dreams), and influenced by personal motives, hence not a reliable source of certainty. [Note: In classical mantiq, senses are considered a valid source of primary knowledge but require rational verification; here the critique is more radical, questioning even the distinction between waking and dreaming.]
الوهم (al-wahm): Illusion or imagination; used in contrast to external reality, as the author questions whether we can distinguish between what the senses transmit and what they create from imagination. [Note: In classical philosophy (e.g., Ibn Sina), wahm is a distinct internal faculty that perceives meanings; here it is used loosely to mean 'illusion'.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the dream argument in the passage?
A) Dreams are always false and cannot be trusted.
B) Since dreams feel real while asleep, we cannot be certain we are not dreaming now, so sense experience alone cannot guarantee truth.
C) The senses are the only reliable source of knowledge.
D) The Quran prohibits thinking about dreams.

Key Takeaway
The dream argument and psychological bias show that sense perception is insufficient for certainty, clearing the way for revelation-based knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Construct a brief argument (in one paragraph) that uses the dream argument to challenge someone who says 'I am certain that the sun has risen because I see it.' Show why seeing is not sufficient for certainty.
?
2. Find a Quranic verse (other than those cited) that describes spiritual blindness or deafness. Explain how this verse reinforces the critique that desires can block perception.

Critique of Empiricism as Sole Source of Knowledge
Author critiques empiricism, citing Quranic examples and logical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the self-referential inconsistency argument and the impossibility argument used to critique pure empiricism.

Core Idea
Empiricism cannot justify itself nor prove impossibility.

The author of this passage challenges the notion that sense perception is the only valid source of knowledge. By examining the Quranic portrayal of those who rely solely on the senses, he sets the stage for two devastating logical critiques. In this lesson, you will analyze these critiques and understand why Islamic epistemology refuses to reduce knowledge to sensory experience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Find the exact claim being criticized: that sense is the sole path to knowledge. The author states 'الاقتصار على الحس طريقاً وحيداً للمعرفة'.
This claim is attributed to empiricists.
2
Follow the self-referential argument
Notice how the author points out that the empiricist principle itself cannot be proven by sense, because a thing cannot be evidence for its own truth. The rule 'sense is the only source' is based on a judgment of the intellect, not on sensory evidence.
3
Analyze the impossibility argument
Understand why judging absolute impossibility is beyond the scope of sense perception. The author argues that impossibility (al-istihalah) is not empirically testable; thus, if sense were the only source, we could never claim anything is absolutely impossible.
4
Examine the shift from epistemic to metaphysical
The author criticizes empiricists for moving from 'cannot be sensed' to 'cannot exist', which is an illicit inference. This contradicts the empiricists' own methodology.
5
Connect to Islamic epistemology
Realize that Islamic thought grants sense a limited, relative role, not absolute certainty. The author contrasts this with Western pragmatism and emphasizes moderation and multiple sources.

وعن الكافرين عموماً: ﴿وَمَثَلُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا كَمَثَلِ الَّذِي يَنْعِقُ بِمَا لَا يَسْمَعُ إِلَّا دُعَاءً وَنِدَاءً صُمٌّ بُكْمٌ عُمْيٌ فَهُمْ لا يَعْقِلُونَ) [البقرة: ١٧٩/٢].
هنا يتضح أن الاقتصار على الحس طريقاً وحيداً للمعرفة يعرض القائلين به لمزالق ومآخذ كثيرة أبرزها:
١ - في هذا القول تحديد لطاقة الفكر البشري، وإنقاص لفعالية العقل بوصفه طريقاً للمعرفة. حيث إن تقرير طريقة الحس إنما أتت بناءً على حكم العقل، وإن لم يعلن الحسيون ذلك صراحة. ذلك أنهم يدركون أن الحس لا يمكن أن يكون هو الذي قرر قاعدتهم تلك، لأن الشيء لا يكون دليلاً على صدق نفسه.
٢- لو اعتمدنا على الحس طريقاً وحيداً للمعرفة لما استطعنا الحكم باستحالة شيء مطلقاً، لأن الاستحالة التي تعني عدم إمكان وجود الشيء ليس مما يدخل في نطاق التجربة، ولا يمكن للحواس أن تكشف عنه. وكون الحسيين يزعمون أنه لا موجود إلا المحسوس بصيغة الحصر فإنهم يكونون قد تجاوزوا حدود اختصاصهم، وانتقلوا من الحكم باستحالة تصور شيء أو إحساسه إلى الحكم باستحالة وجوده في الخارج. وما ذلك إلا استنباط شيء من شيء، وهذا يخالف مذهب الحسيين أنفسهم.
وإذا تأكدت لنا هذه النسبية فإن التربية الإسلامية لا ترى في مصدرية الحس وطريقتها درجة القطع واليقين والإطلاق، بحيث إن أي معرفة يحتوي عليها منهجها معتمداً على الحس ليست على مستوى واحد من هذه الزاوية. فهو يبدأ من اليقين، وينتهي بالظن المرجوح كما أشرنا سلفاً. ومن هنا يبرز الفرق الجوهري بين فلسفة التربية الإسلامية والفكر التربوي الغربي المتمثل في (البراجماتية) غالباً حيث جعلت الأولى الحس واحداً من المصادر الرئيسة لا أنه المصدر الرئيس - إن لم يكن الوحيد لدى بعض غلاة الفكر التربوي الغربي. وهذا الاعتدال في فلسفة التربية الإسلامية يدلل على سعة الأفق، وامتلاك المقدرة لديها على استيعاب المصادر والطرائق الأخرى، ويجعل - من ثَمّ - من حكمها على الظواهر المختلفة، ومن النتائج التي تنتهي إليها أكثر موضوعية وانسجاماً مع المنهج العلمي الدقيق المنبثق من التصور الإسلامي للإنسان والكون والحياة، وليس المنهج العلمي الغربي المتسم بأحادية النظرة والمتأثر برد الفعل الجامح إزاء التيار العقلي.
ومن جانب آخر فإن نسبية الحواس التي تؤمن بها فلسفة التربية الإسلامية تكسبها موضوعية في تعاملها مع الحس والتجريب، رغم النشأة الإسلامية للمنهج التجريبي. ذلك أن هذا المنهج يتسم بجملة سمات من خلالها يتبين أوجه الخلاف بينه وبين المنهج الديني:
Chapter Three: First Section - Sense. So they denied him, and We saved him and those with him in the ship, and We drowned those who denied Our signs; indeed they were a blind people. [Al-A'raf 7:64]. And about the hypocrites: Their example is like one who kindled a fire, but when it illuminated what was around him, Allah took away their light and left them in darkness, unable to see; deaf, dumb, blind, so they cannot return. [Al-Baqarah 2:17-18]. And about the disbelievers generally: And the example of those who disbelieve is like one who calls out to that which hears nothing but a call and a cry; deaf, dumb, blind, so they do not understand. [Al-Baqarah 2:171]. Here it becomes clear that limiting [knowledge] to sense as the sole path of knowledge exposes its proponents to many pitfalls and criticisms, the most prominent of which are: 1 - In this statement there is a limitation of the capacity of human thought, and a diminishment of the effectiveness of the intellect as a path to knowledge. For the determination of the method of sense came only based on a judgment of the intellect, even if the empiricists do not declare that explicitly. That is because they realize that sense cannot be that which determined their rule, because a thing cannot be evidence for its own truth. 2 - If we relied on sense as the sole path to knowledge, we would not be able to judge the absolute impossibility of anything, because impossibility which means the non-possibility of existence of a thing is not within the scope of experience, nor can the senses uncover it. And since the empiricists claim that nothing exists except the sensible in an exclusive form, they have exceeded their jurisdiction, moving from judging the impossibility of conceiving or sensing something to judging the impossibility of its existence in the external world. That is but a deduction of something from something, and this contradicts the very doctrine of the empiricists. And if this relativity is confirmed for us, then Islamic education does not see in the source of sense and its method a degree of certainty, certitude, and absoluteness, such that any knowledge contained in its curriculum relying on sense is not at one level from this angle. It starts from certainty and ends with weak conjecture as we previously indicated. Hence emerges the essential difference between the philosophy of Islamic education and Western educational thought represented mostly by pragmatism, where the former made sense one of the main sources, not the main source—if not the only one for some extremists of Western educational thought. This moderation in the philosophy of Islamic education indicates breadth of horizon, and its possession of capacity to accommodate other sources and methods, and thus makes its judgments on various phenomena and the results it reaches more objective and consistent with the precise scientific method emanating from the Islamic conception of man, the universe, and life—not the Western scientific method characterized by a monocular view and influenced by unruly reaction towards the intellectual current. On the other hand, the relativity of the senses which the philosophy of Islamic education believes in gives it objectivity in its dealing with sense and experimentation, despite the Islamic origin of the experimental method. For this method is characterized by a set of features through which aspects of difference between it and the religious method become clear:
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a critical epistemological analysis of the claim that sense perception is the sole source of knowledge. The author begins by citing Quranic verses describing those who rely solely on sensory perception as blind, deaf, and dumb, thus establishing that such an approach is deficient from an Islamic perspective. The author then presents two major criticisms of empiricism. First, the empiricist position itself relies on a judgment of the intellect (that sense is reliable) but cannot be proven by sense itself, as a thing cannot be evidence for its own truth—this is a self-referential inconsistency. Second, if sense were the only path to knowledge, we could never judge absolute impossibility, because impossibility is not empirically testable. The author argues that empiricists overstep when they move from 'cannot be sensed' to 'cannot exist', which is an illicit inference. The author then discusses the relative nature of sensory knowledge, noting that Islamic education does not grant it absolute certainty but rather degrees of probability. This moderation contrasts with Western pragmatism, which often elevates sense to the primary or sole source. The author concludes that the Islamic approach is more objective and in harmony with a comprehensive scientific method that includes rational and revelation-based sources.

الاستحالة
النسبية
اليقين

D) Empiricism leads to polytheism.

The author demonstrates that empiricism cannot justify its own epistemological foundation and cannot account for absolute impossibility, thereby refuting the claim that sense is the sole source of knowledge.
