Conditional Arguments in Epistemology
Author critiques sense perception and introduces rationalist position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a conditional argument and evaluate its validity in an epistemological context.

Core Idea
Rationalists argue that if knowledge were solely from senses, knowledge would be impossible.

In this passage, the author presents a rationalist critique of sense perception as a reliable source of knowledge. The key move is a conditional argument: if our knowledge were based solely on sensation, then knowledge would be impossible. Understanding this conditional structure helps you see how rationalists support their position and how you can test similar arguments in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the antecedent and consequent
Find the 'if' part (the condition) and the 'then' part (the result). Here, the antecedent is 'if our cognitions were actually based on sensation' and the consequent is 'knowledge would be impossible'.
The Arabic uses 'لو' which indicates a conditional particle.
2
Determine the truth of the antecedent
The rationalists assume the antecedent is false: sensation is not the actual basis. They use this conditional to argue that sensation cannot be a reliable source, because if it were, knowledge would be impossible. Ask yourself: is the antecedent plausible?
In logic, a conditional can be true even if the antecedent is false.
3
Evaluate the logical connection
Check whether the consequent logically follows from the antecedent. The author provides a reason: perception only grasps one state of a thing, not all states. This is the justification linking antecedent to consequent.
For a valid conditional, the support must be sound.
4
Apply to Islamic science
Consider a similar conditional argument in Kalam: 'If the Qur'an were human-made, it would contain contradictions.' The mutakallimun use this to argue for divine origin. Identify the antecedent and consequent.
This helps you see how conditional reasoning underpins theological proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا كان الحس مصدراً من مصادر المعرفة و طريقة من طرائقها حسبما سبق - فإن أصحاب المذهب العقلي لا يوافقون على ذلك، بل يعدون الحواس خداعة كذابة مخطئه. إذ لو كانت معارفنا قائمه بالفعل على الحس لكانت المعرفة مستحيلة، ذلك أن الإدراك و التجربة يخبراننا عن التعلق بحال واحدة من أحوال الشيء، دون تناول جميع أحواله وإن الحواس أقرب إلى عدو المعرفة منها إلى خادمها. بل لقد غلا بعضهم في معارضة الحسيين إلى الحد الذي ادعى فيه أنه لا يصل شيء إلى النفس من الخارج، كما لا يمكن للنفس أن تبتكر شيئاً إذا لم يكن الأصل فيها العقل(۱).
If sensation is a source of knowledge and one of its methods as previously, then the adherents of the rationalist school do not agree with that, rather they consider the senses as deceitful, lying, mistaken. For if our cognitions were actually based on sensation, knowledge would be impossible, because perception and experience inform us of attachment to one state of a thing's states, without encompassing all its states, and the senses are closer to being an enemy of knowledge than its servant. Indeed, some of them went to extremes in opposing the sensationalists to the extent that he claimed that nothing reaches the soul from the outside, just as it is impossible for the soul to invent anything if the intellect is not its origin (1).
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents the rationalist critique of sense perception as a source of knowledge. The author begins by stating that rationalists disagree with the view that sensation is a reliable source, instead deeming the senses deceptive. He then posits a conditional argument: if our knowledge were actually based on sensation, knowledge would be impossible. The reason given is that perception only grasps a single state of a thing, not all its states, making sensation an obstacle rather than an aid. The passage ends by noting some rationalists went so far as to claim that nothing enters the soul from outside, and the soul cannot create anything without the intellect as its origin. This sets up the need to define the intellect.

Conditional reasoning is a powerful tool used by rationalists to critique sense perception; understanding it helps you evaluate epistemological arguments in Islamic thought.

Definitions of the Intellect (al-ʿAql) and Rationalism
Author defines 'aql linguistically, technically, and philosophically, and outlines the rationalist school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the linguistic, technical, and philosophical definitions of 'aql and explain how these definitions gave rise to the rationalist school.

Core Idea
'Aql means restraint, preparedness, and discrimination—three layers shaping Islamic and Western rationalism.

The author begins by insisting on definitions to resolve disputes. He provides a multilayered definition of 'aql, moving from its linguistic root of restraint, through its technical meaning as a power ready for knowledge, to its philosophical use as a tool, a high mental operation, and a set of certain principles. Finally, he traces how these philosophical meanings led to the Western rationalist school. Understanding these definitions is essential for engaging with later discussions on reason versus revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels of definition
Look for the linguistic definition (lughatan), the technical definition (al-quwwa al-mutahayyi'a), and the philosophical definitions (fi al-iṣṭilāḥ al-falsafī).
The linguistic definition emphasizes restraint; the technical emphasizes preparedness; the philosophical gives multiple roles.
2
Extract the key components of each definition
For linguistic: ḥajr (restraint) and nahy (prohibition). For technical: quwwa mutahayyi'a (prepared power) for receiving knowledge. For philosophical: three meanings: tool of discrimination, highest mental operations, certain principles.
3
Distinguish between the three philosophical meanings and the three aspects (wujūh)
The passage lists three philosophical meanings (maʿānī) and then independently three aspects (wujūh) from the majority of philosophers. Note the difference: the aspects are a praiseworthy disposition, meanings as premises, and a power perceiving qualities.
Do not conflate the two lists; both are part of the philosophical elaboration.
4
Connect to the rationalist school
The passage states that these philosophical meanings gave rise to the rationalist school (al-madhhab al-ʿaqlī). Identify the key claim: everything is reducible to rational principles, and note the representatives named (Descartes, etc.).
This is a modern Western development, not a classical Islamic classification.

والعقل هو القوه المتهيئة لقبول العلم، ويطلق على العلم الذي يستفيده الإنسان عن طريق العقل (۱).
وفي الاصطلاح الفلسفي: ورد تعريف العقل لدى الفلاسفة بمعنى من المعاني التالية:
١ - أداة التمييز بين الحق و الباطل و الصواب والخطأ.

(۳) قوة تدرك صفات الأشياء من حسنها وقبحها، أو كمالها و نقصانها). إن هذه المعاني هي التي أفرزت ما عُرف لدى الغرب بالمذهب العقلي (Intlectualisme) أو العقليين (Rationalists)، وهو عبارة عن القول بأن كل ما هو موجود فهو مردود إلى مبادئ عقلية. وهو مذهب ديكارت واسبينوزا، وليبنز، وفولف وهيجل...))(4).
ويقوم هذا الاتجاه على الاعتقاد بأن قوة الفطرة هي الأصل الذي يصدر عنه كل علم حقيقي، بوصفها القوة العاقلة في الإنسان أو أنها على الأخص مصدر أهم صفتين للعلم الحقيقي وهما صفة الضرورة، والصدق المطلق().
To settle the dispute about this matter, it is good for us to address it starting from the definition. Definition of the intellect. Al-ʿaql linguistically means restraint and prohibition, opposite of foolishness, plural ʿuqūl. It is a verbal noun, even though Sibawayh considers it an adjective, because a verbal noun does not come on the pattern mafʿūl at all. It is called ʿaql because it restrains its possessor from falling into perils, i.e., it holds him back (2). Or because one perceives realities with it (3). Chapter Three: Section Two - The Intellect. And the intellect is the power prepared to receive knowledge, and it is applied to the knowledge that a person acquires through the intellect (1). In philosophical terminology: the definition of the intellect among philosophers came with one of the following meanings: 1. The tool of discrimination between truth and falsehood, right and wrong. 2. The highest form of mental operations in general and demonstration and inference in particular. 3. The certain principles upon which all rational people agree (2). And the majority of philosophers apply the intellect to three aspects: (1) A praiseworthy disposition in a person's speech and choice, movements and stillness. (2) Meanings gathered in the mind that become premises, thereby deriving purposes and interests. (3) A power that perceives the qualities of things, their goodness and badness, or their perfection and deficiency. These meanings are what gave rise to what is known in the West as intellectualism or rationalists, which is the claim that everything that exists is reducible to rational principles. It is the school of Descartes, Spinoza, Leibniz, Wolff, and Hegel... (4). And this direction is based on the belief that the power of instinct is the origin from which all true knowledge proceeds, as it is the rational power in man or that it is especially the source of the two most important attributes of true knowledge: necessity and absolute truth (5).
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive definition of 'aql (intellect/reason) from multiple perspectives. It begins by stating the need to start with a definition to settle the dispute. It then gives the linguistic definition of 'aql as restraint (ḥajr) and prohibition (nahy), explaining that it is called such because it restrains its possessor from falling into perils. The technical definition follows: the intellect is the power prepared to receive knowledge, and it is also applied to the acquired knowledge. The philosophical definitions are then enumerated: (1) the tool of discrimination between truth and falsehood, (2) the highest form of mental operations especially demonstration and inference, (3) the certain principles agreed upon by all rational people. Then the passage lists three aspects (wujūh) of 'aql according to philosophers: a praiseworthy disposition, meanings that become premises for deriving purposes, and a power that perceives good/bad and perfect/imperfect. Finally, it explains that these meanings led to the Western rationalist school, which holds that everything is reducible to rational principles, naming Descartes, Spinoza, etc. The passage concludes that this school believes instinct (fiṭra) is the origin of all true knowledge, giving it necessity and absolute truth.

العقل
القوة المتهيئة
المذهب العقلي

Key Takeaway
The intellect ('aql) has multiple layers of meaning—linguistic, technical, and philosophical—and understanding these layers is crucial for analyzing rationalist claims in both Islamic and Western thought.

The Quranic Heart as an Epistemic Organ: Al-Ghazali's Homonymous Analysis
Author discusses Quranic usage of heart and intellect, addressing common misconceptions and presenting al-Ghazali's analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Quranic usage of 'heart' (qalb) as an epistemic tool from its common emotional perception, using al-Ghazali's analysis of homonymy.

Core Idea
The Quranic heart is a tool of knowledge, not just emotion—al-Ghazali reveals its intellectual dimension.

Many assume the heart is purely emotional, but the Quran repeatedly links it to reflection and understanding. This lesson unpacks the Quranic concept of the heart through al-Ghazali's nuanced analysis, showing how the same term can refer to both a physical organ and a spiritual intellect. By the end, you will be able to identify when 'heart' means intellect and when it means emotion, clarifying a key principle in Quranic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verses cited
Locate Quran 47:24, 16:78, and 7:179 in the passage. What do they suggest about the heart's function?
Each verse uses a different term: qulub, af'ida, qalb.
2
Analyze the problem of homonymy
The author notes a common misconception: heart is emotional versus intellectual. How does the Quran's varied usage resolve this? Observe the three categories: pure intellect, pure emotion, both combined.
Homonymy (ishtirak lafzi) is key: one word with multiple meanings.
3
Map al-Ghazali's four meanings of 'aql
Extract the four distinct meanings: (1) knowledge attribute, (2) perceiver, (3) attribute of knowledgeable, (4) locus. Relate each to the heart—physical or spiritual?
The fifth meaning (the knowing subtlety) unifies them.
4
Apply the distinction to Quranic interpretation
Using al-Ghazali's framework, classify each Quranic occurrence of qalb/fu'ad as either physical (organ) or spiritual (intellect). Check if the passage provides criteria.
This tool prevents erroneous readings.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
أَفَلَا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ الْقُرْآنَ أَمْ عَلَى قُلُوبٍ أَقْفَالُهَا (محمد: 24). ووفق هذا المعنى فإن القلب في نظر القرآن أداة من أدوات المعرفة، حيث يعتمد القرآن على مخاطبة القلب في معظم رسالته.
ومثل هذا الاستنتاج مما قد يُشكل استيعابه بالنظر إلى الشائع من كون العقل وظيفته الإرادة في حين أن القلب وظيفته العاطفة ولكن اهتمام القرآن الواضح بالقلب إلى حد احتوائه (122) آيةً تتحدث عنه بجوانبه المختلفة، بحيث تتعدد صوره، فتارة نشعر أننا أمام صورة العقل ذاته، وتارة نشعر أننا أمام العاطفة والمشاعر الوجدانية، وثالثة نشعر أننا أمام الجانبين معاً: جانب العقل وجانب العاطفة وهكذا. ذلك كله مما يساعد على إزالة ذلك الإشكال المفترض.
ونتيجة لذكر القلب في القرآن بوصفه اسم جنس مفرداً ومجموعاً، بخلاف العقل الذي ورد مفرداً مشتقاً من اسم جنسه، فإن ذلك دفع ببعض الباحثين لاستخلاص أن ليس هناك شيء مجسّم في جسم الإنسان، لذات اسمه العقل. أما القلب فإن هناك شيئاً لذات اسمه القلب وهو تلك المضغة القائمة في الصدر. الأمر الذي يدعونا للفصل التام بين كل من العقل والقلب، لنصل إلى أن القلب من الألفاظ المشتركة في معانيها، وأن من جملة تلك المعاني (العقل). أما القلب (المضغة) ذو الذات المحسوسة فشيء آخر.
ولكن الإمام الغزالي مع تمييزه بين القلب العضوي والقلب الرحماني لا يجزم بانفصال هذا الأخير تماماً عن الأول فقال ... لفظ القلب وهو يطلق لمعنيين. أحدهما اللحم الصنوبري الشكل المودع في الجانب الأيسر من الصدر، وهو لحم مخصوص، وفي باطنه تجويف... والمعنى الثاني هو لطيفة ربانية روحية لها بالقلب الجسماني تعلّق. وتلك اللطيفة هي حقيقة الإنسان. وهو المدرك العالم العارف من الإنسان، وهو المخاطب والمعاتب والمطالب، ولها علاقة مع القلب الجسماني...)(1). وعنده – أي الغزالي- أن العقل اسم يطلق بالاشتراك لمعان أربعة مختلفة هي: المعنى الأول: قد يطلق ويراد به العلم بحقائق الأمور فيكون عبارة عن صفة العلم الذي محله (القلب الجسماني). المعنى الثاني: قد يطلق ويراد به المدرك للعلوم، فيكون هو لطيفة القلب (الروح الجسماني). المعنى الثالث قد يطلق ويراد به صفة العالم النفس الشهوانية). المعنى الرابع: قد يطلق ويراد به محل الإدراك أي المدرك (العلوم). وقد يضاف معنى خامس وهو اللطيفة العالمة المدركة من الإنسان والألفاظ الأربعة بجملتها تتوارد عليها (2).
وبالنسبة إلى الأفئدة فإنها جمع فؤاد، وأصله في القلب. ويطلق كثيراً على العقل، وهو المراد في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالْأَبْصَارَ وَالْأَفْئِدَةَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [النحل: 78]. وهذا المعنى جارٍ مجرى الاستخدام المعنوي للقلب، حينما يكون أداةً لفقه حقائق الأمور، والتوصل عن طريقه إلى أصدق المعارف. ولذلك فإن الكافرين حرموا من هذه الوظيفة: ﴿لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لَا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا﴾ [الأعراف: 179] (4).
Chapter Three, Section Two: Intellect. 'Do they not reflect upon the Quran, or are there locks upon their hearts?' (Muhammad 24). According to this meaning, the heart in the Quran's view is a tool of knowledge, as the Quran relies on addressing the heart in most of its message. And such a conclusion may be difficult to grasp given the common notion that the intellect's function is will, while the heart's function is emotion, but the Quran's clear attention to the heart, to the extent that it contains 122 verses speaking about it in its various aspects, such that its forms multiply: sometimes we feel we are facing the image of the intellect itself, sometimes we feel we are facing emotion and sentimental feelings, and thirdly we feel we are facing both aspects together: the aspect of the intellect and the aspect of emotion, and so on. All of this helps to remove that supposed problem. And as a result of the mention of the heart in the Quran as a noun, both singular and plural, unlike the intellect which appears only as a singular derivative of its noun, that led some researchers to conclude that there is no physical thing in the human body with the essence named 'intellect'. As for the heart, there is a thing with the essence named 'heart', and it is that morsel located in the chest. This calls for a complete separation between each of the intellect and the heart, to arrive at the conclusion that 'heart' is among words sharing multiple meanings, and among those meanings is 'intellect'. As for the heart (the morsel) with its sensible essence, it is another thing. But Imam al-Ghazali, despite his distinction between the organic heart and the spiritual heart, does not assert the complete separation of the latter from the former. He said: 'The word heart is used for two meanings. One of them is the pine-shaped flesh lodged in the left side of the chest, which is specific flesh, and inside it is a cavity... The second meaning is a spiritual divine subtlety that has a connection with the physical heart. That subtlety is the reality of the human being. It is the perceiving, knowing, cognizant part of the human, and it is the addressed, blamed, and tasked, and it has a relationship with the physical heart...' According to him – al-Ghazali – the word intellect is used homonymously for four different meanings: The first meaning: it may be used and intended as knowledge of the realities of things, so it is an expression for the attribute of knowledge whose locus is the physical heart. The second meaning: it may be used and intended as the perceiver of knowledge, so it is the subtlety of the heart (the physical spirit). The third meaning: it may be used and intended as the attribute of the knowledgeable (the soul of desire). The fourth meaning: it may be used and intended as the locus of perception, i.e., the perceiver (of knowledge). A fifth meaning may be added, which is the knowing, perceiving subtlety of the human, and all four expressions are applied to it. As for 'af'ida', it is the plural of 'fu'ad', and its origin is in the heart. It is often used for the intellect, and it is intended in the verse: 'And Allah brought you out from your mothers' wombs knowing nothing, and He gave you hearing, sight, and hearts (af'ida) that you might give thanks' (An-Nahl 78). This meaning follows the same course as the metaphorical use of the heart, when it is a tool for understanding the realities of things and attaining through it the truest knowledge. Therefore, the disbelievers are deprived of this function: 'They have hearts with which they do not understand' (Al-A'raf 179).
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological analysis of the Quranic terms 'aql (intellect) and qalb (heart). It opens by citing Quran 47:24 to establish that the heart is a tool of reflection and knowledge, not merely emotion. The author then addresses a common misconception: if the heart is the seat of emotion, how can it also be an intellectual organ? The answer lies in the Quran's multifaceted use of 'heart', which sometimes denotes intellect, sometimes emotion, sometimes both. A linguistic point is made: 'aql appears only as a singular derivative (e.g., ya'qilun), while qalb appears as both singular and plural (qulub), indicating that the heart is a concrete entity while the intellect is an abstract attribute. Some researchers therefore conclude that the physical heart (the morsel) exists, whereas the intellect is not a physical organ but a faculty associated with the heart. Then al-Ghazali's view is presented: he distinguishes between the physical heart (al-qalb al-'udwi) and the spiritual heart (al-qalb al-rabbani), but does not separate them absolutely. The spiritual heart is a divine subtlety (latifa rabbaniyya) that is the true human reality; it is the perceiver and knower, and it is related to the physical heart. Al-Ghazali also lists four homonymous meanings of 'aql: (1) knowledge of realities, an attribute residing in the physical heart; (2) the faculty that perceives knowledge, i.e., the spiritual subtlety; (3) the attribute of the knowledgeable (specifically the soul of desire, perhaps a moral faculty); (4) the locus of perception itself. A fifth meaning is added: the knowing, perceiving subtlety, which encompasses all four. Finally, the term af'ida (plural of fu'ad) is discussed; it is often synonymous with the spiritual heart and intellect, as in Quran 16:78, where it is a gift from Allah for understanding. The disbelievers are described as having hearts that do not understand (7:179), meaning they lack the proper use of this faculty. The commentary by the author synthesizes Quranic philology and al-Ghazali's philosophical psychology to clarify that the heart in the Quran is not merely emotional but an epistemic organ.

اللطيفة الربانية
الفؤاد

B) Two meanings

D) Five meanings

Key Takeaway
The Quranic heart is an epistemic organ; al-Ghazali's homonymous analysis of 'aql reveals its intellectual dimension, grounding Quranic epistemology in a sophisticated linguistic framework.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Qur'anic Method of Striking Intellectual Examples
Author defines Qur'anic method of striking examples as rational comparison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and method of ḍarb al-amthāl in the Qur'an and explain how it activates the intellect.

Core Idea
The Qur'an uses intellectual examples to compare opposites and engage the mind for truth.

The Qur'an does not merely narrate stories; it employs a deliberate method of striking examples to contrast truth and falsehood. These examples are rational tools designed to stimulate the intellect and lead to conviction. In this lesson, we analyze the Qur'anic technique of ḍarb al-amthāl as explained in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method
Recognize that the Qur'an strikes examples (ḍarb al-amthāl) to compare opposites such as tawheed vs shirk, guidance vs misguidance, truth vs falsehood.
The term 'ḍarb al-amthāl' is a deliberate pedagogical technique.
2
List the pairs of opposites
From the passage, extract the three pairs: tawheed and shirk, guidance and misguidance, truth and falsehood.
These opposites are foundational in Islamic theology.
3
Note the purpose
The aim is to activate the intellect ('aql) to arrive at the truth required by the context of the verses.
The intellect is the target and tool for understanding.
4
Examine the cited verses
Read Ghafir 58 (contrast blind/seeing, believers/wrongdoers), Ankabut 41-43 (spider web analogy), and Az-Zumar 27 (summary of purpose).
Each verse illustrates the method with concrete examples.
5
Conclude the educational value
This method is essential in Islamic pedagogy, teaching through rational comparison to foster understanding and remembrance.
The passage states it is adopted in Islamic education and teaching methods.

ضرب الأمثلة:
ويضرب القرآن الكريم الأمثلة العقلية، وذلك للمقارنة بين الأضداد التوحيد والشرك - الهداية والضلال - الحق والباطل بهدف إعمال العقل للوصول إلى الحقيقة التي يقتضيها سياق الآيات:
﴿وَما يَسْتَوِي الأَعْمَى وَالْبَصِيرُ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ وَلَا الْمُسِيءُ قَلِيلاً ما تَتَذَكَّرُونَ) [غافر: ٥٨/٤٠].
مَثَلُ الَّذِينَ اتَّخَذُوا مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ أَوْلِياءَ كَمَثَلِ الْعَنْكَبوتِ الْحَذَتْ بَيْناً وَإِنَّ أَوْهَنَ الْبُيُوتِ لَبَيْتُ الْعَنْكَبُوتِ لَوْ كَانُوا يَعْلَمُونَ، إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَعْلَمُ ما يَدْعُونَ مِنْ دُونِهِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ وَهُوَ الْعَزِيزُ الْحَكِيمُ، وَتِلْكَ الْأَمْثَالُ نَضْرِبُهَا لِلنَّاسِ وَمَا يَعْقِلُها إلا الْعالِمُونَ [العنكبوت: ٤١/٢٩ - ٤٣].
ولخص القرآن أسلوبه في ضرب الأمثلة والهدف العقلي من وراء ذلك
فقال:
﴿وَلَقَدْ ضَرَبْنَا لِلنَّاسِ فِي هَذَا الْقُرْآنِ مِنْ كُلِّ مَثَلٍ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ)
[الزمر: ٢٧/٣٩].
ويتضمن هذا الإفادة من أسلوب ضرب الأمثلة باعتبارها من الأساليب المعتمدة في منهج التربية الإسلامية، وطرائق تدريسها.
Striking examples: The Noble Qur'an strikes intellectual examples, for comparison between opposites: tawheed and shirk, guidance and misguidance, truth and falsehood, with the aim of activating the intellect to reach the truth required by the context of the verses: 'And not equal are the blind and the seeing, and those who have believed and done righteous deeds and the evil-doer. Little do you remember.' [Ghafir 58]. 'The example of those who take allies other than Allah is like that of the spider who takes a home. And indeed, the weakest of homes is the home of the spider, if they only knew. Indeed, Allah knows whatever they invoke besides Him of anything, and He is the Exalted in Might, the Wise. And these examples We present to the people, and none understand them except those who know.' [Ankabut 41-43]. The Qur'an summarized its style in striking examples and the intellectual aim behind that, saying: 'And We have certainly presented for the people in this Qur'an from every [kind of] example, that they might remember.' [Az-Zumar 27]. This includes benefit from the style of striking examples as one of the methods adopted in the curriculum of Islamic education and its teaching methods.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage defines the Qur'anic method of 'striking examples' (ḍarb al-amthāl) as a rational pedagogical tool. The author states that the Qur'an uses examples to compare opposites—tawheed vs. shirk, guidance vs. misguidance, truth vs. falsehood—with the explicit purpose of activating the intellect ('aql) to arrive at truth. Three verses are cited: the first (Ghafir 40:58) contrasts the blind and the seeing, believers and wrongdoers; the second (Ankabut 29:41-43) likens those who take false protectors to a spider's fragile home, emphasizing that only the learned understand these examples; the third (Az-Zumar 39:27) summarizes the aim as making people reflect (tadhakkur). The passage concludes that this method is integral to Islamic educational methodology. The examples are not mere stories but intellectual arguments designed to stimulate reasoning.

Intellectual Impossibility and the Proof of Tawheed
Author defines intellectual impossibility and cites Qur'anic evidence for tawheed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define intellectual impossibility (al-tamānuʿ al-ʿaqlī) and explain why the intellect necessarily rejects the existence of two gods, using the Qur'anic verses cited.

Core Idea
The mind inevitably rejects two contradictories; this proves tawheed.

This lesson introduces a rational method central to Islamic creed: intellectual impossibility. The author defines it as the mind's necessary refusal to accept two contradictory beliefs, and applies it to the impossibility of multiple gods. You will see how the Qur'an itself provides a rational argument that the universe cannot be upright if there were two deities, thus grounding the proof of tawheed in both reason and revelation.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the sentence in the Arabic where the author defines 'intellectual impossibility'. Note the key terms: امتناع تصديق العقل بقبول المتناقضين and الاستبعاد العقلي.
2
Identify the concrete example
The author applies the definition to the case of multiple gods. What precisely makes two gods impossible according to the passage?
3
Examine the Qur'anic evidence
Read the two verses cited. How do they illustrate the intellectual impossibility? In Al-Mu'minun, what would each deity do? In Al-Anbiya, what would be the outcome of multiple gods?
4
Connect to theological method
The passage says this method is especially important in teaching creed. Reflect on why this rational demonstration is considered a foundational proof for tawheed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٩- التمانع العقلي
والمقصود بهذا الأسلوب امتناع تصديق العقل بقبول المتناقضين لامتناع ذلك بالاستبعاد العقلي. ومن ذلك استحالة أن يقبل العقل بوجود إلهين لاستحالة استقامة الكون، بوصفهما ندين متنازعين في إرادتيهما والتوجيهات الصادرة عن كل واحد منهما في تسيير شؤون الكون والإنسان. وإلى هذا المعنى تشير الآيتان التاليتان:
ما اتَّخَذَ اللَّهُ مِنْ وَلَدٍ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِلَهِ إِذَا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهِ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ﴾ [المؤمنون: ٩١/٢٣].
أَمِ اتَّخَذُوا آلِهَةً مِنَ الْأَرْضِ هُمْ يُنشِرُونَ، لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتام [الأنبياء: ۲۱/۲۱-۲۲].
وأسلوب التمانع العقلي معتبر في تدريس العقيدة على وجه الخصوص.
9- Intellectual Impossibility: What is meant by this method is the mind's refusal to accept two contradictories, due to the impossibility of that by intellectual exclusion. Among that is the impossibility of the mind accepting the existence of two gods, due to the impossibility of the universe being upright, since they would be two rivals conflicting in their wills and the directives emanating from each of them in managing the affairs of the universe and humanity. And the following two verses indicate this meaning: 'Allah has not taken any son, nor has there ever been with Him any deity. [If there had been], then each deity would have taken what it created, and some of them would have sought to overcome others.' [Al-Mu'minun 91]. 'Or have they taken gods from the earth who resurrect the dead? If there had been within the heavens and earth gods besides Allah, they would have been ruined.' [Al-Anbiya 21-22]. And the method of intellectual impossibility is considered especially important in teaching creed.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'intellectual impossibility' (al-tamānuʿ al-ʿaqlī). The author explains it as the mind's necessary refusal to accept two contradictory propositions, based on rational exclusion (al-istibʿād al-ʿaqlī). The key example is the impossibility of accepting two gods, because if there were two, they would conflict in their wills and management of the universe, leading to corruption. Two Qur'anic verses are cited: Al-Mu'minun 23:91 argues that if there were multiple gods, each would take control and they would try to overcome each other; Al-Anbiya 21:21-22 states that if there were gods besides Allah in the heavens and earth, they (the heavens and earth) would be ruined. The passage concludes that this method is particularly important in teaching Islamic creed (ʿaqīda). It demonstrates that the Qur'an uses rational argumentation to establish tawheed.

Key Terms
التمانع العقلي
الاستبعاد العقلي
المتناقضين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Qur'an says so without reason

C) Because humans cannot know about gods
D) Because the intellect is limited

Key Takeaway
Intellectual impossibility is a rational proof that the mind necessarily rejects the existence of multiple gods due to inevitable conflict, and the Qur'an endorses this reasoning.

The Quranic Link Between Intellect and Behavior
Author cites Quranic verses on sealing of hearts and concludes intellect and behavior are reciprocal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Quran's description of heart sealing demonstrates a reciprocal relationship between intellect and behavior.

Core Idea
The Quran shows that intellect and behavior are not separate; they influence each other reciprocally.

This lesson examines three Quranic verses that speak of hearts being sealed as a consequence of disbelief. The author draws a profound educational conclusion: intellect and behavior are not independent faculties but are organically connected, each affecting the other. Understanding this reciprocal link is essential for grasping the Quran's holistic view of human psychology and moral responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verses and their context
Read the three verses quoted: An-Nisa 4:155, At-Tawba 9:87, and Al-Munafiqun 63:3. Note the repeated structure: a cause (disbelief, breaking covenant, etc.) leads to 'sealing' of hearts, which results in inability to understand or believe.
The sealing is a divine consequence, not an arbitrary act.
2
Trace the cause-effect sequence
In each verse, there is a clear causal chain: specific negative behaviors (breaking covenant, disbelief, killing prophets, preferring to stay behind) → Allah seals their hearts → they do not understand (or believe). This shows that behavior affects the state of the heart and intellect.
The term 'tab'' (sealing) implies a locking that prevents receptivity to guidance.
3
Extract the reciprocal relationship
The author then states educationally that there is an organic (عضوية) and reciprocal (تبادلي) relationship between intellect and behavior. Reflect: if behavior can lead to sealing of the heart (loss of understanding), then sound behavior preserves or enhances intellect. Conversely, a sound intellect guides behavior. They are mutually reinforcing.
This is not a one-way causation but a two-way interaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَبِمَا نَقْضِهِمْ مِيثَاقَهُمْ وَكُفْرِهِمْ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ وَقَتْلِهِمُ الْأَنْبِيَاءَ بِغَيْرِ حَقٍّ وَقَوْلِهِمْ قُلُوبُنَا غَلْفٌ بَلْ طَبَعَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهَا بِكُفْرِهِمْ فَلَا يُؤْمِنُونَ إِلَّا قَلِيلا [النساء: ١٥٥/٤]. ﴿رَضُوا بِأَنْ يَكُونُوا مَعَ الْخَوالِفِ وَطُبِعَ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ فَهُمْ لا يَفْقَهُونَ ) [التوبة: ٨٧/٩]. ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُمْ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا فَطُبِعَ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ فَهُمْ لا يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [المنافقون: ٣/٦٣]. وتربوياً فإن ذلك يؤكد على أن ثمة علاقة عضوية بين العقل والسلوك فيتأثر كل واحد منهما بالآخر، على نحو تبادلي.
So because of their breaking of the covenant, their disbelief in the verses of Allah, and their killing of the prophets without right, and their saying, 'Our hearts are wrapped,' but Allah has sealed them due to their disbelief, so they do not believe except a few. [An-Nisa 4:155]. 'They were content to be with those who remain behind, and their hearts were sealed, so they do not understand.' [At-Tawba 9:87]. 'That is because they believed then disbelieved, so their hearts were sealed, so they do not understand.' [Al-Munafiqun 63:3]. And educationally, this confirms that there is an organic relationship between intellect and behavior, each one influencing the other in a reciprocal manner.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage begins by quoting three Quranic verses that describe the sealing of hearts as a consequence of disbelief, breaking covenants, and turning away from guidance. The author then draws an educational conclusion: these verses demonstrate a symbiotic relationship between intellect ('aql) and behavior (suluk), each reciprocally affecting the other. The conceptual link is that a corrupted belief leads to a sealed heart and thus lack of understanding, while righteous behavior stems from sound intellect.

سلوك
طبع

A) Intellect controls behavior unilaterally
B) Behavior controls intellect unilaterally
C) They influence each other reciprocally
D) No relationship

Key Takeaway
The Quran teaches that intellect and behavior are organically connected: one's actions affect one's understanding, and vice versa.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Reflect on a modern scenario: someone claims to 'know' Islam is true but behaves contrary to its teachings. Using the passage's principle, how would you analyze the state of their intellect?

The Quran's Rejection of Blind Imitation (Taqlid)
Author explains the Quran's critique of taqlid using pre-Islamic customs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical fallacy of blind imitation (taqlid) in arguments about halal and haram and explain why the Quran condemns it.

Core Idea
The Quran demolishes 'we found our fathers' as an invalid justification for rulings.

The Quran repeatedly critiques the pre-Islamic practice of following ancestors blindly. It lists specific customs like bahira, sa'iba, wasila, and ham that were invented and falsely attributed to Allah. The Quran reveals that the argument 'we found our fathers doing it' does not constitute valid evidence. This lesson shows you how to spot this fallacy in your own reasoning and in contemporary debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the practice and its justification
Notice that the pre-Islamic Arabs forbade certain animals based on the belief that 'our fathers did so'. The Quran records their excuse: 'Enough for us is that which we found our fathers doing'.
See the verse from al-Ma'idah 5:103-104 in the source text.
2
Extract the implicit argument
Their reasoning was: Our ancestors did X (or prohibited X), so X is forbidden. This is an appeal to tradition, a type of informal fallacy.
Logically, it is an argument from authority, but the ancestors had no divine authority.
3
Apply the Quranic critique
The Quran rejects this by pointing out that the ancestors were ignorant and misguided: 'Even if their fathers knew nothing and were not guided?' It also asserts that only Allah has the right to legislate.
For example, the verse from al-A'raf 7:33: 'My Lord has only forbidden immoralities... and that you say about Allah that which you do not know.'
4
Generalize the principle
Any argument that relies solely on ancestral or cultural practice without reference to divine revelation or sound reasoning is invalid in Islam. This principle applies to all areas of religion, not just the pre-Islamic examples.
Taqlid (blind following) is only excusable for those incapable of independent reasoning, but it remains a fallacious justification in discourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسعى القرآن لتحرير العقل من الموروثات السيئة التي يتلقفها الناس بدافع التقليد الأعمى لمسلك الآباء - مثلاً - فإذا بهم يُصدرون أحكام الحل والحرمة لمجرد أنهم ألفوا آباءهم كذلك. ومن تلك المعتقدات التي اشتهرت عند أهل الجاهلية أنهم كانوا يبحرون (أي يشقون أذن الناقة) إذا أنتجت خمسة أبطـن آخرها ذكر، فيحرموا ركوبها وهي البحيرة ويسبون الناقة أو البعير نذراً على الرجل إن سلّمه الله من مرض أو بلغه منزلة. ويجعلون الناقة لأنفسهم إذا ولدت أنثى بعد أنثى، أو الشاة إذا ولدت ذكراً فهي لآلهتهم، وإن ولدت ذكراً أو أنثى فيقولون وصلت أخاها فلم يذبحوا الذكر لآلهتهم. وكانوا إذا ركب ولد الفحل قالوا حمى ظهره فلا يُركب، أو أنه إذا أنتج من صلبه عشرة قالوا: حمى ظهره فلا يُركب ولا يُمنع من كلأ ولا ماء). وذلك كله مما سجّله القرآن في سياق ذمّه لهذه الموروثات المبنية على الافتراء والتقليد لجهالة الآباء وضلالهم: (الشوكاني، فتح القدير، ٨٢/٢). ﴿مَا جَعَلَ اللهُ مِنْ بَحِيرَةٍ وَلا سَائِبَةٍ وَلا وَصِيلَةٍ وَلَا حَامِ وَلَكِنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا يَفْتَرُونَ عَلَى اللهِ الْكَذِبَ وَأَكْثَرُهُمْ لا يَعْقِلُونَ، وَإِذَا قِيلَ لَهُمْ تَعَالَوْا إِلَى مَا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ وَإِلَى الرَّسُولِ قَالُوا حَسْبُنا ما وَجَدْنَا عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَنَا أَوَلَوْ كَانَ آباؤُهُمْ لا يَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا وَلَا يَهْتَدُونَ ﴾ [المائدة: ١٠٣/٥-١٠٤]. إن مسائل الحل والحرمة بوجه خاص، وإصدار الأحكام بعامة ليست من حق آبائهم، تماماً كما ليست من صلاحية أي مراكز تفكير سلطوية، لأن ذلك ضرب من الشرك في توحيد الألوهية: ﴿قُلْ مَنْ حَرَّمَ زِينَةَ اللَّهِ الَّتِي أَخْرَجَ لِعِبَادِهِ وَالطَّيِّبَاتِ مِنَ الرِّزْقِ قُلْ هِيَ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا فِي الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيا خالِصَةً يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ كَذَلِكَ نُفَصِّلُ الآيَاتِ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْلَمُونَ، قُلْ إنّما حَرَّمَ رَبِّيَ الْفَوَاحِشَ مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْهَا وَمَا بَطَنَ وَالإِثْمَ وَالْبَغْيَ بغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ وَأَن تُشْرِكُوا بِاللهِ ما لَمْ يُنَزِّلَ بِهِ سُلْطَاناً وأن تَقُولُوا عَلَى اللهِ ما لا تَعْلَمُونَ [الأعراف: ۳۲/۷ - ۳۳]. قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ ما أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ مِنْ رِزْقٍ فَجَعَلْتُمْ مِنْهُ حَرَامًا وَحَلَالًا قُلْ اللَّهُ أَذِنَ لَكُمْ أَمْ عَلَى اللَّهِ تَفْتَرُونَ﴾ [يونس: ٥٩/١٠]. يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّ كَثِيراً مِنَ الأَخبارِ وَالرُّهْبَانِ لَيَأْكُلُونَ أَمْوالَ النَّاسِ بِالْباطِلِ وَيَصُدُّونَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَالَّذِينَ يَكْنِزُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَّةَ وَلَا يُنْفِقُونَها فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَبَشِّرْهُمْ بِعَذَابٍ أَلِيمٍ﴾ [التوبة: ٣٤/٩]. بل إن سلطة الآباء حين تتعدى حقوقها لتدعى أحقية الطاعة المطلقة، حتى في الإشراك بالله فلا مناص - في هذه الحال - من التحرر من سلطتها في ذلك: ﴿وَإِنْ جاهَدَاكَ عَلَى أَنْ تُشْرِكَ بِي مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ فَلا تُطِعْهُما وَصاحِبَهُما فِي الدُّنْيا مَعْرُوفًا وَاتَّبِعْ سَبِيلَ مَنْ أَتَابَ إِلَيَّ ثُمَّ إِلَيَّ مَرْجِعُكُمْ نَبِّئُكُمْ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [لقمان: ١٥/٣١].
And the Qur'an seeks to liberate the intellect from the bad inheritances that people receive out of blind imitation of the way of the fathers, for example, so they issue judgments of permissibility and prohibition merely because they found their fathers doing so. Among those beliefs that were famous among the people of ignorance is that they would 'bahira' (i.e., split the ear of a she-camel) if she gave birth to five offspring, the last of which was male, so they forbade riding her, and she is the 'bahira'; and they would dedicate the she-camel or the camel as a vow for a man if God saved him from illness or he reached a place; and they would make the she-camel for themselves if it gave birth to a female after a female, or the ewe if it gave birth to a male, then it is for their gods, and if it gave birth to a male or female, they would say it has reached its sibling, so they would not slaughter the male for their gods. And they used to, if the offspring of a stallion was ridden, they would say his back is protected so he is not ridden, or if he produced from his loins ten, they would say his back is protected so he is not ridden and he is not prevented from grazing or water. All of this is recorded by the Qur'an in the context of condemning these inherited practices based on falsehood and imitation of the ignorance and misguidance of the fathers. 'Allah has not appointed any bahira, sa'iba, wasila, or ham. But those who disbelieve invent falsehood against Allah, and most of them do not understand. And when it is said to them, "Come to what Allah has revealed and to the Messenger," they say, "Enough for us is that which we found our fathers doing." Even if their fathers knew nothing and were not guided?' [Al-Ma'idah 5:103-104]. Indeed, matters of permissibility and prohibition in particular, and issuing judgments in general, are not the right of their fathers, just as they are not the authority of any authoritarian centers of thought, because that is a kind of shirk in the oneness of divinity. 'Say, "Who has forbidden the adornment of Allah which He has brought forth for His servants and the good things of provision?" Say, "They are for those who believe during the worldly life, exclusively for them on the Day of Resurrection." Thus do We detail the verses for a people who know. Say, "My Lord has only forbidden immoralities – what is apparent and what is hidden – and sin, and oppression without right, and that you associate with Allah that for which He has not sent down authority, and that you say about Allah that which you do not know." [Al-A'raf 7:32-33]. Say, "Have you seen what Allah has sent down for you of provision and you make some of it forbidden and some lawful?" Say, "Has Allah permitted you, or do you invent falsehood against Allah?" [Yunus 10:59]. 'O you who have believed, indeed many of the rabbis and monks devour the wealth of people unjustly and avert from the way of Allah. And those who hoard gold and silver and spend them not in the way of Allah, give them tidings of a painful punishment.' [At-Tawba 9:34]. Rather, when the authority of fathers transgresses its rights to claim the right of absolute obedience, even in association with Allah, then there is no alternative in this situation but to liberate from its authority in that. 'And if they strive to make you associate with Me that of which you have no knowledge, do not obey them. But accompany them in this world with kindness, and follow the path of those who turn to Me. Then to Me is your return, and I will inform you of what you used to do.' [Luqman 31:15].
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and expansion of the Quranic stance on liberating the intellect from blind imitation (taqlid) and inherited superstitions. The author lists several pre-Islamic customs (bahira, sa'iba, wasila, ham) that the Quran condemns because they were based on false assumptions and mindless following of ancestors. The Quran repeatedly criticizes the argument that 'we found our fathers doing so' as an invalid justification for rulings on halal and haram. The author then cites additional verses that emphasize that only Allah has the authority to legislate, and that obedience to parents or leaders is not absolute when it involves shirk. The lesson underscores the Quran's emphasis on independent reasoning based on revelation and against authoritarian thinking.

Key Terms

بَحيرة
سائبة
وصيلة
حام

Key Takeaway
The Quran teaches that ancestral customs are not a source of Islamic law except when consistent with revelation; blind imitation is a logical fallacy and a form of shirk in legislation.

Quranic Condemnation of Blind Ancestral Tradition
Author critiques blind following of ancestors and warns Muslims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the universal nature of the Quranic critique of ancestral tradition and explain why Muslims are not exempt from this warning.

Core Idea
The Quran's condemnation of ancestral tradition is a universal human warning, not just for non-Muslims.

This passage from the author critiques blind adherence to ancestral ways. It explains that the Quran's strong condemnation is due to the emotional pull of heritage. The author then warns that Muslims can also fall into this trap, and describes how tradition can override reason. Finally, he defines Islamic education as disciplined by reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic condemnation
Locate where the author mentions that the Quran condemned following fathers in a strict manner. This is the starting point of the critique.
The author begins by recalling the Quran's severe stance.
2
Understand the cause of condemnation
The author states the condemnation is due to the extremely appealing attraction that ties people to ancestral inheritance, regardless of its quality. This shows the Quran's awareness of human psychology.
3
Recognize the universal scope
The author explicitly says the problem is human and Muslims are not excluded. Some Muslims may delude themselves into thinking they are immune. This is a key refinement.
The warning is not limited to non-believers.
4
Analyze the mechanism of blind tradition
When tradition dominates reason, it restricts freedom of thought and leads to imposing historical ideals onto present realities instead of learning objectively from history.
This explains how taqlid operates.
5
Identify the solution: disciplined education
The author describes Islamic education as one disciplined by the brakes of the mind, emphasizing the role of reason in producing liberated teachers and questioning students.
The goal is to remove obstacles to objectivity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولعلنا قد لاحظنا أن القرآن الكريم حين أدان اتباع الآباء على ذلك النحو من التشديد فإنما يرجع ذلك - فيما يرجع - إلى الجاذبية الشديدة الإغراء التي تربط الناس بميراث الآباء، بصرف النظر عن نوعية هذا الموروث. ودون أن تلفت إلى سنن الله وقوانينه الثابتة (۱) . ومن هنا فإن مشكلة النزعة الآبائية عند الكافرين؛ تعني جميع من يقع في مشكلة مخالفة السنن حتى وإن كان مسلماً، إذ المشكلة إنسانية بالدرجة الأولى، لا يستثنى منها المسلمون، كما قد يغفل بعضهم أو يتوهم حين يظن لنفسه مزية خاصة على غيره من الأمم، مع أن القرآن الكريم حين سفه تلك المعتقدات تضمن بطريق الإشارة خطورة أن يقع المسلمون في تقليد آبائهم على غير بصيرة . وبتعبير آخر فإنه إذا ما غلبت (٢) على العقل سطوة التقليد لموروث الآباء من التقاليد والعادات، وقيدت بذلك حريته في النظر، فإنه ينصرف عن النظر في مشكلة الحياة الواقعية ليتخذ من غابر الآباء، وغائب تاريخهم مادة للنظر ، يصوغ منها موازين وأحكاماً يسقطها على مشاكل الواقع في شيء من المثالية التاريخية على سبيل الانقياد لموروث الآباء، لا على سبيل البحث في وقائع التاريخ للاعتبار)) (۳). وعلى هذا الأساس يمكن وصف التربية الإسلامية بأنها تربية منضبطة بكوابح العقل. وفي ذلك انعكاس إيجابي على المعلم المتحرر والمتعلم المتسائل، والباحث الذي يحرص على إزالة عوائق الموضوعية في مسار أبحاثه العلمية.
Perhaps we have noted that when the Holy Quran condemned following fathers in such a strict manner, that is due - in what it goes back to - to the extremely attractive appeal that ties people to the inheritance of fathers, regardless of the quality of this inheritance. And without drawing attention to God's laws and constant decrees (1). Hence, the problem of ancestral bias among the disbelievers means all who fall into the problem of violating the laws even if he is a Muslim, for the problem is primarily human, from which Muslims are not excluded, as some of them may neglect or delude when they think they have a special advantage over other nations, while the Holy Quran, when it ridiculed those beliefs, included by way of indication the danger that Muslims fall into imitating their fathers without insight. In other words, if the tyranny of imitation of the inherited traditions and customs of fathers overcomes the mind (2), and thereby restricts its freedom of consideration, it turns away from looking at the real life problem to take from the past of fathers and their absent history a material for consideration, formulating from them criteria and judgments that it projects onto real problems in something of historical idealism in the way of submission to the inherited from fathers, not in the way of researching historical facts for moral lessons (3). On this basis, Islamic education can be described as an education disciplined by the brakes of the mind. And in that is a positive reflection on the liberated teacher and the questioning student, and the researcher who is keen to remove obstacles of objectivity in the course of his scientific research.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a critique of blind adherence to ancestral tradition. The author argues that the Quran's strong condemnation of following the ways of the ancestors is due to the powerful emotional attachment people have to their heritage, regardless of its correctness. This problem is universal; Muslims are not exempt, as they may also fall into imitating their ancestors without insight. The author then explains the mechanism: when tradition dominates reason, it restricts intellectual freedom and leads to a misguided approach where historical ideals are imposed on present realities rather than learning from history objectively. Finally, Islamic education is described as one that is disciplined by reason, emphasizing the importance of free thinking and objectivity for teachers, students, and researchers.

Key Terms
النزعة الآبائية
التقليد
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the Quran's condemnation of following ancestors is a warning for Muslims as well?
A) Muslims are superior to others.
B) The problem is universal and Muslims can also fall into blind imitation.
C) The Quran only addresses non-Muslims.
D) The Quran prohibits any form of tradition.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic condemnation of ancestral tradition is a universal human warning, and Muslims are not immune; Islamic education must be disciplined by reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a contemporary issue where some Muslims insist on following a particular scholarly opinion simply because it is the 'madhab of their fathers'. How would the author's argument apply? Identify the two possible errors: (a) assuming the tradition is correct without examination, (b) ignoring the universal human tendency to be attached to heritage.
?
Read Quran 2:170 (When it is said to them: Follow what Allah has revealed, they say: Rather we follow what we found our fathers doing). Explain how this verse illustrates the Quranic condemnation described in the lesson, and why the author says this applies to Muslims too.

Reason as the Path to Guidance in the Quran
Author presents Quranic verses showing reason as the path to guidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four intellectual faculties associated with Quranic guidance and explain how each is supported by a specific verse.

Core Idea
The Quran commands the use of reason for guidance in creed and law.

This lesson explores a key passage from the author that defines 'guidance' in the Quran as necessarily involving the rational faculties. By examining four Quranic verses, we see how thinking, remembering, reasoning, and reflecting are integral to understanding divine guidance. This establishes the organic unity between Islamic rulings and reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific definition of 'guidance'
Notice that the author narrows 'guidance' to 'doctrinal and legislative guidance based on the mind and its powers'. This is not all guidance, but that which relies on reason.
The author uses the term 'al-hidāya al-ʿaqdiyya wa al-tashrīʿiyya'.
2
List the four faculties of reason mentioned
The passage lists: tafakkur (thinking), tadhakkur (remembering), taʿaqqul (reasoning), and tadabbur (reflecting). These are the intellectual acts the Quran demands.
Each faculty is tied to a specific command in the verses.
3
Match each faculty to its Quranic verse
Find the verse that commands tafakkur (An-Nahl 16:44: 'laʿallahum yatafakkariīn'), tadhakkur (Al-Isra 17:41: 'liyadhkurū'), taʿaqqul (Yusuf 12:2: 'laʿallakum taʿqilūn'), and tadabbur (An-Nisa 4:82: 'afalā yatadabbarūna al-Qur'ān').
Each verse ends with an explicit call to use that faculty.
4
Synthesize the relationship between reason and revelation
The author concludes that there is organic unity (waḥda ʿuḍwiyya) between Islamic rulings and the mind, with no contradiction but mutual support.
This refutes the idea that reason and revelation oppose each other.

ه - العقل سبيل الهداية ونعني بالهداية هنا الهداية العقدية والتشريعية المعتمدة على العقل وقواه ممثلة في التفكير والتذكر والتعقل والتدبر وسواها: ﴿ بِالْبَيِّنَاتِ وَالزُّبُرِ وَأَنْزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الذِّكْرَ لِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِّلَ إِلَيْهِمْ وَلَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَفَكَّرُونَ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٤/١٦]. ﴿وَلَقَدْ صَرَّفْنَا فِي هَذَا الْقُرْآنِ لِيَذْكُرُوا ﴾ [الإسراء: ٤١/١٧]. إنا أَنزَلْنَاهُ قُرْآناً عَرَبِيًّا لَعَلَّكُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [يوسف: ٢/١٢]. ﴿أَفَلا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ الْقُرْآن وَلَوْ كانَ مِنْ عِندِ غَيْرِ اللَّهِ لَوَجَدُوا فِيهِ اخْتِلافاً كثيراً) [النساء: ٨٢/٤). إن هذا يشير إلى أن جانباً من الأحكام العقدية والتشريعية لا ينفصل عن العقل، بما يؤكد الوحدة العضوية بين منظومة أحكام الإسلام وبين العقل، وأن لا تعارض بينهما، بل تضافر ومؤازرة.
H - The mind is the path of guidance. By guidance here we mean doctrinal and legislative guidance based on the mind and its powers represented in thinking, remembering, rationalizing, reflecting, and others: 'With clear proofs and scriptures; and We revealed to you the Reminder that you may make clear to the people what was sent down to them and that they might reflect.' [An-Nahl 16:44]. 'And We have certainly diversified in this Quran that they may remember.' [Al-Isra 17:41]. 'Indeed, We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran that you might reason.' [Yusuf 12:2]. 'Then do they not reflect upon the Quran? If it had been from other than Allah, they would have found within it much contradiction.) [An-Nisa 4:82]. This indicates that a part of doctrinal and legislative rulings are not separate from the mind, confirming the organic unity between the system of Islamic rulings and the mind, and that there is no contradiction between them, but rather cooperation and support.

Commentary
This passage defines 'guidance' in the context of reason as guidance in matters of creed (ʿaqīda) and legislation (sharʿ) that depends on the intellectual faculties of thinking, remembering, reasoning, and reflecting. The author then cites four Quranic verses that explicitly call upon people to use these faculties: reflection on revelation (tafakkur), remembering God's signs (tadhakkur), reasoning through the Arabic Quran (taʿaqqul), and reflecting on the Quran's content (tadabbur). The conclusion is that Islamic rulings and reason are organically united, not contradictory, and they support each other.

Reason as a Tool to Verify Prophethood
Author explains reason's role in verifying prophethood and their complementarity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Quran uses rational reflection to verify prophethood and why reason and prophethood are complementary.

Core Idea
Reason and prophethood are complementary: reason verifies prophethood, and prophethood guides reason.

This passage from an Islamic education textbook cites two Quranic verses that invite rational reflection to ascertain the truth of Prophet Muhammad's message. The author concludes that prophethood does not cancel reason, nor can reason dispense with prophethood, establishing a foundational principle of Islamic thought: faith is not blind but rooted in rational verification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic invitation to reason
Find the two verses cited: Al-A'raf 7:184 and Al-An'am 6:50. Note the verbs used—'tafakkara' (to reflect) and 'ta'qilun' (to reason). What exactly are people asked to reflect upon in each verse?
In the first verse, reflection is on the Prophet's state—that he is not possessed. In the second, the Prophet himself invites reflection on the difference between the blind and the seeing.
2
Extract the two complementary claims
The author states: (1) Prophethood does not mean cancellation of the mind. (2) The mind cannot dispense with prophethood. Paraphrase each claim in your own words, showing how they balance each other.
3
Relate to the broader Islamic epistemological framework
How does this passage show that Islamic education is built on a balance between reason and revelation? Consider what would go wrong if one were neglected.
Without reason, faith becomes blind; without revelation, reason lacks guidance on ultimate truths.

6- The mind and prophethood: There is an invitation to use the mind to ascertain the truth of the prophethood of Muhammad - peace be upon him - and his message: 'Do they not reflect that their companion is not possessed? He is only a clear warner.' [Al-A'raf 7:184]. And say: 'I do not say to you that I possess the treasures of Allah, nor do I know the unseen, nor do I say to you that I am an angel. I only follow what is revealed to me. Say: Are the blind and the seeing equal? Then will you not give thought?' [Al-An'am 6:50]. This means that prophethood does not mean a cancellation of the mind, just as the mind cannot dispense with prophethood, and that is another important pillar of Islamic education.

This passage highlights the role of reason in verifying the prophethood of Muhammad. The Quran invites people to reflect (tafakkur) on the character and message of the Prophet to confirm he is not insane but a warner. The verse from Al-An'am shows the Prophet disclaiming any supernatural knowledge or power, emphasizing that he only follows revelation, and then asks a rhetorical question to prompt rational reflection. The conclusion is that prophethood and reason are complementary: prophethood does not negate reason, nor can reason be independent of prophethood. This is presented as a key foundation of Islamic education.

The Quranic Call to Use Reason
Author discusses the Quran's call to use intellect, citing verses and educational implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic verses that call for the use of reason and explain their educational implications for strengthening faith.

Core Idea
The Quran repeatedly demands the use of intellect as a path to faith.

The Quran does not merely present revelation as a given; it actively engages the reader's mind. In this lesson, we examine key verses that end with rhetorical questions like 'afala ta'qilun' (so will you not use reason?) and explore how they transform intellectual activity into an act of worship and a foundation for mature faith.

Guided Path
1
Locate the 'aql verses
Find the two verses at the beginning of the passage that contrast this world and the Hereafter, ending with a call to reason. Note the phrase 'afala ta'qilun'.
These verses are from Surat al-Qasas and Surat al-Ankabut.
2
Extract the educational implication
The author states that intellectual education strengthens faith in the unseen and moves the believer beyond childish concerns. Identify the key terms: 'tarbiyya 'aqliyya' and 'insan rashid' (mature person).
3
Analyze the rhetorical question
Why does the Quran use a rhetorical question? It demands reflection and personal accountability. Consider how this stimulates the reader to actively use reason rather than passively accept.
The question implies that failing to use reason is a deficiency.
4
Apply to learning from history
The passage later mentions the story of Lot as a 'clear sign for a people who use reason'. Reflect on how historical narratives in the Quran serve as intellectual lessons.

﴿وَما هَذِهِ الْحَيَاةُ الدُّنْيا إِلا لَهْوٌ وَلَعِبٌ وَإِنَّ الدَّارَ الْآخِرَةَ لَهِيَ الْحَيَوَانُ لَوْ كانُوا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٦٤/٢٩].
﴿وَما أُوتِيتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَمَتاعُ الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيا وَزِينَتَهَا وَمَا عِنْدَ اللهِ خَيْرٌ وَأَبْقَى أَفَلا تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [القصص: ٦٠/٢٨].
ومن الناحية التربوية فإن التربية العقلية تمثل عاملاً مساعداً في تعزيز الإيمان بالغيب عن طريق الوحي، كما تسهم في إخراج الإنسان المؤمن الذي لا يقف عند حدود الاهتمامات القريبة، التي قد تكون مناسبة لعالم الطفولة، الذي يسوغ فيه الفرح بالألعاب، ولكنه لا يناسب الإنسان الراشد، صاحب الاهتمامات الكبيرة، وصاحب النظرة الآفاقية، كما أن في هذه الآيات إرشاداً إلى الجمع بين الوسائل والغايات وإلى مرحلة الغايات والأهداف، وذلك من صلب اهتمامات النظام التربوي، والعمل التعليمي في المؤسسات التربوية.
العقل وقصص السابقين:
ودعا القرآن إلى إعمال العقل وأخذ العبرة من قصص السابقين، كما جاء ذلك عقب ذكر قصة لوط - على سبيل المثال - ﴿وَلَقَدْ تَرَكْنَا مِنْهَا آيَةً بَيِّنَةً لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٣٥/٢٩].
وفي ذلك تربية على التعلم بالعبرة، بوصفها أسلوباً تربوياً معتبراً في تدريس التربية الإسلامية.
- الحث على الفقه الكوني:
والفقه الكوني يمثل جماع الوظائف العقلية وأعمقها:
﴿قُلْ هُوَ الْقادِرُ عَلَى أَنْ يَبْعَثَ عَلَيْكُمْ عَذاباً مِنْ فَوْقِكُمْ أَوْ مِنْ تَحْتِ أَرْجُلِكُمْ أَوْ يَلْبِسَكُمْ شِيَعًا وَيُذِيقَ بَعْضَكُمْ بَأْسَ بَعْضِ انْظُرْ كَيْفَ نُصَرِّفُ الآياتِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ٦٥/٦]
وضعف أو انعدم الفقه الكوني أو الحضاري من علامات الضعف النفسي، ولذلك كان التشنيع والازدراء حقيقا بمن تردّى إلى هذا المستوى، سواء كان من اليهود أم من حلفائهم المنافقين، أم كان من المشركين
فقال عن اليهود: ﴿أَنتُمْ أَشَدُّ رَهْبَةً فِي صُدُورِهِمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُمْ قَوْمٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الحشر: ١٣/٥٩].
وقال عن المخلفين من المنافقين ... ﴿بَلْ كانُوا لا يَفْقَهُونَ إِلَّا قَلِيلاً﴾ [الفتح: ١٥/٤٨].
وقال عن المشركين: ﴿وَإِنْ يَكُنْ مِنْكُمْ مِنَةٌ يَغْلِبُوا أَلْفَاً مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِأَنَّهُمْ قَوْمٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الأنفال: ٦٥/٨].
وعلى ذلك فإنّ من أولويات الأهداف العامة للتربية الإسلامية العمل على إخراج الإنسان ذي الفقه الحضاري.
-١٠- الحث على الفقه المقاصدي:
والفقه المقاصدي كذلك يمثل دعوة عقلية للحث على النظر في أسرار ومقاصد الأحكام التشريعية ومن ذلك ... ﴿قَدْ بَيَّنَا لَكُمُ الآيَاتِ إِنْ كُنتُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [آل عمران: ١١٨/٣].
وقد وردت الآية في سياق حث العقل المسلم على تجنب اتخاذ بطانة من دون المؤمنين.
وحث على التفكر بعد ذكره لطائفة من الأحكام في موضوعات متفرقة ..... ﴿كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ اللهُ لَكُمُ الآيَاتِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَتَفَكَّرُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٦٦/٢].
أن ساق جملة من الأحكام المتعلقة بالأحوال الشخصية والعبادات جاء وبعد قوله تعالى في الحث على التعقل: ... ﴿كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ آيَاتِهِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٢/٢].
The third chapter: the second section - the intellect. "And what is the life of this world but amusement and play? But indeed, the home of the Hereafter is the true life, if they but knew." [Al-Ankabut: 64/29]. "And whatever thing you have been given – it is but the enjoyment of the worldly life and its adornment. And what is with Allah is better and more lasting; so will you not use reason?" [Al-Qasas: 60/28]. From an educational perspective, intellectual education represents a supportive factor in strengthening faith in the unseen through revelation, and it contributes to producing a believing person who does not stop at the limits of short-term interests, which may be suitable for the world of childhood, where joy in play is permissible, but it is not suitable for the mature person, the one with great interests and a far-reaching vision. Also, these verses guide to combining means and ends and to the stage of ends and goals, which is central to the concerns of the educational system and the educational work in educational institutions. The intellect and stories of the predecessors: The Quran called for using intellect and taking lessons from the stories of the predecessors, as it came after the mention of the story of Lot – for example – "And we left therein a clear sign for a people who use reason." [Al-Ankabut: 35/29]. In that is education through learning by example, as a considered educational method in teaching Islamic education. Encouragement of cosmic understanding (al-fiqh al-kawni): Cosmic understanding represents the sum of intellectual functions and their deepest: "Say, 'He is the [one] able to send upon you affliction from above you or from beneath your feet or to confuse you [so you become] sects and make you taste the violence of one another. Look how we diversify the signs that they might understand.'" [Al-An'am: 65/6]. Weakness or absence of cosmic or civilizational understanding is a sign of psychological weakness, and therefore scorn and disdain are deserved for those who descend to this level, whether from the Jews, their allies the hypocrites, or the polytheists. He said about the Jews: "You [believers] are more fearful within their breasts than Allah. That is because they are a people who do not understand." [Al-Hashr: 13/59]. He said about the laggards among the hypocrites: "But they do not understand except a little." [Al-Fath: 15/48]. He said about the polytheists: "If there are among you twenty steadfast, they will overcome two hundred of those who disbelieve, because they are a people who do not understand." [Al-Anfal: 65/8]. Accordingly, among the priorities of the general objectives of Islamic education is working to produce a person with civilizational understanding. And tenth – Encouragement of purposive understanding (al-fiqh al-maqasidi): Purposive understanding likewise represents an intellectual call to encourage reflection on the secrets and purposes of legislative rulings, among which is: "We have made clear to you the signs if you will use reason." [Al-Imran: 118/3]. This verse came in the context of urging the Muslim mind to avoid taking intimate friends from outside the believers. He also urged reflection after mentioning a group of rulings on various subjects: "Thus Allah makes clear to you the verses that you might reflect." [Al-Baqarah: 266/2]. He presented a set of rulings related to personal status and acts of worship, and after that came His statement urging reasoning: "Thus Allah makes clear His verses to you that you might use reason." [Al-Baqarah: 242/2].
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the role of the intellect ('aql) in the Quran from an educational perspective. The author begins by citing two Quranic verses that contrast the fleeting nature of this world with the permanence of the Hereafter, ending with the rhetorical question 'afala ta'qilun' (so will you not use reason?), establishing the Quran's call to rational thought. The author then explains that intellectual education strengthens faith in the unseen and matures the believer beyond childish preoccupations. Next, the passage discusses learning from the stories of past nations, citing the example of Lot's story, which the Quran calls a 'clear sign for a people who use reason'. This demonstrates that historical reflection is a tool for intellectual and spiritual growth. The author then introduces two key concepts: al-fiqh al-kawni (cosmic understanding) and al-fiqh al-maqasidi (purposive understanding). Cosmic understanding refers to comprehending the natural world and its phenomena as signs of God; the author cites a verse about God's power over creation and its diversity, concluding with 'la'allahum yafqahun' (that they might understand). He then warns that lack of such understanding is a sign of psychological weakness, citing verses condemning Jews, hypocrites, and polytheists for their failure to understand. Finally, purposive understanding involves reflecting on the wisdom and objectives behind divine legislation, illustrated by verses urging believers to use reason and reflection when encountering legal rulings. The passage overall argues that the Quran consistently promotes intellectual engagement across multiple domains to deepen faith and cultivate a mature, discerning believer.

التربية العقلية

The Quran's repeated call to use reason ('aql) is not optional; it is an essential component of Islamic education that matures the believer and deepens faith.

Cosmic Understanding (al-fiqh al-kawni) in the Quran
Author discusses cosmic understanding as a deep intellectual function and its opposite as a sign of weakness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-fiqh al-kawni, identify its Quranic evidence, and explain its role as a sign of psychological and faith strength.

Core Idea
Understanding the universe as divine signs is the deepest intellectual function.

The Quran does not only call to reason about texts; it urges reflection on the natural world and history. In this lesson, we explore the concept of al-fiqh al-kawni (cosmic understanding) as presented by the author, who argues that lacking this understanding is a sign of weakness. We will analyze the verses cited and their educational implications.

Guided Path
1
Define al-fiqh al-kawni
From the passage, cosmic understanding is described as 'the sum of intellectual functions and their deepest'. Write a definition in your own words.
It refers to understanding natural phenomena and historical events as signs (ayat) of Allah.
2
Find the Quranic evidence
Locate the verse from Surat al-An'am (6:65) that the author cites. Note how it ends with 'la'allahum yafqahun' (that they might understand).
3
Analyze the author's claim about its absence
The author says weakness or absence of this understanding is a sign of psychological weakness. List the three groups condemned for lacking it: Jews, hypocrites, and polytheists. What do the verses say about them?
The verses are from Al-Hashr 59:13, Al-Fath 48:15, Al-Anfal 8:65.
4
Connect to educational objective
The author concludes that one priority of Islamic education is to produce a person with civilizational understanding (figh hadari). Reflect on how this might apply to teaching science or history in an Islamic context.
