الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
﴿وَما هَذِهِ الْحَيَاةُ الدُّنْيا إِلا لَهْوٌ وَلَعِبٌ وَإِنَّ الدَّارَ الْآخِرَةَ لَهِيَ الْحَيَوَانُ لَوْ كانُوا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٦٤/٢٩].
﴿وَما أُوتِيتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَمَتاعُ الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيا وَزِينَتَهَا وَمَا عِنْدَ اللهِ خَيْرٌ وَأَبْقَى أَفَلا تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [القصص: ٦٠/٢٨].
ومن الناحية التربوية فإن التربية العقلية تمثل عاملاً مساعداً في تعزيز الإيمان بالغيب عن طريق الوحي، كما تسهم في إخراج الإنسان المؤمن الذي لا يقف عند حدود الاهتمامات القريبة، التي قد تكون مناسبة لعالم الطفولة، الذي يسوغ فيه الفرح بالألعاب، ولكنه لا يناسب الإنسان الراشد، صاحب الاهتمامات الكبيرة، وصاحب النظرة الآفاقية، كما أن في هذه الآيات إرشاداً إلى الجمع بين الوسائل والغايات وإلى مرحلة الغايات والأهداف، وذلك من صلب اهتمامات النظام التربوي، والعمل التعليمي في المؤسسات التربوية.
العقل وقصص السابقين:
ودعا القرآن إلى إعمال العقل وأخذ العبرة من قصص السابقين، كما جاء ذلك عقب ذكر قصة لوط - على سبيل المثال - ﴿وَلَقَدْ تَرَكْنَا مِنْهَا آيَةً بَيِّنَةً لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٣٥/٢٩].
وفي ذلك تربية على التعلم بالعبرة، بوصفها أسلوباً تربوياً معتبراً في تدريس التربية الإسلامية.
- الحث على الفقه الكوني:
والفقه الكوني يمثل جماع الوظائف العقلية وأعمقها:
﴿قُلْ هُوَ الْقادِرُ عَلَى أَنْ يَبْعَثَ عَلَيْكُمْ عَذاباً مِنْ فَوْقِكُمْ أَوْ مِنْ تَحْتِ أَرْجُلِكُمْ أَوْ يَلْبِسَكُمْ شِيَعًا وَيُذِيقَ بَعْضَكُمْ بَأْسَ بَعْضِ انْظُرْ كَيْفَ نُصَرِّفُ الآياتِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ٦٥/٦]
وضعف أو انعدم الفقه الكوني أو الحضاري من علامات الضعف النفسي، ولذلك كان التشنيع والازدراء حقيقا بمن تردّى إلى هذا المستوى، سواء كان من اليهود أم من حلفائهم المنافقين، أم كان من المشركين
فقال عن اليهود: ﴿أَنتُمْ أَشَدُّ رَهْبَةً فِي صُدُورِهِمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُمْ قَوْمٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الحشر: ١٣/٥٩].
وقال عن المخلفين من المنافقين ... ﴿بَلْ كانُوا لا يَفْقَهُونَ إِلَّا قَلِيلاً﴾ [الفتح: ١٥/٤٨].
وقال عن المشركين: ﴿وَإِنْ يَكُنْ مِنْكُمْ مِنَةٌ يَغْلِبُوا أَلْفَاً مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِأَنَّهُمْ قَوْمٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الأنفال: ٦٥/٨].
وعلى ذلك فإنّ من أولويات الأهداف العامة للتربية الإسلامية العمل على إخراج الإنسان ذي الفقه الحضاري.
-١٠- الحث على الفقه المقاصدي:
والفقه المقاصدي كذلك يمثل دعوة عقلية للحث على النظر في أسرار ومقاصد الأحكام التشريعية ومن ذلك ... ﴿قَدْ بَيَّنَا لَكُمُ الآيَاتِ إِنْ كُنتُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [آل عمران: ١١٨/٣].
وقد وردت الآية في سياق حث العقل المسلم على تجنب اتخاذ بطانة من دون المؤمنين.
وحث على التفكر بعد ذكره لطائفة من الأحكام في موضوعات متفرقة ..... ﴿كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ اللهُ لَكُمُ الآيَاتِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَتَفَكَّرُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٦٦/٢].
أن ساق جملة من الأحكام المتعلقة بالأحوال الشخصية والعبادات جاء وبعد قوله تعالى في الحث على التعقل: ... ﴿كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ آيَاتِهِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٢/٢].
The third chapter: the second section - the intellect. "And what is the life of this world but amusement and play? But indeed, the home of the Hereafter is the true life, if they but knew." [Al-Ankabut: 64/29]. "And whatever thing you have been given – it is but the enjoyment of the worldly life and its adornment. And what is with Allah is better and more lasting; so will you not use reason?" [Al-Qasas: 60/28]. From an educational perspective, intellectual education represents a supportive factor in strengthening faith in the unseen through revelation, and it contributes to producing a believing person who does not stop at the limits of short-term interests, which may be suitable for the world of childhood, where joy in play is permissible, but it is not suitable for the mature person, the one with great interests and a far-reaching vision. Also, these verses guide to combining means and ends and to the stage of ends and goals, which is central to the concerns of the educational system and the educational work in educational institutions. The intellect and stories of the predecessors: The Quran called for using intellect and taking lessons from the stories of the predecessors, as it came after the mention of the story of Lot – for example – "And we left therein a clear sign for a people who use reason." [Al-Ankabut: 35/29]. In that is education through learning by example, as a considered educational method in teaching Islamic education. Encouragement of cosmic understanding (al-fiqh al-kawni): Cosmic understanding represents the sum of intellectual functions and their deepest: "Say, 'He is the [one] able to send upon you affliction from above you or from beneath your feet or to confuse you [so you become] sects and make you taste the violence of one another. Look how we diversify the signs that they might understand.'" [Al-An'am: 65/6]. Weakness or absence of cosmic or civilizational understanding is a sign of psychological weakness, and therefore scorn and disdain are deserved for those who descend to this level, whether from the Jews, their allies the hypocrites, or the polytheists. He said about the Jews: "You [believers] are more fearful within their breasts than Allah. That is because they are a people who do not understand." [Al-Hashr: 13/59]. He said about the laggards among the hypocrites: "But they do not understand except a little." [Al-Fath: 15/48]. He said about the polytheists: "If there are among you twenty steadfast, they will overcome two hundred of those who disbelieve, because they are a people who do not understand." [Al-Anfal: 65/8]. Accordingly, among the priorities of the general objectives of Islamic education is working to produce a person with civilizational understanding. And tenth – Encouragement of purposive understanding (al-fiqh al-maqasidi): Purposive understanding likewise represents an intellectual call to encourage reflection on the secrets and purposes of legislative rulings, among which is: "We have made clear to you the signs if you will use reason." [Al-Imran: 118/3]. This verse came in the context of urging the Muslim mind to avoid taking intimate friends from outside the believers. He also urged reflection after mentioning a group of rulings on various subjects: "Thus Allah makes clear to you the verses that you might reflect." [Al-Baqarah: 266/2]. He presented a set of rulings related to personal status and acts of worship, and after that came His statement urging reasoning: "Thus Allah makes clear His verses to you that you might use reason." [Al-Baqarah: 242/2].
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the role of the intellect ('aql) in the Quran from an educational perspective. The author begins by citing two Quranic verses that contrast the fleeting nature of this world with the permanence of the Hereafter, ending with the rhetorical question 'afala ta'qilun' (so will you not use reason?), establishing the Quran's call to rational thought. The author then explains that intellectual education strengthens faith in the unseen and matures the believer beyond childish preoccupations. Next, the passage discusses learning from the stories of past nations, citing the example of Lot's story, which the Quran calls a 'clear sign for a people who use reason'. This demonstrates that historical reflection is a tool for intellectual and spiritual growth. The author then introduces two key concepts: al-fiqh al-kawni (cosmic understanding) and al-fiqh al-maqasidi (purposive understanding). Cosmic understanding refers to comprehending the natural world and its phenomena as signs of God; the author cites a verse about God's power over creation and its diversity, concluding with 'la'allahum yafqahun' (that they might understand). He then warns that lack of such understanding is a sign of psychological weakness, citing verses condemning Jews, hypocrites, and polytheists for their failure to understand. Finally, purposive understanding involves reflecting on the wisdom and objectives behind divine legislation, illustrated by verses urging believers to use reason and reflection when encountering legal rulings. The passage overall argues that the Quran consistently promotes intellectual engagement across multiple domains to deepen faith and cultivate a mature, discerning believer.

Key Terms
الفقه الكوني
الفقه الحضاري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the absence of cosmic understanding indicate?
A) A person is not a Muslim.
B) A sign of psychological weakness and a cause for divine scorn.
C) A person needs more religious education.
D) It is not important; only fiqh matters.

Key Takeaway
Al-fiqh al-kawni is the deepest intellectual function, and its absence is a sign of weakness; Islamic education must cultivate it to produce a person with civilizational understanding.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the Quranic verse from Al-An'am (6:65) as a model, write a short lesson plan for high school students that teaches them to see natural disasters as signs of Allah's power and a call to reflection.
?
Identify a historical event mentioned in the Quran (e.g., the destruction of 'Ad or Thamud) and explain how it can be used to teach al-fiqh al-kawni in an Islamic history class.

intermediate
10 min
Purposive Understanding (al-fiqh al-maqasidi) in the Quran
Author discusses purposive understanding as an intellectual call to reflect on the purposes of legal rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-fiqh al-maqasidi, identify its Quranic basis, and explain its role in deepening one's understanding of Islamic rulings.

Core Idea
Reflecting on the purposes behind rulings is an intellectual act of worship.

The Quran does not merely present laws; it invites believers to reflect on their wisdom and purposes. In this lesson, we examine the concept of al-fiqh al-maqasidi (purposive understanding) as presented by the author, who cites verses that urge reason and reflection in the context of legal rulings. This approach trains the Muslim mind to go beyond surface-level obedience.

Guided Path
1
Define al-fiqh al-maqasidi
From the passage, it is described as 'an intellectual call to encourage reflection on the secrets and purposes of legislative rulings'. Write a definition in your own words.
The term 'maqasid' refers to objectives or purposes of Shariah.
2
Find the Quranic evidence
Locate the three verses cited: Al-Imran 3:118, Al-Baqarah 2:266, and Al-Baqarah 2:242. Notice how they end with 'la'allahum ta'qilun' or 'tatafakkarun'.
3
Analyze the context of each verse
The author explains that the first verse (Al-Imran 3:118) came in the context of avoiding intimate friends from outside the faith – an ethical ruling. The second (Al-Baqarah 2:266) came after a set of rulings on charity. The third (Al-Baqarah 2:242) came after family and worship rulings. Reflect on why the Quran adds a call to reason after giving laws.
This shows that understanding the wisdom behind rulings is an integral part of obedience.
4
Apply to modern fiqh issues
Consider a contemporary issue like organ donation. How would applying al-fiqh al-maqasidi help a Muslim scholar derive a ruling that is faithful to the purposes of Shariah?

والفقه المقاصدي كذلك يمثل دعوة عقلية للحث على النظر في أسرار ومقاصد الأحكام التشريعية ومن ذلك ... ﴿قَدْ بَيَّنَا لَكُمُ الآيَاتِ إِنْ كُنتُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [آل عمران: ١١٨/٣].
وقد وردت الآية في سياق حث العقل المسلم على تجنب اتخاذ بطانة من دون المؤمنين.
وحث على التفكر بعد ذكره لطائفة من الأحكام في موضوعات متفرقة ..... ﴿كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ اللهُ لَكُمُ الآيَاتِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَتَفَكَّرُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٦٦/٢].
أن ساق جملة من الأحكام المتعلقة بالأحوال الشخصية والعبادات جاء وبعد قوله تعالى في الحث على التعقل: ... ﴿كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ آيَاتِهِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٢/٢].

[Al-Ankabut: 64/29]. "And whatever thing you have been given – it is but the enjoyment of the worldly life and its adornment. And what is with Allah is better and more lasting; so will you not use reason?" [Al-Qasas: 60/28]. Also, these verses guide to combining means and ends and to the stage of ends and goals, which is central to the concerns of the educational system and the educational work in educational institutions. The intellect and stories of the predecessors: The Quran called for using intellect and taking lessons from the stories of the predecessors, as it came after the mention of the story of Lot – for example – "And we left therein a clear sign for a people who use reason." [Al-Ankabut: 35/29]. In that is education through learning by example, as a considered educational method in teaching Islamic education. Look how we diversify the signs that they might understand.'" [Al-An'am: 65/6]. Weakness or absence of cosmic or civilizational understanding is a sign of psychological weakness, and therefore scorn and disdain are deserved for those who descend to this level, whether from the Jews, their allies the hypocrites, or the polytheists. He said about the Jews: "You [believers] are more fearful within their breasts than Allah. That is because they are a people who do not understand." [Al-Hashr: 13/59]. He said about the laggards among the hypocrites: "But they do not understand except a little." [Al-Fath: 15/48]. He said about the polytheists: "If there are among you twenty steadfast, they will overcome two hundred of those who disbelieve, because they are a people who do not understand." [Al-Anfal: 65/8]. Accordingly, among the priorities of the general objectives of Islamic education is working to produce a person with civilizational understanding. And tenth – Encouragement of purposive understanding (al-fiqh al-maqasidi): Purposive understanding likewise represents an intellectual call to encourage reflection on the secrets and purposes of legislative rulings, among which is: "We have made clear to you the signs if you will use reason." [Al-Imran: 118/3]. This verse came in the context of urging the Muslim mind to avoid taking intimate friends from outside the believers. He also urged reflection after mentioning a group of rulings on various subjects: "Thus Allah makes clear to you the verses that you might reflect." [Al-Baqarah: 266/2]. He presented a set of rulings related to personal status and acts of worship, and after that came His statement urging reasoning: "Thus Allah makes clear His verses to you that you might use reason." [Al-Baqarah: 242/2].

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the role of the intellect ('aql) in the Quran from an educational perspective. The author begins by citing two Quranic verses that contrast the fleeting nature of this world with the permanence of the Hereafter, ending with the rhetorical question 'afala ta'qilun' (so will you not use reason?), establishing the Quran's call to rational thought. The author then explains that intellectual education strengthens faith in the unseen and matures the believer beyond childish preoccupations. Next, the passage discusses learning from the stories of past nations, citing the example of Lot's story, which the Quran calls a 'clear sign for a people who use reason'. This demonstrates that historical reflection is a tool for intellectual and spiritual growth. The author then introduces two key concepts: al-fiqh al-kawni (cosmic understanding) and al-fiqh al-maqasidi (purposive understanding). Cosmic understanding refers to comprehending the natural world and its phenomena as signs of God; the author cites a verse about God's power over creation and its diversity, concluding with 'la'allahum yafqahun' (that they might understand). He then warns that lack of such understanding is a sign of psychological weakness, citing verses condemning Jews, hypocrites, and polytheists for their failure to understand. Finally, purposive understanding involves reflecting on the wisdom and objectives behind divine legislation, illustrated by verses urging believers to use reason and reflection when encountering legal rulings. The passage overall argues that the Quran consistently promotes intellectual engagement across multiple domains to deepen faith and cultivate a mature, discerning believer.

مقاصد الأحكام

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the role of al-fiqh al-maqasidi?
A) To memorize the detailed rulings of fiqh.
B) To encourage reflection on the secrets and purposes behind legislative rulings.
C) To replace the need for following Islamic law with general principles.
D) To focus only on the literal text of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Al-fiqh al-maqasidi is a Quranically mandated intellectual exercise that deepens faith by connecting believers to the wisdom behind divine laws.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take one Islamic ruling, such as the prohibition of alcohol. Write a short paragraph explaining the maqasid (purposes) behind this ruling and how understanding them can help a believer obey more thoughtfully.
?
Using the method of al-fiqh al-maqasidi, analyze the wisdom behind the ruling of 'iddah (waiting period) after divorce as mentioned in Surah Al-Baqarah. How does reflecting on its purposes deepen one's appreciation of Shariah?

The Role of Intellect in Islamic Rulings
Author discusses the importance of intellect and its connection to fiqh al-maqasidi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic pattern of urging intellectual acts after legal rulings and explain how this supports the principle of fiqh al-maqasidi.

Core Idea
The Quran repeatedly commands the use of intellect to understand the purposes behind its rulings.

The author demonstrates that Islamic education must prioritize the development of the intellect (al-'aql) as a tool for understanding the higher purposes (maqasid) of Shari'ah. Through a survey of Quranic verses, we see a consistent pattern: after each set of legal instructions, the Quran calls for reflection, reasoning, and understanding. This lesson will guide you through that pattern and its implications for Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of fiqh emphasized
The author highlights 'al-fiqh al-kawni' (civilizational jurisprudence) and 'al-fiqh al-maqasidi' (purposive jurisprudence) as priorities. Notice how each is linked to the use of intellect.
2
Trace the Quranic pattern of intellectual calls
Go through each set of rulings (e.g., marriage with polytheists, divorce, etc.) and identify the specific intellectual act urged: tafakkur (reflection), ta'aqqul (reasoning), tadhakkur (remembrance), or 'ilm (knowing).
The passage lists these sequentially; extract each one.
3
Connect the pattern to fiqh al-maqasidi
Explain why this pattern implies that understanding the purposes (maqasid) behind rulings is essential. The intellectual acts are not random; they are meant to uncover the wisdom behind the law.
The author calls this an 'intellectual call to contemplate the secrets and purposes of legislative rulings.'
4
Extract the educational implication
According to the author, what must change in curricula and teaching methods? Focus on the criticism of 'information padding' and the need for 'functionality.'

Weakness or absence of cosmic or civilizational jurisprudence is a sign of psychological weakness, and therefore denigration and contempt are deserved by whoever falls to this level, whether they are Jews, their hypocritical allies, or polytheists. He said about the Jews: 'You are more fearful in their hearts than Allah, that is because they are a people who do not understand.' [Hashr 59:13]. And he said about the hypocrites who lagged behind: '... but they did not understand except a little' [Fath 48:15]. And he said about the polytheists: 'And if there are among you a [؟] they will overcome a thousand of those who disbelieve because they are a people who do not understand' [Anfal 8:65]. Accordingly, one of the priorities of the general objectives of Islamic education is to bring forth a person with civilizational jurisprudence. -10- Encouragement of purposive jurisprudence: And purposive jurisprudence likewise represents an intellectual call to encourage consideration of the secrets and purposes of legislative rulings. Among that is: 'We have made clear to you the signs if you will reason' [Aal Imran 3:118]. And the verse came in the context of urging the Muslim intellect to avoid taking intimates from outside the believers. And after indicating that there are limited benefits in wine and gambling, but the dangers and harms are greater, He encouraged the intellect to reflect: '... Thus Allah makes clear to you the verses that you might reflect' [Baqara 2:219]. And after mentioning the ruling of marriage with polytheists came the encouragement to remember: 'And He makes clear His signs to the people that they might remember' [Baqara 2:221]. And after mentioning divorce came the encouragement to learn: '... And these are the limits of Allah which He makes clear to a people who know' [Baqara 2:230]. And after mentioning a group of social and educational rulings such as children asking permission, how the elderly woman should dress, and some etiquette of food and visits, He encouraged reasoning in the form of hope: '... that you might reason' [Nur 24:61]. Indeed, this clearly indicates the importance of including purposive jurisprudence as an important part of the content of Islamic education in its judgment of various phenomena. It is also understood from this the necessity of training learners in skills of deduction and comparison between texts, their causes and purposes. This has its reflection on educational work such that it is characterized by functionality, meaning the connection of what the learner learns to his interests, problems, and aspirations, and to the interests, problems, and hopes of his society and nation. And it has its reflection on the curricula and courses that children struggle to carry due to the accumulation of information padding resulting from the absence of connection to purposes and objectives. -1-1 Elevating the status of the intelligent: And if the previous verses encouraged the use and employment of intellects, then the following verses state that those who benefit from their intellects are characterized - automatically -
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the concept of al-'aql (intellect) and its central role in Islamic education. It begins by linking the weakness of 'al-fiqh al-kawani' (cosmic or civilizational understanding) to psychological weakness, citing Quranic verses that criticize those who lack understanding (la yafqahoon) — specifically Jews, hypocrites, and polytheists. The author argues that one of the primary goals of Islamic education is to produce individuals with civilizational fiqh. The second major point is the encouragement of 'al-fiqh al-maqasidi' (purposive jurisprudence), which is described as an intellectual call to contemplate the secrets and purposes behind legal rulings. The author then presents numerous Quranic verses that urge the use of intellect after the mention of specific rulings: after warning about taking disbelievers as intimates (Aal Imran 3:118), after rulings on personal status and worship (Baqara 2:242), after discussing the harms of wine and gambling (Baqara 2:219), after marriage with polytheists (Baqara 2:221), after divorce (Baqara 2:230), and after social and educational rulings (Nur 24:61). The pattern is clear: each set of legal instructions is followed by a call to reason, reflect, remember, know, or understand. The author concludes that this demonstrates the importance of including maqasid (purposes) in Islamic educational content, and implies the need to train students in deductive reasoning and comparison between texts, their causes and purposes. This approach makes education functional, connecting learning to the interests and problems of the individual and society. The passage ends with the start of a new point about elevating the status of those who use their intellects, suggesting that the intelligent are automatically described positively in the following verses.

The Intellect's Domain and the Objection from Revelation's Supremacy
Author asks about the intellect's realm and presents an objection about its role in the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the dialectical exchange about the intellect's role in knowing the unseen and identify the author's initial response to the objection.

Core Idea
Intellect extends to the unseen, but revelation remains the sovereign path to ghayb.

The author begins by asking a fundamental question: in which world does the intellect operate—the visible or the unseen? He first asserts the intellect's vast reach, but then anticipates an objection that seems to contradict the primacy of revelation. Let's trace this dialectical opening and see how the author begins his answer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's initial claim
Read the author's statement: 'the intellect is a vast faculty... its cognitive role extends beyond the visible world to the unseen world.' This is the claim being put forward.
Notice the claim includes two avenues: through the visible world itself and through the unseen in inferring belief in Allah.
2
Locate the objection (mu'tarid)
The author writes 'but perhaps someone might object...' The objection is based on a previously established point: revelation is the sole path to knowledge of the unseen, not the intellect or senses.
This objection creates a tension: how can the intellect have a role if revelation is exclusive?
3
Note the author's immediate concession
The author does not reject the objection outright. Instead, he 'sees the necessity of reminding' of prior points. He acknowledges the established principle.
This shows the author is engaging dialectically, not simply dismissing the counterpoint.
4
Extract the author's initial response
The author recalls that there are evidences (dala'il) that testify to belief in Allah. These come in two types: spontaneous results of faith and signs from the horizons (cosmic evidence). This suggests the intellect can engage these evidences.
The passage cuts off, so the full response is incomplete, but the direction is clear: the intellect's role is not independent but works with data that revelation also confirms.

طبيعة عمل العقل
هي إذا كان العقل على ذلك النحو من الأهمية فما طبيعة عمله؟ بمعنى في أي عالم يقوم العقل بوظائفه : أفي عالم الغيب أم الشهادة؟ وكيف يتجسد دوره في الوحي؟ وكيف يتجسد دور الوحي فيه؟ وحتى يمكننا تحديد الإجابة عن هذين السؤالين يحسن بنا أن ندرك ابتداءً أن العقل ملكة واسعة تجعله يقف وراء الحواس، باعتباره العنصر الحقيقي في عملية الإدراك أو المعرفة العقلية والعلمية، ولذلك فإن دوره المعرفي يتعدى عالم الشهادة إلى عالم الغيب، سواء كان ذلك عن طريق عالم الشهادة نفسه، أم كان عن طريق عالم الغيب في الاستدلال على الإيمان بالله تعالى (۱) - على سبيل المثال - ولكن رُبَّ قائل يعترض على هذا في ضوء ما تم تقريره عند الحديث عن ميدان المعرفة في عالم الغيب، وأن طريقها ليس العقل، كما أنه ليس الحواس، بل الوحي سبيل معرفتها الوحيد. وهنا نرى ضرورة التذكير بما سبقت الإشارة إليه عند الحديث عن ميدان المعرفة في عالم الغيب أيضاً من أن ثمة دلائل تشهد لهذا الإيمان سواء تلك التي تأتي نتائج تلقائية للإيمان بالله تعالى أو تلك التي تبرز في ميداني الآفاق
The Nature of the Intellect's Operation. If the intellect is of such importance, what is the nature of its operation? That is, in which realm does the intellect perform its functions: in the realm of the unseen or the visible? And how is its role embodied in revelation? And how is the role of revelation embodied in it? In order to determine the answer to these two questions, it is appropriate that we first realize that the intellect is a vast faculty that places it behind the senses, as the real element in the process of perception or intellectual and scientific knowledge. Therefore, its cognitive role extends beyond the visible world to the unseen world, whether that is through the visible world itself, or through the unseen world in inferring belief in Allah the Exalted (1) - for example - but perhaps someone might object to this in light of what has been established when discussing the field of knowledge of the unseen, and that its path is not the intellect, nor the senses, but rather revelation is its sole means of knowledge. Here we see the necessity of reminding what was previously indicated when discussing the field of knowledge of the unseen as well: that there are evidences that testify to this belief, whether those that come as spontaneous results of belief in Allah the Exalted or those that appear in the realms of the horizons...
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a discussion on the nature of the intellect's operation. The author poses key questions: In which realm does the intellect function—the unseen (ghayb) or the visible (shahada)? And how do intellect and revelation interact? The author first asserts that the intellect is a vast faculty that stands behind the senses, being the real element in perception and knowledge. Consequently, its role extends from the visible world to the unseen world, either through inference from the visible or directly in the unseen, for example in deducing faith in Allah. However, the author anticipates an objection: earlier it was established that the sole path to knowledge of the unseen is revelation, not intellect or senses. The author then begins to respond by recalling that there are evidences for faith that come either as spontaneous results of belief or from the 'horizons' (a reference to cosmic signs). The passage is cut off, so the full response is incomplete, but the dialectical structure is clear: question, initial claim, objection, and beginning of answer.

Distinction between Tafakkur and Tafkeer
Author defines tafakkur and tafkeer using classical and modern sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish tafakkur from tafkeer by identifying their key features: scope, involvement of the heart, and relation to the intellect.

Core Idea
Tafakkur is uniquely human and heart-centered; tafkeer is a broader cognitive process.

In this passage, the author contrasts two forms of thinking: tafakkur (contemplation) defined by al-Raghib al-Isfahani, and tafkeer (thinking) defined by modern psychologists. The distinction is crucial for understanding the Quranic call to reflection, which involves both mind and heart.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definitions
Find al-Isfahani's definition of tafakkur and the modern definitions of tafkeer by Humphrey and Bartlett.
The definitions are given in the first part of the passage.
2
Analyze tafakkur features
Note that tafakkur is movement of the rational power, according to the intellect, for humans only, and involves the heart (emotional aspect).
Al-Isfahani's definition explicitly excludes animals and includes the heart.
3
Analyze tafkeer features
Note that tafkeer occurs in any organic being facing a problem, involves expanding evidence and filling gaps, is purely mental, and takes forms like critical and creative thinking.
Humphrey and Bartlett's definitions allow for animal cognition and are purely cognitive.
4
Compare and contrast
Contrast the heart involvement and human exclusivity of tafakkur with the broader, purely mental nature of tafkeer.
This distinction shows that tafakkur is a spiritually significant act, while tafkeer is a cognitive tool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
ثالثاً: التفكر
لعل من المناسب كذلك التمييز بين التفكر والتفكير أما الأول فيعرفه الراغب الأصفهاني بأنه جولان تلك القوة بحسب نظر العقل، وذلك للإنسان دون الحيوان ولايقال إلا فيما يمكن أن يحصل له صورة في القلب. وكأنه بهذا المعنى يشمل جوانب وجدانية إلى جانب العقلية. (١)
أما التفكير فيعرفه (همفري): بأنه ما يحدث في خبرة الكائن العضوي، سواء كان إنساناً أم حيواناً، حين يواجه مشكلة، أو يتعرف عليها، أو يسعى لحلها (٢) ويعرفه (بارتلت): بأنه عملية توسيع الدليل على النحو الذي يلائمه، بحيث يتم ملء الفجوات فيه. ويتم هذا بالانتقال في خطوات متتابعة مترابطة يمكن التعبير عنها في حينها، أو يتم التعبير عنها فيما بعد) (٣). وحسب بارتلت فإن أول شرط لحدوث عملية التفكير هو نقصان المعلومات التي بين أيدينا، تأتي الصعوبة، أو تبرز المشكلة (٤) . وهذا - في الواقع - مظهر عقلي خالص. وقد غدا اليوم أسلوباً فاعلاً في عملية التعلم، ويتخذ صوراً عدة لعل أبرزها: التفكير الناقد، والتفكير الإبداعي، وهما من الأساليب المعوّل عليها في عملية التعلم الذاتي. وفي مجال مناهج البحث ثمة تشديد على التزام منهج التفكير العلمي وبصرف النظر عن مدى الاتفاق أو الاختلاف حول مصطلح (التفكير العلمي من مدرسة لأخرى فما يهمنا هنا هو إجراء عملية التفكير على نحو يحقق الوصول إلى الهدف المنشود بعيداً عن الاعتباط وتحكيم العواطف المجردة.
(١) الراغب الأصفهاني، المفردات في غريب القرآن، ٣٨٤.
(٢) سيد أحمد عثمان وفؤاد أبو حطب التفكير دراسات نفسية، ٢٠٠.
(٣) المرجع السابق، ۲۰۰.
(٤) المرجع نفسه، ۲۰۰.

والعلاقة بين وظيفة العقل وعملية التفكير عضوية إذ التفكير واحد من قوى العقل - كما أشرنا من قبل - والذين لا يعقلون لا ينفعهم تفكيرهم. لذلك لا يراهم القرآن جديرين بصفة الإنسانية واعتبرهم في عداد الدواب وما هو أدنى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيراً مِنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنْسِ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌ لا يَسْمَعُونَ بِها أُولَئِكَ كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْغَافِلُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٧٩/٧].
أَمْ تَحْسَبُ أَنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ يَسْمَعُونَ أَوْ يَعْقِلُونَ إِنْ هُمْ إِلا كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ سَبِيلاً [الفرقان: ٤٤/٢٥].
ونخبة القول في هذا الصدد يلخصه الحارث المحاسبي بقوله: (ولا غناء بالعبد عن النظر والتفكر والتذكر ليكثر اعتباره ويزيد في علمه، ويعلو في الفضل فمن قل تفكره قل اعتباره و من قل اعتباره قل علمه، ومـن قـل علـمـه كثر جهله، وبان،نقصه، ولم يجد طعم البر، ولا برد اليقين، ولا روح الحكمة وماذا بلغ مَنْ درس العلم بلسانه، وحفظ الحروفه بقلبه، وأضرب عن النظر ما أقرّ به في حياته من حياة البهائم التي لا تعرف إلا ما باشرته بجوارحها ! لكن المتذكر الناظر فيما يسمع، المتدبّر لما علم المتوهم لما به أمر الطالب لنهاية حدود العلم الغائص والمبصر لما يصلحه وما يفسده القوي على عصيان طبائعه النازعة إلى ما يهلكه، والمخالف لشهواته التي ترديه العارف بعواقب الأمور، وبما يحدث في غابر الدهور، وما حدث منه. الهائب أمر ربه المؤثر لذة عقله على لذة هواه لذة الحكماء في عقولهم ولذة الجهال والبهائم في شهواتهم. أي سرور بعد سرور العلم، وروح اليقين، وعظيم المعرفة، وكثرة الصواب، والظفر الذي لا يثبت ولا ينال إلا بحسن النظر، وطول التذكر، وتكرار الفكر والتقديم في التدبير)(١).
(١) الحارث المحاسبي، شرف العقل وما هيته ٤٥-٤٦.
Chapter Three: Second Section - The Intellect
Third: Tafakkur (Contemplation)
It may be appropriate as well to distinguish between tafakkur and tafkeer. As for the first, al-Raghib al-Isfahani defines it as 'the movement of that power according to the view of the intellect, and that is for humans not animals, and it is only said regarding what can obtain a form in the heart.' It seems that in this meaning it includes emotional aspects alongside intellectual ones.
As for tafkeer, Humphrey defines it as 'what occurs in the experience of an organic being, whether human or animal, when it faces a problem, or recognizes it, or seeks to solve it.' And Bartlett defines it as 'the process of expanding the evidence in a manner that suits it, so that the gaps in it are filled. This is done by moving in successive interrelated steps that can be expressed at the time, or expressed later.' According to Bartlett, the first condition for the occurrence of the thinking process is the deficiency of information in our hands, then difficulty comes or the problem emerges. This - in reality - is a purely mental manifestation. Today it has become an effective method in the learning process, taking several forms, most notably: critical thinking and creative thinking, which are among the methods relied upon in self-learning. In the field of research methodologies, there is emphasis on adhering to the method of scientific thinking, regardless of the extent of agreement or disagreement about the term 'scientific thinking' from one school to another; what matters to us here is to conduct the thinking process in a way that achieves reaching the desired goal, far from arbitrariness and the imposition of bare emotions.

The relationship between the function of the intellect and the thinking process is organic, for thinking is one of the powers of the intellect - as we indicated before - and those who do not reason (do not use intellect) do not benefit from their thinking. Therefore the Quran does not consider them worthy of the attribute of humanity and considers them among the cattle and what is lower: {And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. They are the heedless.} [Al-A'raf 7:179].
{Or do you think that most of them hear or reason? They are except like cattle; rather, they are more astray in the way.} [Al-Furqan 25:44].
And the cream of the saying in this regard is summarized by al-Harith al-Muhasibi in his statement: 'There is no sufficiency for the servant without reflection, contemplation, and remembrance, so that his consideration may increase, his knowledge may increase, and he may rise in virtue. For whoever's reflection is little, his consideration is little; and whoever's consideration is little, his knowledge is little; and whoever's knowledge is little, his ignorance is great, and his deficiency becomes apparent, and he does not find the taste of piety, nor the coolness of certainty, nor the spirit of wisdom. And what has he attained who studies knowledge with his tongue and memorizes its letters with his heart but turns away from reflection? That which he has acknowledged in his life is the life of beasts that know only what they directly experience through their senses! But the one who remembers, looks into what he hears, ponders what he knows, imagines what he is commanded, seeks the ultimate limits of knowledge, dives deep, sees what benefits him and what corrupts him, is strong against his innate inclinations that pull him toward destruction, opposes his desires that bring him low, is aware of the consequences of affairs and what occurs in the passing of ages and what has occurred from it, fears his Lord's command, prefers the pleasure of his intellect over the pleasure of his desire - the pleasure of the wise lies in their intellects, and the pleasure of the ignorant and beasts lies in their desires. What joy is there after the joy of knowledge, the spirit of certainty, great knowledge, abundance of correctness, and the victory that is not established nor attained except by good reflection, long remembrance, repeated thought, and prioritization in planning.'
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exploration of the two terms 'tafakkur' (contemplation) and 'tafkeer' (thinking), as well as their relationship to the intellect ('aql). The author begins by citing al-Raghib al-Isfahani's classical definition of tafakkur as the movement of the rational power according to the intellect, exclusive to humans, and involving the heart, thus including emotional aspects. Then he contrasts it with modern definitions of tafkeer by Humphrey and Bartlett, which focus on problem-solving and evidence expansion, emphasizing its purely mental nature. The author notes that today thinking takes forms like critical and creative thinking. Next, he discusses the organic link between thinking and intellect: since thinking is a faculty of the intellect, those devoid of 'aql do not benefit from thinking. He supports this with Quranic verses (Al-A'raf 7:179, Al-Furqan 25:44) comparing such people to cattle. Finally, he quotes al-Harith al-Muhasibi's extended exhortation on the necessity of reflection (tafakkur), remembrance (tadhakkur), and consideration (i'tibar) for increasing knowledge and virtue, contrasting the wise who use their intellect with the ignorant who follow desires. The passage thus integrates classical Islamic psychological concepts with modern cognitive terminology, all within a Quranic framework.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): The intellect; the faculty of reasoning and understanding that distinguishes humans from animals. Thinking is one of its powers. [Note: No significant shift—this term is stable across classical and modern Islamic thought.]
التفكر (al-tafakkur): Contemplation or reflective thought that involves movement of the rational power according to the intellect, exclusive to humans, and includes the heart, thus encompassing emotional aspects. [Note: In some classical texts, tafakkur and tafkeer are used interchangeably; here they are distinctly differentiated.]
التفكير (al-tafkeer): Thinking; a cognitive process that occurs in organisms when facing a problem, involving expansion of evidence and filling gaps, and can be either human or animal. [Note: Modern psychological definition imported; in classical Islamic texts, this term often overlaps with tafakkur.]
النظر (al-nazar): Reflection or consideration; a key component in al-Muhasibi's quote, involving thoughtful examination leading to knowledge. [Note: In logic, nazar sometimes refers to syllogistic reasoning; here it is more general.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about tafakkur?
A) It can occur in animals.
B) It involves the heart.
C) It is purely mental.
D) It is synonymous with tafkeer.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between tafakkur and tafkeer lies in tafakkur's exclusivity to humans and its heart involvement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the definition of tafakkur by al-Isfahani. In your own words, write two sentences explaining why tafakkur cannot be applied to animals.
?
The passage mentions critical thinking and creative thinking as forms of tafkeer. Give an example from Islamic education (e.g., ijtihad) where tafkeer is used but tafakkur might be more appropriate.

The Intellect and Its Vital Role in Thinking
Author discusses the relationship between intellect and thinking, citing Quranic verses and al-Muhasibi's wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Quran considers those who do not use their intellect as lower than cattle, and how al-Muhasibi connects reflection to knowledge and virtue.

Core Idea
Thinking without intellect is like a body without a soul; it reduces humans to the level of animals.

Having defined tafakkur and tafkeer, the author now explores the organic relationship between the intellect and the thinking process. He uses Quranic verses to show that those who possess faculties but do not use their intellect are worse than cattle. Then he quotes al-Muhasibi to illustrate the spiritual fruits of reflection and remembrance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
The author states that thinking is one of the powers of the intellect, and those who do not use their intellect do not benefit from thinking.
This is the premise linking intellect and meaningful thought.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Read verses 7:179 and 25:44. Note that they describe people with faculties (hearts, eyes, ears) who do not use them properly, equating them to cattle.
The Quran emphasizes that without active intellect, humans are lower than animals.
3
Examine al-Muhasibi's chain
Trace the causal sequence: reflection (tafakkur) leads to consideration (i'tibar), which increases knowledge ('ilm), which leads to virtue. Conversely, lack of reflection leads to ignorance and deficiency.
Al-Muhasibi's quote shows the practical consequences of using or neglecting the intellect.
4
Understand the contrast
Al-Muhasibi contrasts the wise who prefer the pleasure of the intellect over desire, with the ignorant who follow their desires like beasts.
This highlights the ethical dimension of using one's intellect for reflection.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل

لعل من المناسب كذلك التمييز بين التفكر والتفكير أما الأول فيعرفه الراغب الأصفهاني بأنه جولان تلك القوة بحسب نظر العقل، وذلك للإنسان دون الحيوان ولايقال إلا فيما يمكن أن يحصل له صورة في القلب. وكأنه بهذا المعنى يشمل جوانب وجدانية إلى جانب العقلية. (١)
أما التفكير فيعرفه (همفري): بأنه ما يحدث في خبرة الكائن العضوي، سواء كان إنساناً أم حيواناً، حين يواجه مشكلة، أو يتعرف عليها، أو يسعى لحلها (٢) ويعرفه (بارتلت): بأنه عملية توسيع الدليل على النحو الذي يلائمه، بحيث يتم ملء الفجوات فيه. ويتم هذا بالانتقال في خطوات متتابعة مترابطة يمكن التعبير عنها في حينها، أو يتم التعبير عنها فيما بعد) (٣). وحسب بارتلت فإن أول شرط لحدوث عملية التفكير هو نقصان المعلومات التي بين أيدينا، تأتي الصعوبة، أو تبرز المشكلة (٤) . وهذا - في الواقع - مظهر عقلي خالص. وقد غدا اليوم أسلوباً فاعلاً في عملية التعلم، ويتخذ صوراً عدة لعل أبرزها: التفكير الناقد، والتفكير الإبداعي، وهما من الأساليب المعوّل عليها في عملية التعلم الذاتي. وفي مجال مناهج البحث ثمة تشديد على التزام منهج التفكير العلمي وبصرف النظر عن مدى الاتفاق أو الاختلاف حول مصطلح (التفكير العلمي من مدرسة لأخرى فما يهمنا هنا هو إجراء عملية التفكير على نحو يحقق الوصول إلى الهدف المنشود بعيداً عن الاعتباط وتحكيم العواطف المجردة.

[Note: In some classical texts, tafakkur and tafkeer are used interchangeably; here they are distinctly differentiated.]

التذكر (al-tadhakkur): Remembrance or recollection; actively recalling past knowledge and experiences for reflection. [Note: No significant shift; used consistently in Islamic spiritual literature.]

According to al-Muhasibi, what happens when reflection (tafakkur) is little?
A) Consideration increases.
B) Knowledge increases.

Key Takeaway
The intellect is the foundation of meaningful thinking; without it, humans fall to the level of beasts, and reflection is the key to knowledge and virtue.

The Intellect and Thinking in the Quran
Author defines the intellect's role in thinking and lists characteristics of rational knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic basis for the necessity of using the intellect in acquiring knowledge and explain why the Quran considers those who do not reason as lower than cattle.

Core Idea
Without intellect, humans descend to the level of beasts.

In this passage, the author begins by establishing the organic relationship between the intellect and thinking. He quotes two Quranic verses that condemn those who possess sensory faculties but do not use their intellect, likening them to cattle. Then he cites al-Harith al-Muhasibi, who emphasizes that true knowledge and virtue come through reflection, remembrance, and consideration. This lesson focuses on the Quranic and spiritual imperative to engage the intellect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses cited
Find the two verses (7:179 and 25:44) in the source Arabic. Notice how they equate lack of reason with being like cattle.
2
Analyze al-Muhasibi's argument structure
He gives a conditional chain: little reflection leads to little consideration, leads to little knowledge, leads to ignorance.
3
Extract the distinction between sensory and rational knowledge
Based on the verse commentary, the senses alone are insufficient; the intellect must be used to truly understand and benefit.
4
Restate the core claim
The intellect is not optional; it is essential for being fully human in the Quranic worldview.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل والعلاقة بين وظيفة العقل وعملية التفكير عضوية إذ التفكير واحد من قوى العقل - كما أشرنا من قبل - والذين لا يعقلون لا ينفعهم تفكيرهم. لذلك لا يراهم القرآن جديرين بصفة الإنسانية واعتبرهم في عداد الدواب وما هو أدنى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيراً مِنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنْسِ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌ لا يَسْمَعُونَ بِها أُولَئِكَ كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْغَافِلُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۹/۷]. أَمْ تَحْسَبُ أَنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ يَسْمَعُونَ أَوْ يَعْقِلُونَ إِنْ هُمْ إِلا كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ سَبِيلاً [الفرقان: ٤٤/٢٥]. ونخبة القول في هذا الصدد يلخصه الحارث المحاسبي بقوله: (ولا غناء بالعبد عن النظر والتفكر والتذكر ليكثر اعتباره ويزيد في علمه، ويعلو في الفضل فمن قل تفكره قل اعتباره و من قل اعتباره قل علمه، ومـن قـل علـمـه كثر جهله، وبان نقصه، ولم يجد طعم البر، ولا برد اليقين، ولا روح الحكمة وماذا بلغ مَنْ درس العلم بلسانه، وحفظ الحروفه بقلبه، وأضرب عن النظر ما أقرّ به في حياته من حياة البهائم التي لا تعرف إلا ما باشرته بجوارحها ! لكن المتذكر الناظر فيما يسمع، المتدبّر لما علم المتوهم لما به أمر الطالب لنهاية حدود العلم الغائص والمبصر لما يصلحه وما يفسده القوي على عصيان طبائعه النازعة إلى ما يهلكه، والمخالف لشهواته التي ترديه العارف بعواقب الأمور، وبما يحدث في غابر الدهور، وما حدث منه. الهائب أمر ربه المؤثر لذة عقله على لذة هواه لذة) الحكماء في عقولهم ولذة الجهال والبهائم في شهواتهم. أي سرور بعد سرور العلم، وروح اليقين، وعظيم المعرفة، وكثرة الصواب، والظفر الذي لا يثبت ولا ينال إلا بحسن النظر، وطول التذكر، وتكرار الفكر والتقديم في التدبير))(۱).

خصائص العقل
في ضوء ما تقدم بوسعنا تلخيص خصائص المعرفة العقلية بما يلي:
(١ القدرة المبهرة على التنظيم والتصنيف، بعد جهل وعدم دراية، وذلك عن طريق تفاعله مع الحواس.
(۲) القدرة المبهرة على الاحتفاظ بصور الأشياء، بخلاف أي حاسة كالعين مثلا. فعلى الرغم من رؤيتها لشيء ما، وقدرتها على نقله إلى الذهن حسب قوانين الإبصار، إلا أنها عاجزة عن الاحتفاظ به على وجه التصريح، كما يفعل العقل حينما يختزن تلك الصور في حافظته العجيبة. فإن جئت لتبحث عن هذه الحافظة أو الخزان لا تجد شيئاً فأنى ذلك(۱).
وأما ميزة المعرفة العقلية على الحسية فتتمثل في التالي: (١ الضرورة أي رجوع المعرفة إلى معلومات أولية ضرورية بحكم العقل، وإن لم تكن مكتسبة له بطريق النظر.
(۲) صدق التعميم أو الكلية: أي إنه نظراً لصدق وثبات المعرفة وشمولها لأفراد موضوعها فإنه بالإمكان تعميم الحكم على أفراد النوع كله على نحو يقيني وجازم(٢).
صفة السببية (۳):
يتميز العقل بمقدرته على تعليل الظواهر وتفسيرها يارجاع كل سبب إلى (۱) صابر طعيمة، المعرفة في منهج القرآن، ١٦٥-١٧١. (۲) راجح الكردي، مرجع سابق، ٦٥١-٦٥٢.
(۳) السببية هي المبدأ الرابع من مبادئ العقل أو قوانينه الفطرية وهي مبدأ الهوية ويعني أن الموجود هو ذاته دائماً فلا يختلط به غيره ولا يلتبس به ماليس منه ومبدأ عدم التناقض ويعني أنه لا يمكن أن يكون الشيء في آن واحد موجوداً وغير موجود، ومبدأ الوسط المرفوع ويعني أن القضيتين لا واسطة بينهما، ويسمى أحياناً مبدأ الثالث مرفوع، ومبدأ القياس أو العلية أو السببية ويعني أنه إذا كانت (أ) تتضمن (ب) و (ب) تتضمن (ج) فإن (أ) تتضمن (ج) لا محالة. (مجمع اللغة العربية، المعجم الفلسفي، ١٦٥-١٦٦). وأشير إلى أن جانباً من مبدأ السببية تم تناوله عند الحديث عن طبيعة المعرفة في المظاهر السننية لميدان الأنفس، وحري أن يراجع ليكتمل تصور الموضوع.
Chapter Three: Section Two - The Intellect. The relationship between the function of the intellect and the process of thinking is organic, for thinking is one of the powers of the intellect - as we pointed out before - and those who do not reason, their thinking does not benefit them. Therefore the Quran does not consider them worthy of the quality of humanity and considers them among cattle and what is lower: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. It is they who are the heedless.' [Al-A'raf 7:179]. 'Or do you think that most of them hear or reason? They are not except like livestock; rather, they are more astray in way.' [Al-Furqan 25:44]. And the cream of the speech in this regard is summarized by al-Harith al-Muhasibi in his saying: 'The servant cannot do without reflection, contemplation, and remembrance, so that his consideration may increase, his knowledge may increase, and he may rise in virtue. For one whose reflection is little, his consideration is little; and one whose consideration is little, his knowledge is little; and one whose knowledge is little, his ignorance increases, his deficiency becomes apparent, and he does not find the taste of righteousness, nor the coolness of certainty, nor the spirit of wisdom. And what has one attained who studied knowledge with his tongue, memorized its letters with his heart, but turned away from reflection? He has admitted in his life to the life of beasts, which know only what they directly experience through their senses! But the one who remembers, who reflects on what he hears, who contemplates what he knows, who imagines what he is commanded, who seeks the ultimate limits of knowledge, who dives and perceives what benefits him and what corrupts him, who has strength to disobey his natures that incline toward what destroys him, who opposes his desires that bring him low, who knows the consequences of matters and what will happen in the passing ages and what has happened from them, who fears his Lord's command, who prefers the pleasure of his intellect over the pleasure of his desire - the pleasure of the wise is in their intellects, and the pleasure of the ignorant and beasts is in their desires. What joy is like the joy of knowledge, the spirit of certainty, the greatness of knowledge, the abundance of correctness, and the victory that is not established nor attained except through good reflection, long remembrance, repeated thinking, and advance planning.' (1).

Characteristics of the Intellect
In light of the above, we can summarize the characteristics of rational knowledge as follows:
(1) The extraordinary ability to organize and classify, after ignorance and lack of knowledge, through its interaction with the senses.
(2) The extraordinary ability to retain images of things, unlike any sense such as the eye, for example. Despite its seeing of something, and its ability to transmit it to the mind according to the laws of vision, it is incapable of retaining it explicitly, as the intellect does when it stores those images in its wonderful memory. If you come to look for this memory or storehouse, you find nothing - so how is that? (1).
As for the advantage of rational knowledge over sensory knowledge, it is represented in the following: (1) Necessity, i.e., knowledge refers to primary necessary information by virtue of the intellect, even if it was not acquired by it through the path of reflection.
(2) The truth of generalization or universality: i.e., because of the truth, stability, and comprehensiveness of knowledge to all individuals of its subject, it is possible to generalize the judgment to all individuals of the whole type in a certain and decisive manner (2).
Property of Causality (3):
The intellect is distinguished by its ability to explain phenomena and interpret them by tracing each cause to (1) Saber Ta'ima, Knowledge in the Methodology of the Quran, 165-171. (2) Rajih al-Kurdi, previous reference, 651-652.
(3) Causality is the fourth principle of the intellect or its innate laws: the principle of identity, meaning that the existent is always itself, so nothing else mixes with it nor does what is not from it become confused with it; the principle of non-contradiction, meaning that a thing cannot at the same time exist and not exist; the principle of the excluded middle, meaning that there is no middle ground between two propositions, sometimes called the principle of the excluded third; and the principle of syllogism or causality, meaning that if (A) implies (B) and (B) implies (C), then (A) necessarily implies (C). (Arabic Language Academy, Philosophical Dictionary, 165-166). It is noted that part of the principle of causality was addressed when discussing the nature of knowledge in the lawful manifestations in the domain of souls, and it should be reviewed to complete the concept of the subject.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion that first establishes the role of the intellect ('aql) as the faculty through which thinking operates. It emphasizes the Quranic view that those who do not use their intellect are not considered fully human but are likened to cattle. The author supports this with Quranic verses and a lengthy quote from al-Harith al-Muhasibi, which extols the virtues of reflection (tafakkur), remembrance (tadhakkur), and consideration (i'tibar) as keys to true knowledge and wisdom. The second part of the passage lists characteristics of rational knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-'aqliyya). First, it mentions the intellect's ability to organize and classify sensory input. Second, its ability to retain images, unlike the senses. Then it lists three distinctive features of rational knowledge over sensory knowledge: (1) necessity (al-darura) – rational knowledge is grounded in self-evident truths; (2) truth of generalization (al-ta'mim) – rational judgments apply universally with certainty; and (3) causality (al-sababiyya) – the intellect can explain phenomena by tracing causes, which is linked to the principles of identity, non-contradiction, excluded middle, and syllogism. The passage concludes with a note that some aspects of causality were previously discussed.

Key Terms
العقل
التفكر
الاعتبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Quran call people who do not use their intellect?
A) Hypocrites
B) Like cattle
C) Believers
D) Scholars

Key Takeaway
The intellect is the faculty that elevates humans above animals; using it is a Quranic imperative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find another Quranic verse that commands humans to use their intellect (e.g., 'Afala ta'qilun'). Write down the verse and explain in one sentence how it supports the author's argument.

intermediate
6 min
The Intellect's Abilities: Organization and Retention
Author defines the intellect's role in thinking and lists characteristics of rational knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the intellect's abilities of organization and retention compared to the senses.

Core Idea
The intellect organizes sensory chaos and retains images that the senses lose.

In this part of the passage, the author describes two remarkable abilities of the intellect: its power to organize and classify sensory input, and its ability to retain images of things long after the senses have stopped perceiving them. This lesson focuses on these two abilities and how they distinguish rational knowledge from sensory knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two abilities mentioned
The text lists two abilities: (1) organizing and classifying after ignorance, (2) retaining images of things, unlike the eye which cannot retain explicitly.
2
Compare with sensory abilities
The eye sees but cannot retain; the intellect retains and stores. Consider how the senses provide raw data but the intellect structures it.
3
Consider the interaction
The intellect interacts with the senses to organize and retain. It is not independent of sensory input but transforms it.
4
Formulate the distinction
Sensory knowledge is fleeting and unorganized; rational knowledge is structured and permanent.

Chapter Three: Section Two - The Intellect. The relationship between the function of the intellect and the process of thinking is organic, for thinking is one of the powers of the intellect - as we pointed out before - and those who do not reason, their thinking does not benefit them. Therefore the Quran does not consider them worthy of the quality of humanity and considers them among cattle and what is lower: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. It is they who are the heedless.' [Al-A'raf 7:179]. 'Or do you think that most of them hear or reason? They are not except like livestock; rather, they are more astray in way.' [Al-Furqan 25:44]. And what has one attained who studied knowledge with his tongue, memorized its letters with his heart, but turned away from reflection? He has admitted in his life to the life of beasts, which know only what they directly experience through their senses! What joy is like the joy of knowledge, the spirit of certainty, the greatness of knowledge, the abundance of correctness, and the victory that is not established nor attained except through good reflection, long remembrance, repeated thinking, and advance planning.' (1).

(1) The extraordinary ability to organize and classify, after ignorance and lack of knowledge, through its interaction with the senses.
(2) The extraordinary ability to retain images of things, unlike any sense such as the eye, for example. The intellect is distinguished by its ability to explain phenomena and interpret them by tracing each cause to (1) Saber Ta'ima, Knowledge in the Methodology of the Quran, 165-171. (2) Rajih al-Kurdi, previous reference, 651-652.
(3) Causality is the fourth principle of the intellect or its innate laws: the principle of identity, meaning that the existent is always itself, so nothing else mixes with it nor does what is not from it become confused with it; the principle of non-contradiction, meaning that a thing cannot at the same time exist and not exist; the principle of the excluded middle, meaning that there is no middle ground between two propositions, sometimes called the principle of the excluded third; and the principle of syllogism or causality, meaning that if (A) implies (B) and (B) implies (C), then (A) necessarily implies (C). Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion that first establishes the role of the intellect ('aql) as the faculty through which thinking operates. It emphasizes the Quranic view that those who do not use their intellect are not considered fully human but are likened to cattle. The author supports this with Quranic verses and a lengthy quote from al-Harith al-Muhasibi, which extols the virtues of reflection (tafakkur), remembrance (tadhakkur), and consideration (i'tibar) as keys to true knowledge and wisdom. The second part of the passage lists characteristics of rational knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-'aqliyya). First, it mentions the intellect's ability to organize and classify sensory input. Second, its ability to retain images, unlike the senses. Then it lists three distinctive features of rational knowledge over sensory knowledge: (1) necessity (al-darura) – rational knowledge is grounded in self-evident truths; (2) truth of generalization (al-ta'mim) – rational judgments apply universally with certainty; and (3) causality (al-sababiyya) – the intellect can explain phenomena by tracing causes, which is linked to the principles of identity, non-contradiction, excluded middle, and syllogism. The passage concludes with a note that some aspects of causality were previously discussed.

The Three Features of Rational Knowledge: Necessity, Universality, Causality
Author defines the intellect's role in thinking and lists characteristics of rational knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three distinguishing features of rational knowledge – necessity, universality, and causality – and provide an Islamic example for each.

Core Idea
Rational knowledge is necessary, universal, and causal – three marks of certainty that sensory knowledge lacks.

The author lists the advantages of rational knowledge over sensory knowledge: necessity, universality, and causality. These features make rational knowledge more certain and reliable. This lesson unpacks each feature and shows how they are applied in Islamic reasoning, particularly in the principle of causality which includes the four innate principles of the intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the three features listed
Find 'necessity' (al-darura), 'generalization/universality' (al-ta'mim/al-kulliyya), and 'causality' (al-sababiyya) in the text.
2
Understand necessity
It refers to self-evident truths that the intellect knows without reflection, like the whole being greater than a part.
3
Understand universality
A rational judgment like 'every action requires an agent' applies to all members of the class with certainty.
4
Understand causality
The intellect explains phenomena by tracing causes. The footnote expands it to four principles: identity, non-contradiction, excluded middle, and syllogism (if A implies B and B implies C, then A implies C).
Causality here is equated with the syllogistic principle.
5
Apply to Islamic sciences
In usul al-fiqh, qiyas relies on causality; the 'illah (cause) transfers the ruling from the original case to the new case, assuming necessity and universality.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل والعلاقة بين وظيفة العقل وعملية التفكير عضوية إذ التفكير واحد من قوى العقل - كما أشرنا من قبل - والذين لا يعقلون لا ينفعهم تفكيرهم. لذلك لا يراهم القرآن جديرين بصفة الإنسانية واعتبرهم في عداد الدواب وما هو أدنى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيراً مِنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنْسِ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌ لا يَسْمَعُونَ بِها أُولَئِكَ كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْغَافِلُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۹/۷]. أَمْ تَحْسَبُ أَنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ يَسْمَعُونَ أَوْ يَعْقِلُونَ إِنْ هُمْ إِلا كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ سَبِيلاً [الفرقان: ٤٤/٢٥]. ونخبة القول في هذا الصدد يلخصه الحارث المحاسبي بقوله: (ولا غناء بالعبد عن النظر والتفكر والتذكر ليكثر اعتباره ويزيد في علمه، ويعلو في الفضل فمن قل تفكره قل اعتباره و من قل اعتباره قل علمه، ومـن قـل علـمـه كثر جهله، وبان نقصه، ولم يجد طعم البر، ولا برد اليقين، ولا روح الحكمة وماذا بلغ مَنْ درس العلم بلسانه، وحفظ الحروفه بقلبه، وأضرب عن النظر ما أقرّ به في حياته من حياة البهائم التي لا تعرف إلا ما باشرته بجوارحها ! لكن المتذكر الناظر فيما يسمع، المتدبّر لما علم المتوهم لما به أمر الطالب لنهاية حدود العلم الغائص والمبصر لما يصلحه وما يفسده القوي على عصيان طبائعه النازعة إلى ما يهلكه، والمخالف لشهواته التي ترديه العارف بعواقب الأمور، وبما يحدث في غابر الدهور، وما حدث منه. الهائب أمر ربه المؤثر لذة عقله على لذة هواه لذة) الحكماء في عقولهم ولذة الجهال والبهائم في شهواتهم. أي سرور بعد سرور العلم، وروح اليقين، وعظيم المعرفة، وكثرة الصواب، والظفر الذي لا يثبت ولا ينال إلا بحسن النظر، وطول التذكر، وتكرار الفكر والتقديم في التدبير))(۱).

خصائص العقل
في ضوء ما تقدم بوسعنا تلخيص خصائص المعرفة العقلية بما يلي:
(١ القدرة المبهرة على التنظيم والتصنيف، بعد جهل وعدم دراية، وذلك عن طريق تفاعله مع الحواس.
(۲) القدرة المبهرة على الاحتفاظ بصور الأشياء، بخلاف أي حاسة كالعين مثلا. فعلى الرغم من رؤيتها لشيء ما، وقدرتها على نقله إلى الذهن حسب قوانين الإبصار، إلا أنها عاجزة عن الاحتفاظ به على وجه التصريح، كما يفعل العقل حينما يختزن تلك الصور في حافظته العجيبة. فإن جئت لتبحث عن هذه الحافظة أو الخزان لا تجد شيئاً فأنى ذلك(۱).
وأما ميزة المعرفة العقلية على الحسية فتتمثل في التالي: (١ الضرورة أي رجوع المعرفة إلى معلومات أولية ضرورية بحكم العقل، وإن لم تكن مكتسبة له بطريق النظر.
(۲) صدق التعميم أو الكلية: أي إنه نظراً لصدق وثبات المعرفة وشمولها لأفراد موضوعها فإنه بالإمكان تعميم الحكم على أفراد النوع كله على نحو يقيني وجازم(٢).
صفة السببية (۳):
يتميز العقل بمقدرته على تعليل الظواهر وتفسيرها يارجاع كل سبب إلى (۱) صابر طعيمة، المعرفة في منهج القرآن، ١٦٥-١٧١. (۲) راجح الكردي، مرجع سابق، ٦٥١-٦٥٢.
(۳) السببية هي المبدأ الرابع من مبادئ العقل أو قوانينه الفطرية وهي مبدأ الهوية ويعني أن الموجود هو ذاته دائماً فلا يختلط به غيره ولا يلتبس به ماليس منه ومبدأ عدم التناقض ويعني أنه لا يمكن أن يكون الشيء في آن واحد موجوداً وغير موجود، ومبدأ الوسط المرفوع ويعني أن القضيتين لا واسطة بينهما، ويسمى أحياناً مبدأ الثالث مرفوع، ومبدأ القياس أو العلية أو السببية ويعني أنه إذا كانت (أ) تتضمن (ب) و (ب) تتضمن (ج) فإن (أ) تتضمن (ج) لا محالة. (مجمع اللغة العربية، المعجم الفلسفي، ١٦٥-١٦٦). وأشير إلى أن جانباً من مبدأ السببية تم تناوله عند الحديث عن طبيعة المعرفة في المظاهر السننية لميدان الأنفس، وحري أن يراجع ليكتمل تصور الموضوع.
Chapter Three: Section Two - The Intellect. The relationship between the function of the intellect and the process of thinking is organic, for thinking is one of the powers of the intellect - as we pointed out before - and those who do not reason, their thinking does not benefit them. Therefore the Quran does not consider them worthy of the quality of humanity and considers them among cattle and what is lower: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. It is they who are the heedless.' [Al-A'raf 7:179]. 'Or do you think that most of them hear or reason? They are not except like livestock; rather, they are more astray in way.' [Al-Furqan 25:44]. And the cream of the speech in this regard is summarized by al-Harith al-Muhasibi in his saying: 'The servant cannot do without reflection, contemplation, and remembrance, so that his consideration may increase, his knowledge may increase, and he may rise in virtue. For one whose reflection is little, his consideration is little; and one whose consideration is little, his knowledge is little; and one whose knowledge is little, his ignorance increases, his deficiency becomes apparent, and he does not find the taste of righteousness, nor the coolness of certainty, nor the spirit of wisdom. And what has one attained who studied knowledge with his tongue, memorized its letters with his heart, but turned away from reflection? He has admitted in his life to the life of beasts, which know only what they directly experience through their senses! But the one who remembers, who reflects on what he hears, who contemplates what he knows, who imagines what he is commanded, who seeks the ultimate limits of knowledge, who dives and perceives what benefits him and what corrupts him, who has strength to disobey his natures that incline toward what destroys him, who opposes his desires that bring him low, who knows the consequences of matters and what will happen in the passing ages and what has happened from them, who fears his Lord's command, who prefers the pleasure of his intellect over the pleasure of his desire - the pleasure of the wise is in their intellects, and the pleasure of the ignorant and beasts is in their desires. What joy is like the joy of knowledge, the spirit of certainty, the greatness of knowledge, the abundance of correctness, and the victory that is not established nor attained except through good reflection, long remembrance, repeated thinking, and advance planning.' (1).

Characteristics of the Intellect
In light of the above, we can summarize the characteristics of rational knowledge as follows:
(1) The extraordinary ability to organize and classify, after ignorance and lack of knowledge, through its interaction with the senses.
(2) The extraordinary ability to retain images of things, unlike any sense such as the eye, for example. Despite its seeing of something, and its ability to transmit it to the mind according to the laws of vision, it is incapable of retaining it explicitly, as the intellect does when it stores those images in its wonderful memory. If you come to look for this memory or storehouse, you find nothing - so how is that? (1).
As for the advantage of rational knowledge over sensory knowledge, it is represented in the following: (1) Necessity, i.e., knowledge refers to primary necessary information by virtue of the intellect, even if it was not acquired by it through the path of reflection.
(2) The truth of generalization or universality: i.e., because of the truth, stability, and comprehensiveness of knowledge to all individuals of its subject, it is possible to generalize the judgment to all individuals of the whole type in a certain and decisive manner (2).
Property of Causality (3):
The intellect is distinguished by its ability to explain phenomena and interpret them by tracing each cause to (1) Saber Ta'ima, Knowledge in the Methodology of the Quran, 165-171. (2) Rajih al-Kurdi, previous reference, 651-652.
(3) Causality is the fourth principle of the intellect or its innate laws: the principle of identity, meaning that the existent is always itself, so nothing else mixes with it nor does what is not from it become confused with it; the principle of non-contradiction, meaning that a thing cannot at the same time exist and not exist; the principle of the excluded middle, meaning that there is no middle ground between two propositions, sometimes called the principle of the excluded third; and the principle of syllogism or causality, meaning that if (A) implies (B) and (B) implies (C), then (A) necessarily implies (C). (Arabic Language Academy, Philosophical Dictionary, 165-166). It is noted that part of the principle of causality was addressed when discussing the nature of knowledge in the lawful manifestations in the domain of souls, and it should be reviewed to complete the concept of the subject.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion that first establishes the role of the intellect ('aql) as the faculty through which thinking operates. It emphasizes the Quranic view that those who do not use their intellect are not considered fully human but are likened to cattle. The author supports this with Quranic verses and a lengthy quote from al-Harith al-Muhasibi, which extols the virtues of reflection (tafakkur), remembrance (tadhakkur), and consideration (i'tibar) as keys to true knowledge and wisdom. The second part of the passage lists characteristics of rational knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-'aqliyya). First, it mentions the intellect's ability to organize and classify sensory input. Second, its ability to retain images, unlike the senses. Then it lists three distinctive features of rational knowledge over sensory knowledge: (1) necessity (al-darura) – rational knowledge is grounded in self-evident truths; (2) truth of generalization (al-ta'mim) – rational judgments apply universally with certainty; and (3) causality (al-sababiyya) – the intellect can explain phenomena by tracing causes, which is linked to the principles of identity, non-contradiction, excluded middle, and syllogism. The passage concludes with a note that some aspects of causality were previously discussed.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
